    括异志　　宋 张师正

    　　●卷一
    　　○宋州狂僧
    　　太祖仕周日，尚未领宋州节钺，时有狂僧携弹走荆棘中，顾谓人曰：“此地当出天子。”又，显德末，一人青巾白衫，登中书政事堂，吏批其颊曰：“汝是何人敢至此！”其人曰：“宋州官家遣我去擒见宰相范质。”质曰：“此病心耳，安足问”遂叱去。其后太祖果自归德军节度使受禅，遂升宋州为应天府，后号南郡（一名南郡，事具国史）。

    Explanation

    1

    Record of Strange Events by Zhang Shizheng of the Song Dynasty

    Volume One

    The Mad Monk of Song Prefecture

    When Emperor Taizu of Song was serving under the Later Zhou dynasty, he had not yet been appointed as the governor of Song Prefecture. At that time, there was a mad monk who carried a bow and walked through thorny bushes, turning to say to someone, "This place will produce an emperor." Another incident occurred at the end of Emperor Shizong's reign when a man wearing a blue cap and white shirt entered the Hall of Political Affairs. A clerk slapped his cheek and asked, "Who are you to dare come here?" The man replied, "The official from Song Prefecture sent me to capture and present to Chancellor Fan Zhongyan." Chancellor Fan said, "It's just a mental illness; there's no need to ask." He then shouted at him to go away. Indeed, Emperor Taizu became the military governor of Guide Army and received the imperial throne. Then Song Prefecture was elevated to the status of Ying Tianfu, and later it was called Nan Jun (also known as Nan Jun, as recorded in the national history).

    2

    ○黑杀神降
    　　开宝中，有神降于凤翔府俚民张守真事，自称玄天大圣玉帝辅臣，其声婴儿，历可辨，远近之民祷祠者旁午。太祖召至京师，设醮于宫廷，降语曰：“天上宫阙成，玉锁开，十月二十日陛下当归天。”艺祖恳祈曰：“死固不惮，所恨者幽并未并，乞延三数年，俟克复二州，去亦未晚。”神曰：“晋王有仁心，历数攸属，陛下在天，亦自有位。”（时太宗王晋为开封尹）太祖命系于左军，将无验而罪焉，既而事符神告。太宗践祚，度守真为道士，仍赐紫袍，遂营庙于之太平镇，神位次序，殿庑规模，一由神授，仍尊黑杀，号为翊圣。至仁宗朝，追谥守真为传真大法师。事见《翊圣别传》。
    　　○来和天尊

    Explanation

    2

    Translation:

    Black Killing Spirit Descends

    During the reign of Emperor Taizu in the Kai Bao era, a spirit descended upon Zhang Shouzhen, a commoner from Fengxiang Prefecture, and identified itself as the Holy Great Saint of the Black Heaven, the Assistant Minister of the Jade Emperor. Its voice was that of an infant, yet clear and distinguishable. People from near and far were praying and offering sacrifices in large numbers. Emperor Taizu summoned it to the capital, where a ritual was set up in the imperial palace. The spirit spoke, saying: "The heavenly palaces have been completed, the jade lock has been opened, and on the twentieth day of the tenth month, Your Majesty will ascend to heaven." The emperor, in earnest supplication, said: "Death is not feared, but I regret that the regions of You and Wei have not yet been conquered. I request an extension of three or more years, until the two states are conquered, it is not too late to leave." The spirit replied: "Prince Jin has a compassionate heart and is destined for the throne. Your Majesty will have a place in heaven." (At the time, Emperor Taizong, Prince Jin, was the Prefect of Kaifeng.) Emperor Taizu ordered the spirit to be confined in the left military camp, planning to punish it if there was no verification. Soon after, the events corresponded to the spirit's prediction. Upon ascending the throne, Emperor Taizong appointed Zhang Shouzhen as a Taoist priest, granting him a purple robe, and built a temple in Taiping Town, . The arrangement of the deities and the structure of the temple were all determined by the spirit. The Black Killing Spirit was honored and given the title "Yi Sheng." During the reign of Emperor Renzong, posthumously bestows the title "Fa Zhen Da Fa Shi" (Great Master of Transmitting the True Teachings) on Zhang Shouzhen. The story is recorded in the "Yi Sheng Bie Zhuan" (Biography of Yi Sheng).

    Lai He Heavenly Venerable

    (No additional content provided in the source text.)

    3

    刑部尚书杨公砺为员外郎时，常梦人引导云：“谒来和天尊。”及见天尊，年甚少，穆之姿，若冰玉焉。杨公伏谒，天尊慰藉之甚厚。及觉，莫谕其事。后章圣皇帝育德储闱，尹正神州，杨公入幕，始谒而归，语诸子弟曰：“吾适谒皇太子，乃吾顷梦来和天尊之仪状也。”事在砺本传。
    　　○乐学士
    　　乐学士史，景德末为西都留台御史，尝梦一人具冠服，称帝命来召，共行十余里，俄见宫阙壮丽，殆非人世，因问使者，云：“此帝所也。”既陛见，帝谓曰：“而主求嗣，吾为择之，汝姑伺此。”少选，导一人至，气色和粹，似醺酣状。帝谓曰：“中原求嗣，汝往勿辞。”即顿首祈免者再三，帝曰：“往哉，惟汝宜。”遂唯而去。旁拱者谓史曰：“此南岳赤脚李仙人也，尝酣于酒。”帝急呼史至前，曰：“适见者，主之嗣也。”寤而识之，既而密以闻，具述所梦，曰：“宫中不久有甲观之庆。”明年神文诞圣。安退处士刘易尝记斯事。

    Explanation

    3

    During his tenure as an officer of the Imperial Censorate, Yang Gong Li, the Minister of Justice, often dreamed of someone guiding him and saying, "Visit Lai He Tianzun." Upon meeting the deity, he found him to be very young, with a serene and graceful demeanor, like ice and jade. Yang Gong Li knelt and paid respects, and the deity consoled him greatly. Upon waking, he could not understand the meaning of the dream. Later, when Emperor Zhenzong was raised to be the heir apparent and began to govern the empire, Yang Gong Li joined his inner circle. He then met the Crown Prince and, upon returning, told his disciples, "I just met the Crown Prince, and he is exactly like the deity I dreamed of in my recent dream." This event is recorded in Yang Gong Li's biography.

    Scholar Shi

    Scholar Shi, at the end of the Jingde era, served as a censor in the Western Capital. He once dreamed of a man dressed in official robes, who claimed that the emperor had summoned him. They walked together for more than ten miles and soon saw a magnificent palace, which seemed not of this world. Shi asked the messenger, "This is the emperor's residence, isn't it?" After ascending the palace steps and paying his respects, the emperor said to him, "Your master is seeking an heir, and I have chosen one for him. You should wait here." Shortly after, a man was led in, with a serene and slightly intoxicated appearance. The emperor said, "The Central Plains are seeking an heir, and you should not hesitate to go." Shi immediately knelt and begged for exemption several times, but the emperor said, "Go, for you are the most suitable." Shi then went away. A courtier beside him said to Shi, "This is the Taoist immortal Li of Mount Heng, who often indulges in wine." The emperor quickly called Shi to the front and said, "The person you just saw is the heir of your master." Upon waking, Shi recognized this. He then secretly reported the dream and described it in detail, saying, "There will soon be a grand celebration in the palace." The next year, Emperor Shenzong was born. The reclusive scholar Liu Yi once recorded this event.

    4

    ○司马待制
    　　故天章阁待制司马公池，乾兴中以职官知光山县，秩满，考绩于吏部。时章圣临脚，一夕，梦引对于便殿，仰视黼座，状甚幼冲，即觉，窃语交亲，以谓改官之期方远。铨司既质成课，将取旨，会真宗不豫，神文以皇太子监国，引见资善堂，仰视睿姿，一如所梦。
    　　○后苑亭
    　　嘉末，仁宗于后苑建一亭，题其榜曰迎曙亭。未几，神文弃天下，英宗嗣位，则亭之名岂徒然哉昔汉昭帝时，上林柳叶虫蠹成字，曰：公孙病已立。霍光既废昌邑，立戾太子之孙，是为宣帝，实名病己。唐宣宗晚年，长安小儿叠布蘸水向日捩之，谓之拔晕，懿宗果自郓王嗣立。以今方古，事实符契，古语有云：乾鹊噪而行人至，火花燃而得酒食。此言虽小，可以喻大，况王者之兴，岂无开先之兆也异哉！

    Explanation

    4

    Translation

    ○司马待制

    The former supervisor of the Tianzhang Pavilion, Sima Gongchi, served as the county magistrate of Guangshan County during the reign of Emperor Zhenzong. After completing his term, he had his performance evaluated by the Ministry of Personnel. One night, he dreamed of being summoned to a small hall for an audience with the emperor, who appeared very young and inexperienced. As soon as he woke up, he secretly told his close relatives that the time for promotion was still far off. The Ministry of Personnel had already evaluated his performance and was about to seek the emperor's approval, but just then, Emperor Zhenzong fell ill. Emperor Shenzong appointed the crown prince to act as regent and summoned Sima Gongchi to the Zisha Hall. When he looked up at the emperor, he saw the same wise and capable appearance as in his dream.

    ○后苑亭

    In the late Jia You period, Emperor Renzong built a pavilion in the imperial garden and named it the Dawn Pavilion. Soon after, Emperor Shenzong passed away, and Emperor Yingzong succeeded to the throne. The name of the pavilion, Dawn Pavilion, was not merely coincidental. In the time of Emperor Zhao of Han, a message appeared on the leaves of willow trees in the imperial gardens, saying: "Gong Sun Bing has been established." After Huo Guang deposed the ruler of Changyi, he enthroned the grandson of the Marquis of Li, who became Emperor Xuan, whose real name was Bing. In the later years of Emperor Xuanzong of Tang, children in Chang'an would fold cloth, dip it in water, and hold it up to the sun to create a rainbow effect, which they called "pulling a halo." Emperor Yizong indeed succeeded to the throne from the Prince of Yun. Comparing the present with the past, the facts align perfectly. As the old saying goes: "When a magpie caws, a traveler arrives; when a spark ignites, one finds food and drink." These sayings, though small, can be used to illustrate great truths. How much more so, then, for the rise of a king, which surely has omens beforehand! How extraordinary!

    5

    ○衡山僧
    　　嘉八年三月，衡山县僧某来湘潭，干事既毕，归衡山，至中途宿逆旅，忽梦行道中，车骑戈甲，旌麾仪卫，去地丈余，蹑空北去，僧伏道左。少时既过，复前，又逢数骑，叱之曰：“安得犯跸”僧自疏得免，因问：“何官也”曰：“新天子即位，南岳神往受职耳。”僧既觉。明日至衡山，白所梦于邑令，令戒僧曰：“秘之，勿妄言。”后数日，闻仁宗遗诏，至考其所梦之夕，正月二十九日也。《金匮》云：武王胜殷纣，大雪平地盈尺，旦日，有车马诣军门，行无辙迹，太公曰：“此四海之神洎河北来受职也。”因祀之，约束而去。与此正类。

    Explanation

    5

    A Monk from Mount Heng

    In the third month of the eighth year of the Jia You era, a certain monk from Hengshan County came to Xiangtan to complete his affairs. After finishing his tasks, he returned to Mount Heng and stayed at an inn on the way. Suddenly, he dreamed of walking in a road, where he saw carriages, horses, spears, and armor, flags and banners, and ceremonial guards rising a few feet above the ground, moving northward through the air. The monk bowed on the left side of the road. After a short time, the procession had passed, and he moved forward. He then encountered several riders who rebuked him, saying, "How dare you trespass on the imperial procession?" The monk explained himself and was allowed to pass. He asked, "What kind of officials are you?" They replied, "The new emperor has ascended the throne, and the god of Mount Heng is going to receive his official position." The monk woke up the next day. Upon reaching Mount Heng, he reported his dream to the county magistrate, who warned him, "Keep it secret, do not speak of it lightly." A few days later, he heard of Emperor Renzong's will and realized that the night of his dream corresponded to the twenty-ninth day of the first month. The Jin Gui records: When King Wu defeated King Zhou of Shang, heavy snow covered the ground to a depth of a foot. The next day, there were carriages and horses at the military gate, leaving no tracks. Duke Tai Gong said, "These are the gods of the four seas and the north coming to receive their positions." Therefore, they were worshipped and then departed with strict orders. This is exactly similar to the monk's dream.

    6

    ○南岳真人
    　　庞相国籍既致政，居于京师，嘉八年春三月，公被疾，至下旬，病革，一旦奄然，家人聚哭，数刻复生。翌日，命纸笔，屏左右，手书密封，俾其子奏，家人咸谓久病恍惚，书字不谨，遂寝不以闻。公既薨，发视之，云：初死，有人引导令朝玉皇，入一大殿庭排班，庞处下列，拜讫，有一人传玉皇诏，云：“庞某令且归。伺与南岳真人偕来。”既出殿门，又有人前导，云：“当见南岳真人。”复至一殿庭列班，庞居上游，卷帘毕，既拜，熟视乃仁宗皇帝也。时神文久不豫，庞既复苏，觉体候小康，又闻圣躬亦复常膳，乃窃喜，故欲上闻。三月二十七日庞薨，越一日，仁庙上仙。

    Explanation

    6

    The South Mountain True Person

    When Pang Xiangguo, a former official, retired and settled in the capital, he fell ill in the spring of the eighth year of the Jia You era (1063). By the end of the month, his condition had worsened, and one day he suddenly passed away. His family gathered to mourn, but after a few moments, he revived. The next day, he called for paper and ink, dismissed his attendants, and wrote a sealed message, instructing his son to present it. The family, believing him to be delirious from his long illness, thought his handwriting was careless and ignored the message. After Pang's death, they opened the sealed letter, which read: "Upon my death, someone guided me to pay homage to the Jade Emperor. I entered a grand hall where I stood in a line, with Pang below. After bowing, a person delivered a decree from the Jade Emperor, saying: 'Pang, you are to return. Wait and come with the South Mountain True Person.' After exiting the hall, another person led me, saying: 'You will meet the South Mountain True Person.' I returned to another hall, stood in line, and found myself in a higher position. The curtains were drawn, and I bowed again, looking closely to see that it was Emperor Renzong. At that time, the emperor had been ill for a long time. After Pang's revival, he felt a slight improvement in his health and heard that the emperor was also resuming normal meals. He secretly rejoiced and wanted to inform the emperor. On the twenty-seventh day of March, Pang died, and the following day, Emperor Renzong passed away."

    7

    ○会圣宫
    　　会圣宫在洛都东八十里望仙桥，祖宗之神御在焉。嘉八年三月二十九日昼漏尽，宫侧之人见王者羽卫，陈布道中，最后二人衣赭袍，张黄盖，乘马相次至宫前，乃不见。明日，宫门大敞，诸殿门锁不钥而启，主事者大骇，少时，闻仁庙上仙。
    　　○曹门谣
    　　天圣末洎明道中，京师市井坊巷之人，凡物之美嘉者，即曰曹门好，物之高大者，即曰曹门高，耆壮童稚无不道者。景初，神文诏册曹王女孙为皇后，曹王为国功臣之冠，虽圭爵蝉联者三世，洎作配宸极，居外戚之尊，可谓高且好矣。王辅艺祖定天下，降蜀平吴，抗丑虏，破强敌，将百万之众，未尝妄杀一人，宜乎后裔之兴也。唐郭尚父功盖天下，位极人臣，侈穷人欲，寿登耆艾。天谓报施之道，由或歉然，至暧女为宪宗元妃，历七朝，王居母后之尊，人君行子孙之礼。唐史臣谓子仪社稷之功未泯，复钟庆于懿安焉。以曹氏之余烈，近之矣。

    Explanation

    7

    Translation

    会圣宫

    The Temple of the Converging Saints is located eighty miles east of Luoyang, at the Bridge of the Immortal View, where the spirits of the ancestors are enshrined. On the twenty-ninth day of the third month in the eighth year of the Jia You era, at the end of the day, people near the temple saw the ceremonial guard of a king, arranged along the road, with the last two figures wearing red robes and holding yellow canopies, riding horses in succession to the front of the temple, after which they disappeared. The next day, the temple gates were wide open, and the locks on the doors of all the halls were not fastened but opened, causing great alarm among the officials. Shortly after, news came that Emperor Ren's temple had ascended to the heavens.

    曹门谣

    In the late Tiansheng period and early Mingdao era, the common people of the capital city would say that anything of fine quality came from Caowei, and anything tall or grand also came from Caowei, with this saying being known by both the elderly and the young. In the early Jing You era, Emperor Ren issued an edict to make the granddaughter of the Prince of Cao the empress. The Prince of Cao was the foremost among national heroes, and his descendants held high ranks for three generations, eventually being matched to the imperial throne and holding the esteemed position of an imperial relative by marriage. It can be said that the Wang family was both high and good. The ancestors of the Wang family assisted in establishing the Song dynasty, conquering Shu and Wu, resisting barbarian enemies, defeating powerful foes, leading a million troops, and never unjustly killing anyone, which is why their descendants prospered. Guo Ziyi, a general of the Tang dynasty, achieved great feats, reached the highest rank among ministers, indulged in every desire, and lived to an old age. Heaven's way of retribution, however, sometimes seems lacking, as his daughter became the empress dowager of Emperor Xianzong, serving through seven reigns, with the Wang family holding the esteemed position of empress dowager and the emperor performing the rites of a son. The Tang historian said that Guo Ziyi's merit in founding the state had not diminished, and blessings were bestowed upon Empress E'anan. The legacy of the Wang family is close to that of Guo Ziyi.

    8

    ○陈靖
    　　陈靖，字唐臣，钜野人，少倜傥有气节，通《诗》《易》，尝从范讽、石延年、刘潜游。景五年，以进士特奏名得三礼出身，荐为邑佐，皆有能声。稍迁孝感令，以公事忤郡太守，辄致所事而去，即日僦舟东下，隐于叶山。未几诏下，以太子中舍致仕，值岁荒，徙家京师，卖药自给。朝之公卿多故人，踵门者辄避去，或遗金帛，即散道士丐者，未尝有所蓄。与其妻孔氏皆学辟谷，往往经岁不食。嘉四年，思武陵山水之嘉，尽室出彼，王介甫高其行，以诗送，有“知君欲上武陵溪，水自东流人自西”之句。既至武陵，结庐于高梧市，居数月，丧其妻，自是不接人事，杜门称疾，惟焚香诵《易》而已。

    Explanation

    8

    Tian Jing, courtesy name Tangchen, was from Juye. In his youth, he was bold and unrestrained, with a strong sense of integrity, and proficient in the Shijing (Book of Poetry) and Yijing (Book of Changes). He once studied under Fan Feng, Shi Yanian, and Liu Qian. In the fifth year of the Jingyou era (1038 AD), he obtained a degree in the Three Rituals through a special imperial examination and was recommended for a local administrative position, where he gained a reputation for his ability. He was later promoted to the position of magistrate in Xiaogan, but offended the prefect with official matters and immediately resigned, hiring a boat to travel eastward and retreat to Yeshan. Soon after, an imperial edict came down, and he retired from official service as a scholar in the Imperial Academy. During a year of famine, he moved his family to the capital and supported himself by selling medicine. Many of the officials and scholars he knew visited him, but he avoided them, and if they left behind money and silk, he immediately distributed it to Taoist priests and beggars, never accumulating anything. Both he and his wife, Kong, learned the practice of abstaining from food and sometimes went for a whole year without eating. In the fourth year of the Jiahe era (1059 AD), thinking the landscape of Wuling was beautiful, he moved his entire family there. Wang Anshi admired his conduct and sent him a poem, which included the lines, "I know you wish to ascend the Wuling Creek, where the water flows eastward while people go westward." After arriving in Wuling, he built a hut in Gao Wu Market. After living there for a few months, he lost his wife and no longer interacted with people, closing the door and pretending to be ill, only burning incense and reciting the Yijing.

    9

    六年七月十七日亭午，遽命其子庠具纸札，作书遗张郎中曰：“近上帝以靖平生无谄，俾主判地下平直司，候天符下，即之任矣。”张时职江东漕运，得书以靖为病心者，不复报。是日又躬为一书，封缄甚密，戒其子曰：“张公归乡，以此书授之，不可示他人及私发，违吾言，汝为不孝。”其子谨藏之。自是多为歌诗，皆有脱去世俗之意。七年十一月十二日平旦，谓其子曰：“吾数尽矣，后事一托张秘丞主之。”言讫而终。时张秘丞将赴官益阳，前一日与靖别，翌日得其讣，亟为办丧事，葬于耆山之侧。治平元年七月，张仲孚自江东还，其子庠捧父书，号泣来献，封缄如初。发之，其始末皆叙诀之辞，中乃云：“平直司必然失为议定皇嗣事，勿怪草草。”明年秋，英宗由大宗正为皇子，而靖于六年七月为此书，己有选定之语，由是知帝王之兴皆受命于天，默有符契，非偶然矣。此皆略取张仲举学士所撰《陈靖传》云。

    Explanation

    9

    On the seventeenth day of the seventh month in the sixth year, at noon, Chen Jing hastily ordered his son Xiang to prepare paper and writing materials, and to write a letter to Zhang Langzhong Zhi, saying, "Recently, the Heavenly Emperor, because of my lifelong integrity and lack of flattery, has appointed me to judge the Underworld Justice Department, awaiting the heavenly decree to assume the position." At the time, Zhang was in charge of canal transportation in Jiangdong. Upon receiving the letter, he thought that Chen Jing was suffering from a mental illness and did not respond. On the same day, Chen Jing personally wrote another letter, sealing it very tightly, and warned his son, "When Zhang returns to his hometown, give this letter to him, do not show it to others or open it privately. If you disobey my words, you will be ungrateful." His son kept the letter carefully. From then on, Chen Jing often wrote poems, all expressing a desire to transcend the mundane world. On the twelfth day of the eleventh month in the seventh year, early in the morning, he told his son, "My time is up. Entrust all after-death affairs to Zhang, the Secretariat Commissioner." After finishing speaking, he died. At that time, Zhang, the Secretariat Commissioner, was about to take office in Yiyang. The day before, he had bid farewell to Chen Jing. The next day, he received the news of his death and hurriedly arranged the funeral, burying him on the side of Qiji Mountain. In the first month of the seventh month of the Zhiping era, Zhang Zhongfu returned from Jiangdong. His son Xiang held his father's letter, crying, and presented it. The letter was sealed as before. When opened, the beginning and end contained parting words, and in the middle it said, "The Underworld Justice Department must have made a mistake in deciding the heir. Do not blame me for the hasty writing." The following autumn, Emperor Yingzong, from the position of Grand Chief Justice, became the crown prince. Chen Jing wrote this letter in the seventh month of the sixth year, already having chosen words. Thus we know that the rise of emperors is ordained by heaven, with a secret correspondence, not by chance. All this is taken from the biography of Chen Jing written by Zhang Zhongju.

    10

    ○醴泉观
    　　祥符中，京师东南隅醴泉涌，龟蛇见其侧，饮之者疾瘳。即其地营祥源观，其后灾，再加缮构，改号醴泉观。熙宁八年，又易倾朽，荐加垩饰。功毕落成，命教坊伶人奏乐于庭，是日真武影现于殿脊火珠中，其部从神官纛之类，望之悉具，京师奔走观瞩者数千万人。
    　　○贾魏公
    　　贾魏公昌朝先德名注，尝为棣州推官，公方在孕。一夕，梦绯衣冠者一人自空而下，以巨箱捧貂蝉冠以献，俄而公生。始数岁，先令公为瀛幕，公时在膝下，契丹数十万攻围逾月，城甚危，守陴者闻空中神告曰：“城有中朝辅相，勿忧贼也。”数日，虏遁去，城卒无患。公自宰相出镇、拥节钺者垂二十年，官至兼侍中。若然，则贵贱之分，淹速之数，固由默定，世之汲汲于进者无所不至，岂昧于居易之理乎

    Explanation

    10

    During the Xiangfu era, a spring of sweet water suddenly surged forth in the southeastern corner of the capital city, accompanied by the appearance of turtles and snakes nearby. Those who drank from it were cured of their illnesses. At that site, the Xiangyuan Temple was built, but it was later destroyed by a disaster and had to be reconstructed. It was then renamed the Liquan Temple. In the eighth year of the Xining era, the temple was rebuilt after falling into disrepair, with additional whitewashing added. Upon its completion, musicians from the Imperial Music Bureau were ordered to play music in the courtyard. On that day, the image of Zhenwu appeared in the fire pearl on the roof ridge, along with its accompanying deities, officials, and banners, all clearly visible. Millions of people in the capital rushed to see it.

    The late Mr. Zhu, the ancestor of Duke Jia, once served as a judge in Dizhou, while Duke Jia was still in his mother's womb. One night, a person dressed in red appeared from the sky, presenting a large box containing a crown, and Duke Jia was subsequently born. When he was just a few years old, his father was placed under the care of a high-ranking official, and Duke Jia was with him. At that time, the Khitans attacked with tens of thousands of troops, besieging the city for over a month, and the city was in great danger. Those guarding the walls heard a voice from the sky say, "The city has a chancellor from the central government; do not worry about the enemy." A few days later, the enemy fled away, and the city was finally safe. Duke Jia, who had served as a chancellor, spent nearly twenty years in various military and civil posts, eventually rising to the position of Vice Premier. If such is the case, then the distinction between high and low status, the speed of progress, is determined secretly. Those who are eager to advance will go to any lengths, but are they not ignorant of the principle of ease?

    11

    ○大名监埽
    　　河自大坯而下，多泛溢之患，岸有缺圮，则以薪ド窒塞，补薄增卑，谓之埽岸，每一二十里则命使臣巡视。凡一埽岸，必有薪茭竹捷椿木之类，数十百万，以备决溢。使臣始受命，皆军令约束。熙宁九年，大名府元城县一监埽使臣所主埽岸，有大鼋屡来，啮岸之薪ド，似将穴焉，遂彀弩射之，中首而死。是夜，梦一绿衣创首谓监埽曰：“汝杀我，我已诉于官矣。”又月余，病疽死。见二使者执之而去，曰：“汝尝杀人。”监埽窃思之曰：“此必杀鼋事也。”行仅百里，入一城，使者曰：“吾有事，当先白所由司，汝姑止此，无他适。

    Explanation

    11

    Daming Supervisory Official

    The river from Daming often experiences flooding, causing many hazards. When the riverbank has gaps or collapses, it is plugged with wood, and weak areas are reinforced and raised. This is known as "suo" (堵塞, plugging). Every twenty to thirty miles, officials are sent to inspect the riverbank. For each section of the riverbank, there must be a large amount of wood, bamboo, and other materials, totaling tens of millions, to prepare for any overflow.

    When the official first received his command, he was subject to military discipline and regulations. In the ninth year of Xining, the supervisory official of Daming Fu's Yuancheng County was responsible for a section of the riverbank. A large turtle frequently appeared, biting at the wood used to block the riverbank, as if trying to dig a hole. The official then drew a crossbow and shot the turtle, hitting it in the head and killing it. That night, he dreamed of a green-clad figure with a head wound who said to the supervisory official, "You killed me, and I have complained to the authorities." About a month later, the official developed a boil and died. He saw two officials take him away and said, "You once killed a turtle." The supervisory official thought to himself, "This must be because of the turtle incident." After traveling about one hundred miles, he entered a city, and the officials said, "We have something to report, so we will go first. You can stay here for now, do not go anywhere else."

    12

    ”二使既去，仰视高阁金碧相照，有二神人守阍，如道士观所谓龙虎君者。以姓名白之，乃引入，仰视其阁，有榜题曰：朝元之阁，下见韩侍中稚圭凭几而坐，侍者数十人，若神仙仪卫。乃再拜讫，韩问来状，遂白杀鼋事，因曰：“堤岸有决，当受军令之责，非徒杀也。”韩曰：“汝亦何罪倘见阴官，但乞检上清格。”即出门，见二使者至，遂引到一官府庭下，果诘以杀鼋事，对曰：“某主埽岸，河流奔猛，涨溢不常，苟有决漏，则当诛。鼋败吾防，不可不杀，乞检上清格。”阴官取络，视讫谓曰：“上清格云：无益于世，有害于人，杀而不偿，罪固难加。”阴官命前使者引出，行十余里，若堕眢井，遂寤。

    Explanation

    12

    After the two messengers had departed, I looked up at the high pavilion where gold and green jade shone together, and there were two divine beings guarding the gate, like the dragon and tiger lords mentioned in the Taoist temple. I told them my name, and they then led me in. Looking up at the pavilion, I saw a plaque that read: "The Pavilion of Aspiring to the Supreme." Below, I saw Han Zhigu, the Attendant in Waiting, sitting on a table, with dozens of attendants, like the retinue of a divine being. I then bowed twice again, and Han asked about my coming. I then reported the matter of killing the turtle, and he said, "If the dike breaks, I will be held responsible by military law, not just for killing." Han said, "What crime have you committed? If you see the officials of the underworld, just ask them to check the Upper Clear Register." I immediately went out and saw the two messengers arrive. They then led me to the courtyard of an official building, where they indeed questioned me about the matter of killing the turtle. I replied, "I am in charge of sweeping the bank. The river is swift and surging, overflowing irregularly. If there is a breach, I will be executed. The turtle damaged our defenses, so it could not be spared. I ask them to check the Upper Clear Register." The official of the underworld took a register, looked it over, and then said, "The Upper Clear Register states: 'If it is of no benefit to the world and harmful to people, killing it without compensation is difficult to punish.'" The official of the underworld ordered the previous messengers to lead me out. After walking for over ten miles, it was as if I fell into a dry well, and I woke up.

    13

    ○仆射厅
    　　陈英公执中，初以左正言谪为中允，监永州酒税，郡守常以谏官待之。间日，具肴膳就其所治以延款之。英公即座，周视居宇，忽于榱桷楣间注目久之，顾侍吏曰：“见一牌否”左右对以无睹，郡守而下皆曰：“未尝有牌。”陈笑而杂以他语。及归家，人怪而询之，公曰：“宛见一金字牌，书仆射厅字。”公由是益自负，既而两正台府，竟践此位。虽以司徒致政，然在仕之时，官为端揆。
    　　○吕枢密
    　　吕枢密公弼，丞相申公之次子，始秦国妊娠而疾，将去之，命医工陈逊煮药。时方初夜，逮药将熟已二鼓，坐而假寐，忽然鼎覆；取诸药品差М末再煮之，俄以严鼓，不觉再覆；既而又煮，而加火焉。困甚就榻，梦一神人，披黄金甲持剑叱陈曰：“在胞者本朝宰相也，汝何等人，敢以毒药加害”陈恐忄栗而寤，遂以所梦洎覆鼎事白于秦国，曰：“在孕者贵人也，虽疾，当无所损。”其后生宝臣。熙宁中，自枢密使出镇而薨。

    13

    ○Pushe Hall
    Chen Yinggong Zhi Zhong, originally demoted from the position of Left Remonstrator to Middle Allow, was sent to supervise the wine tax in Yongzhou. The prefecture governor often treated him as a censor. One day, he prepared food and wine and went to his office to entertain him. As Chen Yinggong took his seat, he inspected the residence thoroughly, and suddenly, he looked at the beams and rafters for a long time. He turned to the attendant and asked, "Have you seen a sign?" The attendants replied that they did not see anything, and the prefecture governor and those below him said, "There has never been a sign." Chen Yinggong smiled and talked about other things. When he returned home, people were curious and asked him about it. He said, "I distinctly saw a golden plaque inscribed with the words 'Pushe Hall.'" From then on, he became even more confident. Later, he held the two main government offices and finally attained this position. Although he retired as a Grand Tutor, during his career, he held the highest position in the government.

    ○Lu Shumai
    Lu Shumai Gong Bi, the second son of Chancellor Shen Gong, was born to Qin Guo, who was pregnant and ill. She was about to miscarry, so she ordered the physician Chen Xun to prepare medicine. It was just the beginning of the night, and by the time the medicine was almost ready, it was already the second drumbeat. Chen Xun sat and took a nap, but suddenly the tripod overturned. He took some of the medicine, mixed it again, and cooked it. Soon after, the drum was beaten loudly, and he did not notice it overturn again. He cooked it again and added more fire. He was very tired and went to bed, where he dreamed of a divine person wearing golden armor and holding a sword. The divine person scolded Chen Xun and said, "The one in the womb will be a prime minister of this dynasty. Who are you to dare to harm him with poison?" Chen Xun was frightened and woke up. He then told Qin Guo about his dream and the overturned tripod, saying, "The one in the womb is a noble person, even if she is ill, it should not cause harm." Later, she gave birth to Baocen. During the Xining era, he died after being transferred from the position of Chief Military Commissioner.

    14

    ●卷二
    　　○盛枢密
    　　枢密使文肃盛公度修起居注日，尝感疾而死，支体犹温，故家人未敢殓，越宿乃苏，云：始为人追摄，若行田野间，气候昏塞如欲雨状。良久，入一府，见主者被古诸侯服，起而接公，且谂以同姓名而误追，亟命公还。既而复行田间，远望有数人皆若旧识，及追视之，乃故相国沈公义伦也，喜揖盛曰：“审知学士得还，为我语家人，颇为汗脚袜所苦。”草草别去。盛神还，疾亦渐愈，遂以冥中所嘱语沈孤，其孤泣，而不悟汗脚袜之说，及服除彻相公灵榻，而神座之横桄有败袜焉。究其所自，则守灵老卒之物，偶致于此，旦起忘之，谓已亡失，故不复索。

    Explanation

    14

    Book Two
    ○ Sheng Shumimi

    The Shumimi, Wen Su Sheng Gong Du, who was responsible for recording the emperor's daily activities, once felt ill and died. His limbs were still warm, so his family did not dare to prepare the body for burial. The next day, he woke up and said: "At first, I was summoned by someone, as if walking through the fields. The atmosphere was dim and stuffy, like it was about to rain. After a long while, I entered a hall and saw the official dressed in ancient feudal attire. He stood up to greet me and explained that I was mistakenly summoned due to having the same name. He quickly ordered me to return. Later, I walked through the fields again and saw several people who seemed familiar. When I approached them, I realized they were the former chancellor, Mr. Shen Yilun. He greeted me warmly and said, 'If you know the scholar has returned, tell my family that I am quite troubled by sweaty socks.' He left hastily. After returning to the living world, my illness gradually improved. I then fulfilled the request made to Shen's orphan in the afterlife. The orphan cried but did not understand the reference to sweaty socks. After the mourning period ended and the chancellor's spirit tablet was removed, there was a worn-out sock on the horizontal bar of the spirit tablet. Upon investigation, it turned out to be an item belonging to the old soldier guarding the spirit tablet. It had happened to be placed there, and the soldier had forgotten about it when getting up in the morning, thinking it had been lost, so he did not look for it again.

    15

    ○余尚书
    　　余尚书靖，韶州曲江人，天圣元年第进士，又中拔萃，始自曲江将求荐于天府，与一同郡进士刘某偕行，刘已四预计偕。行至洲头驿，有祠颇灵，余谓刘曰：“与足下万里图身计，盍乞灵焉”遂率刘以楮镪香酒祷祠下，乞梦中示以休咎。是夕，余梦神告，召而谓曰：“公禄甚厚，贮于数廪，官至尚书，死于秦亭。刘某穷薄，止有禄六斗耳。”公谢而退，遂寤。其后出入清华，声望赫然，中罹废黜者累岁，其后竟至工部尚书。常语交亲曰：“关中任使决不敢去。”既罢广州，至乌江得疾，遂入金陵就医，舣舟秦淮，扶病登亭，视其榜，曰秦淮亭，公不怿，数日而薨。刘某者以累举不第，就南迁，遂摄一尉，才逾旬而卒。

    Explanation

    15

    Yu Jing, the Shangshu, was from Qiaojiang, Shaoguan. In the first year of the Tian Sheng era, he passed the jinshi examination and also excelled in the higher-level examinations. He set out from Qiaojiang to seek recommendations in the capital, accompanied by a fellow jinshi from the same prefecture named Liu. Liu had already planned to travel with him four times. They reached Zhou Tou Posthouse, where there was a shrine known for its spiritual power. Yu said to Liu, "Since we are planning our careers over long distances, why not seek divine assistance?" So, Yu led Liu to offer a bundle of paper money and wine at the shrine, praying for a dream that would reveal good or bad omens. That night, Yu dreamed that a spirit summoned him and said, "Your salary will be very generous, stored in several granaries. You will rise to the position of Shangshu and die at Qinting Pavilion. Liu is poor and has only a salary of six dou. Liu thanked the spirit and woke up. Later, Yu entered the imperial service, gained a reputation, and was demoted for several years before eventually becoming Minister of Works. He often told his friends, "I will not accept any position in Guanzhong." After being dismissed from his post in Guangzhou, he fell ill at Wujiang and went to Nanjing for medical treatment. He docked his boat on the Qinhuai River, climbed a pavilion while ill, and saw the sign, which read "Qinting Pavilion." Yu was displeased and died a few days later. Liu, who had failed the imperial examinations multiple times, was exiled to the south and temporarily served as a magistrate. He died after only ten days.

    16

    ○郎侍郎
    　　郎侍郎简致政之年，将赴阙，更图一郡，然后悬车，管次奔牛，宿于堰下。时盛暑，月色澄亮，命从者皆寝，辟船门默坐，乙夜闻岸侧有人语云：“吾儿明日过此，幸若曹悉力曳船，渠齿幼，恐致惊怖。”郎大讶，登岸四顾，人皆酣寝，惟群牛卧＜齿台＞于屋下。翌日，郎驻舟以伺，俄有称监簿者，年甫弱冠，由途于此，船既及堰，群牛不待呵捶，旋转如风，顷刻而过堰。郎太息曰：“吾平生历官治民，自谓无冤抑，安能垂老更黾勉于王事乎”即抗章告老，南归余杭。牛之子不传名氏者，郎为之讳也。

    Explanation

    16

    The Deputy Minister

    The Deputy Minister, in his year of retirement, was about to depart for the capital but decided to seek another prefecture before fully retiring. He stopped at a place called Guan Ci Ben Niu and stayed under an embankment. It was a scorching summer, and the moonlight was clear and bright. He commanded his attendants to sleep and opened the boat door to sit quietly. In the second watch of the night, he heard a voice from the shore saying, "My child will pass by here tomorrow. Please all of you pull the boat with all your strength. The child is young, and I fear he might be frightened." The Deputy Minister was greatly surprised and climbed ashore to look around. Everyone was sound asleep, except for a group of cows lying under the eaves of the house. The next day, he anchored the boat and waited. Soon, there was someone called the supervisor of the records, who was just turned twenty and passed by there. When the boat reached the embankment, the cows did not need to be shouted at or beaten; they spun like the wind and passed the embankment in a moment. The Deputy Minister sighed and said, "I have served as an official and governed the people all my life. I consider myself to have done no wrong. How can I, in my old age, still strive for the state's affairs?" He immediately submitted a petition to retire and returned south to Yuhang. The child of the cow, whose name and family are not recorded, was avoided by the Deputy Minister in his writings.

    17

    ○刘密学
    　　天禧中，刘密学师道守潭州，有衡山民之长沙市易者，冒夜而行，道中见旌旗仪卫，呵导甚厉，民相与拱立道左，因询前驱者曰：“何处大官”曰：“潭州刘密学授南岳北门侍郎，明日礼上。”是夜，复有内臣江供奉者来岳庙烧香，宿庙下，梦供帐纷纭言新官礼上，洎见，乃刘密学也。又，马尚书亮，时尹京南，午己之间，有一道士至，客次展谒，谓曰：“侍郎已下厅，不敢通刺。”道士曰：“无他事，欲投潭州刘密学书耳。”典谒曰：“既要相见，何不早来”又曰：“为今日南岳北门侍郎上事毕方来，以故后时。”言讫，失道士所在。晚衙马视事，典谒以告，马大惊，以为不祥，数日，凶讣至。考道士求见之辰，刘捐馆之日也。先是刘在长沙，一旦称受子赴阙，即具舟舰，立俾徙行李、族属于舟中，又曰：“吾未交符印，今日且宿寺居。”明日，洗沐讫，穿膝坐正寝，俨然而逝。今衡潭之人严奉之，礼与岳神等。或闻祖舍人士衡有传。

    Explanation

    17

    During the Tianxi era, Liu Shidao, the governor of Tan Prefecture, was in Hunan. A person from Mount Heng was traveling to Changsha at night to trade. On the road, he saw a procession with banners and guards, and the command was very strict. The people stood with their hands clasped on the left side of the road. He asked the person in front, "Where is the high-ranking official?" The person replied, "Governor Liu Shidao of Tan Prefecture has been appointed as the South Gate Attendant of Mount Heng, and he will take up his post tomorrow."

    Later, there was an imperial eunuch named Jiang who came to the temple to burn incense. He stayed at the temple and had a dream in which he saw a grand assembly and heard that a new official would take up his post. When he woke up, he saw that it was Governor Liu Shidao.

    Also, Ma Liang, the Shangshu (Minister) of the Southern Capital, was governing at the time. During the noon to the hour of the sheep (11 AM to 1 PM), a Taoist priest arrived and visited the guest quarters. He said, "The Shangshu has already left the hall, so I dare not deliver the message." The Taoist priest replied, "I have no other business; I only want to deliver a letter to Governor Liu Shidao of Tan Prefecture." The official in charge said, "If you wanted to meet, why didn't you come earlier?" The Taoist priest said, "I will come after the ceremony of the South Gate Attendant of Mount Heng is completed today, which is why I am late." After he finished speaking, the Taoist priest disappeared.

    In the evening, when Ma Liang was handling official business, the official in charge reported what had happened. Ma Liang was greatly alarmed and considered it an omen. A few days later, the news of Liu Shidao's death arrived. It turned out that the day the Taoist priest wanted to see him was the same day Liu Shidao died.

    Before this, Liu Shidao was in Changsha. One day, he claimed to have received an imperial decree and was going to the capital. He immediately prepared boats and ships, ordered his family and belongings to be moved onto them, and said, "I have not yet taken up my official seal and stamp, so I will stay in a temple today." The next day, after washing and dressing, he sat cross-legged in the main bedroom and passed away in a dignified manner.

    Now, the people of Heng and Tan venerate him strictly, with the same rites as the mountain god. It is said that there are records or stories about this in the ancestral hall of the Li family.

    18

    ○刘待制
    　　待制刘公，彭城人，清修检重，时所推与，自金陵尹移守高密，时已抱疾，乘船沿淮，至水车驿舍遂卒。先是驿居人见驱群羊及负荷酒食横陈之具，入驿者视之则无人，如此累日，刘既卒，始悟鬼神之来迓。水车沟在海、密州界。
    　　○杨省副
    　　杨省副日华自言：应举日，与数同人税宅于饮马巷，居数月无他异。一日探榜归，时春季颇暄，相与解带席地而坐，俄觉身之欹侧者再三，以谓地动，问诸仆隶，则不知。杨取剔耳篦画甓罅中，胃出浅红线，长数寸，以手牵之，有缣衣如线色，随牵而长，约尺余。惧而舍之，其下若有人引之者，徐徐尽入。坐者大骇，莫敢发视，即时迁于旅邸。

    Explanation

    18

    The Attendant Scholar Liu

    Attendant Scholar Liu Gong, from Pengcheng, was known for his pure and refined character, strict and serious demeanor, and was highly esteemed by his contemporaries. He was transferred to govern Gaomi from his position as the magistrate of Jinling, but he was already ill. Traveling by boat along the Huai River, he died at the Waterwheel Inn. Prior to this, the inn's residents had seen a group of sheep being driven along with food and drink laid out in a disordered manner. Those who entered the inn found no one there, and this phenomenon occurred repeatedly over several days. After Liu's death, they finally realized that the ghosts and spirits had come to welcome him. The Waterwheel Gully is located in the border area between Hai and Mì states.

    The Provincial Deputy Yang

    Yang Shengfu, the Provincial Deputy, recounted: On the day he took the imperial examinations, he and several companions rented a house in Drinking Horse Lane. They stayed there for several months without any unusual occurrences. One day, after checking the results of the exam, they returned on a spring day when the weather was quite warm. They unbuckled their belts and sat on the ground, relaxing together. Suddenly, they felt their bodies leaning repeatedly. They thought it was an earthquake and asked their servants, but the servants did not know what was happening. Yang took a comb for cleaning ears and saw a thin red line drawn in the crack of a brick. The line was about an inch long. He pulled it with his hand, and a fine silk garment appeared, colored like a thread, and it grew longer as he pulled it, reaching about a foot in length. Frightened, he let go of it, and it seemed that someone was pulling it from below, gradually disappearing completely. Those sitting with him were greatly frightened and dared not look at it. They immediately moved to an inn.

    19

    ○魏侍郎
    　　刑部侍郎魏公，初以金部员外郎知洪州，罢官，舟经大孤山。方乘顺风，杨ぎ甚，一女使涤器而坠水，援之不及，舟速浪沸，顷刻已十里余，公惋叹良久。一女奴忽沉冥狂语趋前，而举止语言皆所溺婢也，泣且言曰：“某不幸而溺于水，实命之至是，无所恨。然服勤左右久矣，一旦不以理而终，夫岂不大戚耶倘岁时月朔赐草具馔，化楮泉于户外，使某得以歆领，虽泉下亦不忘报。”公与夫人闻之恻然，悉允其求。语次，一渔艇载所溺婢棹及公舟，告曰：“溺婢为浪泊而出，获援之以送。”婢固醒，然未尝死，而女奴亦不复降语。

    Explanation

    19

    Minister Wei of the Wei Dynasty, Deputy Minister of Justice, was initially appointed as Officer of the Gold Department and Governor of Hongzhou. After being dismissed from office, his boat passed by Dagu Mountain. Riding the favorable wind, the boat moved swiftly, and a female servant fell into the water while washing a utensil. Unable to save her, the boat moved swiftly through the turbulent waves, traveling more than ten miles in a short while. The minister lamented deeply for a long time. Suddenly, a female servant rushed forward in a trance-like state, speaking wildly, and her movements and words were those of the servant who had fallen into the water. She wept and said, "Unfortunate as it was for me to drown in the water, it was truly my fate, and I have no regrets. However, I had served faithfully for a long time, and if I did not die in a proper way, would that not be a great sorrow? If you would provide simple food offerings on seasonal and monthly occasions and burn paper money outside the house, allowing me to enjoy it, even in the afterlife, I would never forget to repay you." The minister and his wife, moved by her words, fully granted her request. As they spoke, a fishing boat carrying the servant who had fallen into the water approached their boat and said, "The servant who drowned was rescued from the waves and brought here." The servant was indeed awake, but she had not actually died, and the female servant no longer spoke.

    20

    ○司马少卿
    　　太常少卿司马公里自言：未冠时，侍仲父待制光山县，门下客张某者亦年少，同舍肄业，常苦资用不足。张忽叹曰：“□□□□愿得乾汞法，以快吾欲。旁有黥卒执汛扫之役者，笑曰：“秀才年少，安知世间有此事耶”张曰：“神仙之术不可妄求，岂不知之乎”卒曰：“某尝得此术，愿试之。”张大喜，脱衣质钱市汞及炭，初夜，以水银一两纳鼎中，出小瓢取药一粒如芥子投之，又以小瓦覆鼎口，泥封甚密，炽炭围之，急扇良久，鼎中如风声，倾之成白金矣。翌日，召金工视之，曰：“此汞银也。比闻有黥卒得此术，间或鬻之，岂非此人所为乎”张亦秘而不言。张谓司马曰：“斯人而有斯术也，图之固易，然缓而取之善也。”自此屡以美言抚存之。一日请浣衣于江滨，去遂不复，竟不知所适。

    Explanation

    20

    A Story of the Master of the Imperial Rituals

    The Deputy Master of the Imperial Rituals, Master Sigu, recounted: In his youth, before he had received his cap, he served as an attendant to his elder brother, the Deputy Master of Guangshan County. Among his fellow students, there was a young man named Zhang who also struggled with insufficient funds for his studies. One day, Zhang sighed and said, "I wish to learn the method of alchemy with mercury to satisfy my desires." A tattooed soldier who performed menial tasks nearby laughed and said, "Young scholar, how could you know that such things exist in the world?" Zhang replied, "The arts of immortals cannot be sought lightly; do you not know this?" The soldier said, "I have once obtained this technique and am willing to demonstrate it." Zhang was greatly pleased and pawned his clothes to buy mercury and charcoal. On the first night, he placed one ounce of mercury in a cauldron, used a small ladle to take a pill as tiny as a mustard seed and dropped it in, then covered the mouth of the cauldron with a small tile, sealed it tightly with clay, surrounded it with burning charcoal, and fanned it vigorously for a long time. The cauldron made a sound like the wind, and when he poured out the contents, it had turned into silver. The next day, he summoned a goldsmith to examine it, who said, "This is amalgamated silver. I have heard that a tattooed soldier has this technique and sometimes sells it. Could this not be the work of this person?" Zhang kept the secret and did not speak of it. He told Master Sigu, "This person possesses this technique; plotting against him is easy, but it is better to proceed slowly." From then on, he often used kind words to maintain the relationship. One day, the soldier asked to wash clothes at the riverbank and left, never to return, and his whereabouts remained unknown.

    21

    ○梁学士
    　　梁状元固，博达俊伟人也，未仕室职于史馆，数年而卒，未克敛，凭侍姬玉儿者降灵语云：“吾今弃世才信宿，家事不治乃尔。”又召子弟戒敕曰：“吾家素贫，尚有铅器数十，事兼朝廷，必有赠赐，足办丧事，不得倚四郎中，但托祖舍人可也。”家人问曰：“学士今居何所”云：“见作阴山谏议，寄任不轻。”又索毫楮作启。令子弟取某书还某家，于某家取所借某书，还者收，取者得。复索茶，合饮一杯已，手自封牌，真梁之迹也。须臾乃去，姬如醉醒，诘之殊不自如。

    Explanation

    21

    Liang, the scholar, was an exceptionally knowledgeable and talented individual. He held a position in the history bureau but had not yet entered official service. After several years, he passed away, and his funeral preparations were incomplete. The spirit of his concubine, Yu'er, appeared and spoke, saying, "I have just left this world for a short time, and the family has neglected its duties." She then instructed the family members, "Our family has been poor historically, but there are still some lead utensils left. Because of my position, I would likely receive gifts from the court, which should be enough to cover the funeral expenses. Do not rely on the assistance of Si Langzhong; instead, trust Zu She Ren." She asked, "Where is the scholar now?" and was told, "He is serving as a counselor in the underworld, with a significant role." She requested ink and paper to write a letter, instructing the family members to retrieve a book from a specific family and to return a borrowed book from another family, with the borrower receiving it back. She then requested tea and drank a cup together, sealing a document with her own hand. These actions confirmed that they were indeed those of Liang. After a short time, she left, and Yu'er woke up as if from a trance, unable to explain what had happened.

    22

    ○张郎中
    　　张郎中景晟，洛阳人也，去华侍郎之孙，登进士第，始逾强仕，为屯田郎中。熙宁四年，奉朝请于京师，忽疡生于手，痛不可忍。时有御医仇鼎者，专治创，呼视之，遂取少药傅其上，既而苦楚尤甚，仇虽复注以善药，而痛不能已，数日而卒。沉困之际，但云：“仇鼎杀我，必诉于阴府，不汝致也。”月余，仇坐药肆中，见二人，一衣绯一衣绿，入鼎家，手持符檄，谓鼎曰：“张郎中有状相讼，可往对事。

    Explanation

    22

    Zhang Langzhong Jingsheng, a native of Luoyang, was the grandson of Shilang Qu Hua. He passed the imperial examination and became a Jinshi, serving as a Langzhong responsible for managing state-owned land and agricultural production. In the fourth year of Xining, he attended court in the capital. Suddenly, an ulcer appeared on his hand, causing unbearable pain. At the time, there was an imperial physician named Chou Ding, who specialized in treating wounds and ulcers. Chou was called to examine Zhang and applied a small amount of medicine to the ulcer. However, the pain worsened, and despite Chou applying more good medicine, the pain could not be relieved. Zhang died after several days. In his deep suffering, he said, "Chou Ding has killed me; I will surely complain to the underworld and not let you get away with it." A month later, Chou was sitting in his pharmacy when he saw two people, one dressed in red and the other in green. They entered Chou's home, holding a talisman and an official document, and said to Chou, "There is a complaint against Zhang Langzhong; you should go to face the matter."

    23

    ”仇曰：“张郎中病疽而死，何预我事”绯衣曰：“奉命相逮，不知其他。”仇知不免，哀求延数日之命，二人相顾曰：“延三日可矣。”绯衣曰：“虽然，当记之而去。”遂出一印，印其膝下，遂不见。所印之处即肿溃，创中所出如膏油，痛若火灼，后三日而死。始仇之知张橐实良厚，款欲先以毒药溃其创，然后加良药愈之，以邀重赂，遂至不救。鬼之来，独鼎见之，左右但见纷纭号诉而已。噫！庸医之视疾，多以药返其病，使困而后治，欲取厚谢，因而致毙者众矣。倘尽若张君之显报，则小人之心庶几乎革矣。

    Explanation

    23

    "Chou said, 'Zhang Langzhong died of a boil, what does it have to do with me?' The man in red clothes replied, 'I came on a mission to apprehend you, I don't know about anything else.' Chou realized he could not escape and pleaded for an extension of his life by a few days. The two men looked at each other and said, 'We can extend your life by three days.' The man in red clothes said, 'Even so, we must mark it and leave.' He then took out a seal and stamped it on Chou's knee, and disappeared. The place where it was stamped immediately swelled and burst, the wound oozed like oil, and the pain was as if burned by fire. Three days later, Chou died. It turned out that Chou knew Zhang Tu very well, and intended to first use poison to break open the wound, then apply good medicine to heal it, in order to seek a large bribe, which ultimately led to his death. When the ghost appeared, only Ding saw it, while those around only saw chaos and cries. Alas! Mediocre doctors treating diseases often worsen the illness with medicine, making the patient suffer before treating, seeking a generous reward, and as a result, many people have died. If all doctors were punished like Zhang Jun, perhaps the hearts of the wicked might be reformed."

    24

    ○韩侍中
    　　侍中韩公稚圭知泰州日，卧疾数日，冥冥无所知，倏然而，语左右曰：“适梦以手捧天者再，不觉惊悟。”其后援英宗于藩邸，翼神宗于春宫，捧天之祥已兆于庆历中。固知贤臣之勋业，非偶然而致也。
    　　○张职方
    　　张职方，太宁宿州人，家富于财，登进士第，性恶鸱，每至官，必下令左右挟弹逐之。熙宁六年，丁内艰，权居于符离之佛寺，尝有鸱巢于殿之鱼尾。育二雏，羽翼渐成，飞跃于外，鸣啸不已，张亲弹之，中丸而毙。既而二大鸱盘空，鸣声甚悲。翌日，张步庭中，一鸱下抟其巾，方惊骇，一鸱复来攫，伤其鬓，创亦不甚，旬余溃决，腐及喉，遂死。嗟乎！哀子之死，仁也；报子之仇，义也。孰谓禽兽无仁义之心乎父子之道天性也，处万物之灵，亲爱之心宜其甚焉。熙宁甲寅乙卯岁，天下蝗旱，至父子相啖者，真禽兽之不若也。悲夫！

    Explanation

    24

    Translation

    Han the Attendant

    During his tenure as the Attendant in Taizhou, Han Gong Zhi Gui fell ill and lay bedridden for several days, in a state of deep unconsciousness, knowing nothing. Suddenly, he woke up with a start and told those around him, "I just had a dream where I held up the sky twice, and I was not aware of it until I woke up." Later, he supported Emperor Yingzong during his time in the palace of a prince and assisted Emperor Shenzong during his time as the crown prince. The auspicious sign of holding up the sky had already been foretold during the Qingli era. It is clear that the achievements of a virtuous minister are not achieved by chance.

    Zhang the Inspector

    Zhang the Inspector, from Taoning Xuzhou, was wealthy and passed the imperial examination. He had a strong aversion to owls and, whenever he took office, would order his attendants to carry catapults and chase them away. In the sixth year of Xining, he encountered a period of mourning for a close relative and temporarily resided at a temple in Fuli. Once, an owl built its nest on the roof of the temple, which was shaped like a fish tail. The owl raised two chicks, whose wings gradually grew, and they flew out, continuously making a loud, mournful sound. Zhang personally shot one of the owls, and it was killed by the projectile. Soon after, two large owls circled in the sky, making very sad calls. The next day, as Zhang walked in the courtyard, one owl swooped down and grabbed his hat, causing him to be startled. Another owl then came and attacked him, injuring his hair. The wound was not severe, but after a few weeks, it became infected and pus spread to his throat, leading to his death. Alas! Mourning the death of one's child is an act of compassion; avenging one's child is an act of justice. Who would say that animals lack a sense of righteousness? The relationship between father and son is a natural law, and among all intelligent beings, the feeling of love and affection should be especially strong. During the Xining years of Jia Yin and Yi Mao, there was a nationwide famine and drought, to the point where fathers and sons ate each other. Truly, they were worse than animals. How sad!

    25

    ○陈少卿
    　　太常少卿陈公希亮，曩岁刺宿州，厅事后门常扃钥，相传云开则有怪云见。陈刚方明，决不之信，遽命启之，果有群妖昼夜隐见于房闼间，陈亦不甚惧。一日，偶至土地堂，见土偶数十，疑其为妖，命碎之，投诸汴水，妖遂绝。盖每岁立春出土牛，牛既为众所分裂，衙卒乃取策牛人置于土地之祠也。
    　　○杨状豫前进士黄通与状元杨公相善，尝梦杨投刺自称龙首山人。庆历初，既登第，丁内艰，未终丧而卒。其后好事者解之曰：“龙首，谓状元登第也；山人，无禄之称也。”

    Explanation

    25

    Final Translation

    Tchen Shaoqing

    Tchen Gong Xiliang, the Vice Minister of Rites, served as the governor of Suzhou in the past year. The back door of the hall was usually locked, and it was said that a strange phenomenon appeared when it was opened. Tchen Xiliang was firm, upright, and wise, and he did not believe the rumors. He immediately ordered the door to be opened, and indeed, a group of spirits appeared and disappeared between the rooms day and night. Tchen Xiliang was not very afraid. One day, he happened to visit the land god's temple and saw several dozen clay figures. Suspecting they were spirits, he ordered them to be broken and threw them into the Bian River, which eliminated the spirits. It was said that during the beginning of spring, a clay ox was made, and once it was divided by the crowd, the officials placed the person who made the ox in the land god's temple.

    Yang Zhangyu

    Yang Zangyu, a candidate for the imperial examination, was friends with the top-ranked scholar Huang Tong. Once, Huang Tong dreamed that Yang Zangyu submitted a letter of introduction and called himself a man from Longshou Mountain. During the early years of the Qingli era, after passing the imperial examination, Yang Zangyu suffered the death of a close relative and died before the mourning period ended. Later, those who were interested explained that "Longshou" means "top rank" and "Shanren" means "a recluse without an official salary."

    26

    ○郭延卿
    　　郭延卿，洛阳人，少以文行称于乡里，吕公蒙正、张公齐贤未第时，皆以师友事之。太平兴国中，陈抟自华州被召，抟素以知人名天下，及道西洛，三人者皆进谒，抟倒履迎之，目吕曰：“先辈当状元及第，位至宰相；张先辈科名虽在行间，而福禄延永又过于吕。”然殊不言延卿。于是二人相与言曰：“郭君文行，乡里所椎，辛与一目。”抟曰：“固知之，然亦甚好。”遂草草别去，抟送之门，顾张吕二君：“今晚更过访。”及期往，抟曰：“二君前程，某固已言，然所惜延卿禄薄，伺吕君作相，始合得一命，张君作相，当得职官耳。”既而吕果状元中第，及为相，荐延卿得试校书郎。及张作相，益念郭之潦倒，一夕语其子宗诲曰：“为我作奏札子，荐郭延卿京官。”及翌日造朝，遽索奏扎，宗诲草奏，误书京字为职字，及书可，降制乃职官，皆如抟言也。

    Explanation

    26

    De Guo Yanqing

    Guo Yanqing, from Luoyang, was renowned in his hometown for both his literary talent and moral character when he was young. During the reign of Emperor Taizong of Song, when Lu Mengzheng and Zhang Qixian had not yet passed the imperial examinations, they both treated Guo Yanqing as a teacher and friend. In the early years of the Taiping Xingguo era, Chen Tuan, who was summoned from Huazhou, was famous for his ability to recognize talent. When Chen Tuan traveled to Xi Luo, the three men paid him a visit. Chen Tuan removed his shoes to greet them, and he looked at Lu and said, "You will become the top scholar and reach the position of prime minister; although Zhang's official career may not be as prominent, your longevity and fortune will surpass that of Lu." However, he did not mention Guo Yanqing at all. Thus, the two men said to each other, "Guo's literary talent and moral character are well-known in the village, yet he received only one glance from Chen." Chen replied, "I know this, but he is also very good." They then parted hastily, and Chen Tuan saw them off at the gate, saying to Zhang and Lu, "Come visit me again tonight." When they arrived as agreed, Chen Tuan said, "Your future prospects, I have already mentioned, but I am sorry for Guo Yanqing's meager official salary. When Lu becomes prime minister, he will finally receive an appointment; when Zhang becomes prime minister, he will become an official." Indeed, Lu eventually became the top scholar and then prime minister, recommending Guo Yanqing to take the exam for the position of junior scholar-official. When Zhang became prime minister, he felt even more concerned about Guo's impoverished state. One night, he told his son Zonghui, "Write an imperial edict for me to recommend Guo Yanqing for a position in the capital." The next day, when they went to court, Chen Tuan suddenly asked for the edict. Zonghui hastily wrote it, mistakenly writing "capital" instead of "official." When the edict was approved, it was decreed that Guo Yanqing would become an official, just as Chen Tuan had predicted.

    27

    ●卷三
    　　○马少保
    　　太子少保马公亮自言：少肄业于庐州城外佛寺，一夕临窗烛下阅书，有大手如扇自窗伸于公前，若有所索，公不为视，阅书如故，如是比夜而至。公因语人，有道士云：“素闻鬼畏雄黄，可试以辟之。”公乃研雄黄渍水，密置案上。是夕大手又至，公遽以笔濡雄黄，大书一草字。书毕，闻窗外大呼曰：“速为我涤去，不然，祸及与汝。”公雅不为听，停烛而寝。有顷，怒甚，而索涤愈急，公不应，逮晓更哀鸣而不能缩，且曰：“公将大贵，我且不为他怪，徒以相戏而犯公，何忍遽致我于极地耶我固得罪，而幽冥之状由公以彰暴于世，亦非公之利也。公独不见温峤尾犀照牛渚之事乎”公大悟，即以水涤去草字，且戒他日勿复扰人，怪逊谢而去。

    Explanation

    27

    Volume Three
    Chapter: Marquis Ma

    Marquis Ma Shao-bao recounted that when he was young, he was studying at a Buddhist temple outside the city of Luzhou. One night, while reading by the window under the candlelight, a large hand like a fan extended through the window towards him, as if making a demand. He did not look at it and continued reading as usual. This happened repeatedly at night. He then told others about it, and a Taoist priest said, "I have heard that ghosts fear realgar. You could try using it to repel them." Ma Shao-bao then ground realgar into a paste, mixed it with water, and secretly placed it on the desk. That night, the large hand came again. Ma Shao-bao quickly dipped his pen in the realgar and wrote a large grass character. After finishing, he heard a loud shout from outside the window: "Quickly wash it away, or I will bring disaster upon you!" He did not listen and put out the candle to go to sleep. Soon after, the ghost became very angry, and its demand for the wash became more urgent. Ma Shao-bao did not respond. By dawn, the ghost continued to mourn in a sorrowful voice and could not retract its hand, saying, "You will become very powerful. I will not cause other troubles, but I am only here to play and offend you. How can I bear to be brought to such a dire state? I have already committed a fault, and the state of the underworld will be revealed to the world through you, which is also not beneficial for you. Have you not seen the story of Wen Qiao using his rhinoceros horn to illuminate the river at Niu Zhu?" Ma Shao-bao suddenly realized the truth. He immediately washed away the grass character and warned the ghost not to disturb people again in the future. The ghost apologized and left.

    28

    ○潘郎中
    　　潘郎中继宗，清河人，以明经发第，有吏材。天圣中，自国子博士通判乾宁军。其母亡以十余岁，一日，于堂前呼家人令召其子，容状衣服宛如平昔。潘再拜号哭，母急止之曰：“可于堂西偏隔以幕，前下一帘，中安二榻，吾将与伴我者二妇人息焉。”既而语云：“吾死，亦无大过，阴官但致我一室中，不令他适，汝既升朝，封我为县太君，阴官乃纵我出入。汝前岁知寻江县，我尝至彼相视，以水晶柱斧倒置植扉后，吾亦未有生期，恐久溷汝，聊以为识也。今我往生冀州北门内街西磨坊某人媳妇处为女，因得来此。”家人日夕具饮食，惟闻匕箸声，视之如故，留月余告去，举家送之郊外，空中有哭泣声，久而不闻。潘既受代，道出信都，询之皆如所说。潘后常以缗帛遗其家，潘之子士龙，今为正郎。胡讷尝著《孝行录》，亦记潘夫人事。
    　　○乐大卿

    Explanation

    28

    ○Pan Langzhong
    Pan Langzhong Jizong, from Qinghe, passed the mingjing examination and was granted an official position, and he had administrative talent. During the Tian圣 era, he served as the tongpan of Qianning Military District, having previously been a guozijiao bo (Doctor of the Imperial Academy). His mother had passed away more than ten years ago. One day, she appeared before him at the front of the hall, calling his family to summon her son. Her appearance and attire were just as they were in life. Pan bowed twice and wept, and his mother quickly stopped him, saying, "You can set up a curtain rod and a curtain in the western side of the hall, hang a screen in front, and place two beds inside. I will rest here with the two women who accompany me." She then said, "After my death, I did not commit any grave offenses, so the officials of the underworld confined me to a single room and did not allow me to go elsewhere. Once you entered the imperial court, you should have me posthumously enfeoffed as a County Lady, and only then would the officials of the underworld permit me to come and go freely. Last year, when you served as the magistrate of Xunjian County, I visited you there. I placed a crystal column-shaped axe upside down behind the door as a sign. I do not yet have a fixed time for rebirth, but I am afraid of troubling you for too long, so I left this as a marker. Now I have been reborn as a girl in the home of a certain woman in the western street of the northern gate of Jizhou, which is why I have come here." The family prepared food and drink for her every day, and they could only hear the sound of chopsticks and spoons, but she appeared as usual. After staying for more than a month, she announced her departure, and the whole family accompanied her to the outskirts of the city, where they heard a cry in the air that eventually faded away. After Pan was relieved of his post, he passed through Xindu on his journey, and upon inquiring, everything matched what his mother had said. Afterward, Pan often sent silk and money to his mother's family. His son, Shi Long, is now a zhenglang (Senior Civil Servant). Hu Ne once wrote Xiaoxing Lu (《孝行录》), which also records the story of Pan's mother.

    29

    光禄卿乐公滋，性沉厚，少年修学时，尝就祖母寝榻前灯下看书。一夕二鼓后，灯檠摇，动如人携持，周行室中复止故处，乐亦不惧。明日言于门下客，客不之信，是夜取檠置学舍中，明灯而坐，才二鼓，复行如初，客大呼而走。遂命斧碎，亦无他异。
    　　○徐郎中
    　　徐郎中，莱州人，忘其名，弱冠，侍父假守岭外。乾兴中，仁宗登极，部贺礼赴阙，至武陵一驿，将舍正寝，驿卒言：“其中有物怪往来，无敢居者，愿易他次。”虽不以为然，亦出寝于厅之屏后。夜将半，梦有神人状甚伟，手携竹篮，其中皆人鼻也，叱：“汝何等人，敢辄居此以妨吾路”徐恐惧愧谢，神乃端视之，曰：“形相非薄，但其鼻曲而下，吾与若易之。”遂于篮中择一鼻，先劓徐鼻掷去，以所择鼻安之，仍以手指周固四际，梦中亦觉痛楚。神笑曰：“好一正郎鼻也。”徐之鼻素不隆正，自梦易之后，自然端直。历官驾部郎中，致仕，随其子秘书丞朔在维扬签判，治平四年物故。

    Explanation

    29

    The Right Minister Le Gongzi, known for his profound and substantial character, was once a young scholar. During his early studies, he would often read by the light of a lamp in front of his grandmother's bed. One night, after the second drumbeat, the lampstand began to shake as if it were being carried by someone, moving around the room before returning to its original position. Despite this, Le Gongzi was not afraid. The next day, he told this to his followers, but they did not believe him. That night, he took the lampstand and placed it in his study, lit the lamp, and sat down. Just as the second drumbeat sounded, the lampstand moved again as before, causing his followers to shout and run away. He then ordered the lampstand to be smashed with an axe, and there were no further strange occurrences.

    ○ Minister Xu
    Minister Xu was from Laizhou, and his name is forgotten. As a young adult, he accompanied his father, who was temporarily governing the southern regions. During the reign of Emperor Renzong, when the emperor ascended the throne, Xu led the ceremonial delegation to the capital. They arrived at a驿站 in Wuling, where they were about to stay in the main hall. The station attendant said, "There are strange creatures that come and go here, and no one dares to stay. Please choose another place." Although Xu did not agree, he still slept behind the screen in the hall. In the middle of the night, he dreamed of a tall and imposing divine figure holding a bamboo basket filled with human noses. The figure scolded, "What kind of person are you to dare to stay here and obstruct my path?" Xu was filled with fear and apologized. The divine figure then looked at him carefully and said, "Your appearance is not bad, but your nose is crooked and low. I will exchange it for you." The figure then selected a nose from the basket, first cutting off Xu's nose and throwing it away, and then placing the selected nose on him, securing it firmly with his fingers. Even in the dream, Xu felt pain. The divine figure smiled and said, "What a fine nose for a minister!" Xu's nose had never been straight, but after the dream, it naturally became so. He served as a minister in the Department of Transport, retired, and lived with his son, the Secretary of the Secretariat, in Yangzhou. He passed away in the fourth year of the Zhiping era.

    30

    ○刘太博
    　　兴州依山为守居，层叠而上，正寝尤高，复构楼于上，俯视仪门如指掌。宝元中，太常博士刘公中达假守是郡，一日与家人登楼，见白衣者入客次，若举人状，刘遽曰：“有客至，吾将延之。”遂下楼升厅。果有举人投刺，刘接之坐，移刻，各不语。告去，遂循东庑而下，左右告曰：“当自西庑。”举人不答，直趋东庑井次，投身而入。刘大骇，遽索井中，无所得，而亦不能究举人者自何而来。月余刘卒。

    Explanation

    30

    In the prefecture of Xingzhou, the governor's residence was built into the mountains, with layers of buildings rising step by step, and the main hall was especially high, with another building constructed on top. From this vantage point, the ceremonial gate could be seen as clearly as the palm of one's hand. During the reign of Emperor Zhaozong in the Bao Yuan period, Mr. Liu Zhongda, a Grand Doctor of the Imperial Academy, was temporarily appointed to govern this prefecture. One day, he climbed the tower with his family and saw a person in white clothes entering the guest room, who looked like a scholar. Mr. Liu immediately said, "There is a guest arriving, I will invite him." He then descended from the tower and went to the hall. Indeed, a scholar presented a visiting card, and Mr. Liu received him and seated him. After a while, they did not speak. The scholar then left, following the eastern wing downward. The attendants said, "One should go from the western wing." The scholar did not respond and went directly to the well in the eastern wing, jumping in. Mr. Liu was greatly frightened and immediately searched the well, but found nothing. He could not investigate where the scholar came from. After a month, Mr. Liu died.

    31

    ○刁左藏
    　　刁左藏允升，尝提举大名府左厢马监，在职岁余卒。其家先寓于大名朝城县，熙宁二年秋，刁捐馆半岁，次子总忽见父坐于城门之侧，行李从者，无异平昔，惟从人悉衣白。方惊惧，其父以手招之，即诣前拜且哭，刁遽止之，总问曰：“大人今主何事”刁曰：“吾尝事范希文，渠今主阴府，俾我提举行疫者。今欲往许州以南巡按，道出此，故暂来视汝。”因曰：“汝母明年八月当死，但预为备，勿告之，恐渠忧挠。孙某来年五月亦当卒。此皆冥籍先定，汝宜自宽。”孙乃总之爱子也。又曰：“市中仇某不半岁，必刑死。”因怀中取鸦青纸一幅，有金书七十余字，授总曰：“善保持，勿失坠。

    Explanation

    31

    刁左藏允升，曾任大名府左厢马监提举，任职一年多后去世。他的家人原本居住在大名府的朝城县。熙宁二年的秋天，刁左藏去世半年后，他的次子刁总突然见到父亲坐在城门旁边，随行的行李和仆从与往常无异，只是仆人们都穿着白色的衣服。刁总正感到惊恐时，父亲用手招呼他，他立刻上前跪拜哭泣，父亲急忙制止了他。刁总问道：“父亲现在负责什么？”父亲回答说：“我曾侍奉过范希文，现在他主管阴府，让我负责管理那些因疫病而死的人。我现在打算前往许州以南巡视，路过这里，所以暂时来看看你。”接着说：“你母亲明年八月将会去世，你可以提前做好准备，但不要告诉她，以免她忧心忡忡。孙某明年五月也会去世。这些都是冥籍中早已注定的，你应该放宽心。”孙某是刁总最疼爱的儿子。父亲又说：“市中的仇某不到半年就会被处决。”随后从怀里拿出一张乌黑色的纸，上面用金笔写了七十多个字，交给刁总说：“要好好保管，不要丢失。”

    32

    ”遂上马呵道出南门而去，闾巷悉见。行数里，逢市人张五者，避立路左，刁谓之曰：“我欲倩君可乎”张曰：“诺。”乃谓曰：“若暂到我家，语吾儿：后月南市当灾，且慎之，我已留后者五人防视，必免焚如。”张亦不知是鬼也，遂诣刁宅，欲达其语，闻宅中大哭。少选，总出询，方知刁久已弃世。其妻洎孙如期而死。邑中官吏知有火灾，日夕戒居人储水，谨火禁，月余火自空屋发，与刁居密迩，四邻悉焚，惟刁宅独完。仇某者闻当刑死，杜门不出，一日与客奕棋于所居之门下，有诵佛书而丐者，仇屡谢之不去，语颇不逊，仇忘刁之言，殴之即死，竟毙于枯木。金书人皆不识之，字书亦无。

    Explanation

    32

    Then he mounted his horse, shouted for a clear path, and left through the south gate, and everyone in the streets and alleys saw him. After traveling several miles, he met a commoner named Zhang Wu, who stood aside on the left side of the road. Dao asked him, "May I ask you to do something for me?" Zhang replied, "Yes." Dao then said, "If you go to my house temporarily, tell my son: next month the southern market will face disaster, be careful. I have left five people to guard and watch, and they will certainly avoid burning." Zhang did not know that Dao was a ghost, so he went to Dao's house, intending to convey the message. He heard loud crying in the house. A short while later, everyone came out and asked, only then knowing that Dao had long ago died. His wife and grandson died as scheduled. The officials in the town knew there would be a fire disaster, and warned residents day and night to store water and be cautious about fire prohibition. More than a month later, fire started from an empty house, very close to Dao's house, and all four neighbors burned, but only Dao's house remained intact. A certain enemy heard he was to be punished to death, shut the door and did not go out. One day, with a guest, he played chess under his residence's gate. There was a beggar who recited Buddhist scriptures, and he repeatedly refused him and did not leave. His speech was quite rude. He forgot Dao's words, beat him, and he died immediately, finally dying on a dead tree. People all did not recognize it, and character books also none.

    33

    ○吕郎中
    　　吕郎中元规，治平初为广南东路提点刑狱，公宇在韶州，宅堂之后有园亭，亭下植荔枝数株，夏五月实尽丹，翌日，将召宾僚开樽以赏之。其亭暮则扃，人迹所不至，诘旦启户，无一实在枝，但见壳核盈地，于板壁题诗一绝云：我曹今日会家亲，手把洪钟饮数巡。满地狼藉不知晓，荔枝还是一番新。岁余，吕以事去官。

    Explanation

    33

    Translation:

    The Magistrate of Luoyang

    Magistrate Lu Yuanwei, during the early Zhiping era, served as the Inspector of Criminal Justice for the Eastern Road of Guangnan. His official residence was in Shaoyang Prefecture, where behind the main hall stood a garden pavilion. Beneath the pavilion were several litchi trees. In the fifth month of summer, the litchi fruit ripened and turned red. The next day, he intended to invite his guests and serve wine to enjoy the fruit. The pavilion was locked at night and seldom visited. The following morning, when the door was opened, there was not a single litchi left on the trees; instead, the ground was littered with shells and seeds. On the wall, he inscribed a short poem:

    "We gathered today with family and friends,
    Holding cups of wine and drinking several rounds.
    The ground was littered, and we didn't know what happened,
    The litchi trees are as new as ever."

    After a year or so, Magistrate Lu was dismissed from office due to some matter.

    34

    ○钱斋郎
    　　治平中，有钱斋郎者调于吏部，挈其妻居京师。一日，其妻被夫之衣冠，语言皆男子也，状如病心，召符禁者视之，术皆不效。闻孔监丞者有道术，能已人疾苦，遂诣其居，告以妻之所为，孔许至其居。翌日，乃来与钱偶坐，其妻冠帻束带，往来于左右，詈曰：“汝是何人，预我家事”久之，孔都不与语。俄而独曰：“莫须着去否”孔因谓曰：“汝本何人辄凭人之室家可乎”乃曰：“我尝被一命而死，亦曾举进士，颇探释老书。昨到京师，无处寓止，暂凭附于此人。”孔曰：“既若曾涉猎三教，是识理之人也。汝在世仕宦之日，汝之室肯令他入凭之乎”鬼默然。又谓曰：“汝既言曾探释老，有尔许大虚空，何所不容而言无寓止之所。”言讫，钱妻瞢然而倒，半日乃寤，询其前事，皆不知也。

    Explanation

    34

    During the reign of Emperor Shenzong of Song, there was a man named Qian Zailang who was assigned to the Ministry of Personnel and brought his wife to live in the capital. One day, his wife wore his clothes and cap, spoke like a man, and appeared as if suffering from a mental illness. They summoned exorcists to examine her, but none of their methods worked. They heard that Kong Jiancheng, an official with the title of Jiancheng, had the ability to cure people's suffering. They went to his residence and told him about their wife's condition. Kong agreed to come and help. The next day, he arrived and sat with Qian. Qian's wife, wearing a hat and a sash, walked back and forth, cursing and saying, "Who are you? Why are you interfering in our family affairs?" Kong remained silent. After a while, he said, "Should we let you go?" Kong then asked, "Who are you originally, and why did you possess someone's household?" The spirit replied, "I once held an official position and died, and I also passed the imperial examination. I have studied Buddhist and Taoist texts. Yesterday, I arrived in the capital and had nowhere to stay, so I temporarily attached myself to this person." Kong said, "If you have studied the three teachings, you are a person of knowledge and reason. When you were alive and served as an official, would your wife allow someone else to possess her?" The spirit remained silent. Kong then said, "Since you claim to have studied Buddhism and Taoism, there is so much space in the vast universe. Why do you say you have nowhere to stay?" After he finished speaking, Qian's wife fainted and remained unconscious for half a day before regaining consciousness. When they asked her about the previous events, she did not remember anything.

    35

    ○邢文济
    　　华阴县云台观道士邢文济，常掌华阴道司事，故得紫其服，号虚寂大师。既免道职，专主金天南祠，乡人岁时献施金帛甚伙，邢悉裒为私藏，间充酒色之费。有巡检某人者知其事，密令人喻旨，邢屡以所得赂之。一夕，邢梦人摄至金天殿下，见巡检亦在廷中，有若胥吏者诘二人以盗用神物，皆服罪，各鞭背十二遣归。邢既寤觉，背间楚痛，遂诣巡检，话昨日之梦，惊曰：“我梦亦然。”月余刑病背疮死，巡检者亦患疽相继而殂。

    Explanation

    35

    邢 Wenji, a Taoist priest at YunTai Temple in Huayin County, often managed the Taoist affairs of Huayin, thus earning the right to wear purple robes and being styled as Master Xuyi. After being relieved of his Taoist duties, he became the chief priest at the southern shrine of Jintian Temple. Villagers offered a lot of gold and silk during festivals, which Xing collected all for his private hoard and sometimes spent on wine and women. There was a certain patrol officer who knew about his deeds and secretly instructed someone to convey his orders. Xing often bribed him with what he had obtained. One night, Xing dreamed that he was taken to the foot of the Jintian Temple, where he saw the patrol officer also in the courtyard. A person like a scribe questioned them about stealing sacred objects, and both confessed to their crimes, each being whipped twelve times and sent back. Xing woke up after the dream and felt his back aching painfully. He then went to see the patrol officer and told him about the dream from yesterday, who exclaimed in surprise, "I had the same dream." A month later, Xing died from a back ulcer, and the patrol officer also suffered from a boil and died soon after.

    36

    ○蒿店巡检
    　　渭州蒿店有巡检廨宇，率命班行领卒数百戍焉，庆历中，羌人入冠，巡检张殿直者应援于外，其家悉为番贼所俘虏。既入贼境，骨肉皆为赏口，其妻分隶一番酋，俾主汲炀之役，每荷汲器至水次，必南望，大恸而后归其家。一犬亦攘掠而得者，常随妻出入，屡衔其衣，呦呦而吠，摇尾前行十数步，回顾又鸣，如此者半岁。妻因泣谓犬曰：“汝能导我归汉耶”犬即跃鸣，妻乃计曰：“住此而生不若逃而死，万一或得达汉。”计遂决。俟夜，随犬南驰，天将晓，犬必择草木岑蔚之处，令妻ㄣ伏，犬即登高阜顾望，意若探候者，时捕雉兔衔致妻前，得以充饥，凡旬日达汉境。巡逻者以闻，访其夫尚在，乃好合如故。自此朝暮所食必分三器，一以饲犬。斯事番人具知之。
    　　评曰：犬，六畜也，惟豢养之恋。既陷夷狄之域，尚由思汉，又能导俘虏之妇，问关而归，可谓兽貌而人心也。有被衣冠而叛父母之国者，斯犬之罪人也。

    Explanation

    36

    ○Hao Town Patrol Officer
    　　In Hao Town, Weizhou, there was a patrol office where the patrol officer was ordered to lead hundreds of soldiers to guard the area. During the Qingli period, the Qiang people invaded, and the patrol officer Zhang Dianzhi responded to the call for aid from the outside. His entire family was captured by the Qiang invaders. Once they entered the enemy territory, his family members were all taken as captives. His wife was assigned to a Qiang chieftain and tasked with fetching water and heating tasks. Every time she carried her water vessel to the water source, she would look southward, weep bitterly, and then return home. A dog that was also taken as a captive often accompanied her, frequently biting her clothes and barking softly, wagging its tail as it walked ahead for several dozen steps before turning back and barking again. This happened for half a year. The wife wept and said to the dog, "Can you guide me back to the Han lands?" The dog immediately barked and leaped. The wife then thought, "Living here is worse than dying in escape; perhaps I might reach the Han lands." She decided to escape. At night, she followed the dog southward, and as dawn approached, the dog would choose a place with dense vegetation, instructing her to hide. The dog would then climb a high hill to look around, as if scouting, and sometimes catch pheasants or rabbits, bringing them to her to eat. After ten days, they reached the Han territory. The patrol officers reported this, and upon finding that her husband was still alive, they reunited as before. From then on, the food they ate every day was divided into three portions, one for the dog. This story was well-known among the Qiang people.
    　　Comment: A dog is one of the six domestic animals, yet it shows such loyalty and affection. Even when trapped in the barbarian lands, it still longs for the Han, and it was able to guide a captive woman through checkpoints and back home. It can truly be said to have the appearance of an animal but the heart of a human. There are those who, despite wearing the clothes of civilization, betray their homeland—these are the true criminals compared to this dog.

    37

    ○王廷评
    　　王廷评俊民，莱州人，嘉六年进士状头，登第释褐廷尉评，签书徐州节度判官。明年充南京考试官，未试间，忽谓监试官曰：“门外举人喧噪诟我，何为不约束”令人视之，无有也，如是者三四。少时又曰：“有人持檄逮我。”色若恐惧，乃取案上小刀自刺，左右救之，不甚伤。即归本任医治，逾旬创愈，但精神恍惚，如失心者。家人闻嵩山道士梁宗朴善制鬼，迎至，乃符召为厉者，梦一女子至，自言为王所害，已诉于天，俾我取偿，俟与签判同去尔。道士知术无所施，遂去，旬余，王亦卒。或闻王未第时，家有井灶，婢蠢戾不顺，使令积怒，乘间排坠井中。又云：王向在乡与一娼妓切密，私约俟登第娶焉，既登第为状元，遂就媾他族，妓闻之，忿恚自杀。故为女厉所困，夭阏而终。

    Explanation

    37

    Wang Tingping Junmin, a native of Laizhou, was the top-ranked candidate in the imperial examinations of the sixth year of Jia You (1061 AD). He was appointed as a Tingping and signed as the deputy judge of the Jiedu of Xuzhou. The following year, he was appointed as the examiner in Nanjing. Before the exam, he suddenly told the supervising official, "People outside are shouting and insulting me, why aren't you restraining them?" When someone checked, there was no one. This happened several times. After a short while, he said, "Someone is holding a warrant to arrest me." His face looked fearful, and he took a small knife from the desk and stabbed himself. The people around him tried to save him, but he was not seriously injured. He returned to his post for medical treatment and recovered after ten days. However, his mind was confused, as if he had lost his sanity. The family heard that the Taoist priest Liang Zongpu from Mount Song was skilled in exorcism, so they brought him. The priest summoned the ghost, and in a dream, a woman appeared and said, "I was wronged by Wang, and I have already appealed to heaven. I am here to seek retribution, and I will accompany the signatory judge to his death." The Taoist priest realized that his methods were ineffective, so he left. Ten days later, Wang died. Some say that before passing the exams, Wang had a servant who was stupid, rebellious, and disobedient. Wang, filled with anger, took advantage of an opportunity to push her into a well. Others say that Wang, while serving as a local official in his hometown, had a close relationship with a courtesan. They privately agreed that he would marry her after passing the exams. However, after becoming the top-ranked candidate, he married another family. The courtesan, upon hearing this, committed suicide out of anger and resentment. Therefore, he was troubled by a ghost and died prematurely.

    38

    ○樊预
    　　樊预，眉州人，登进士第，为杭州观察推官，素有异相，胸生四乳。一日，忽题于厅之堂扉云：三声鼓角云中见，一簇楼台海上高。人莫喻其旨。后数日，若有牙兵数百人来云：“吴山大王遣以奉迎。”预乞延数日，处置家事，迓者乃去。亟召同僚具以事告，且诉乡里辽远期津遣孥累之意，同官见其无疾而遽有是语，以为病狂，或讯其事之委曲，终不答。又信宿乃卒，卒时正严鼓时也。吴山即子胥之祠，据州中之高阜，有楼殿亭宇之胜，鼓角楼台之句，乃自谶也。后州民闻甲马巡徼之声，或见樊总督者，州人遂塑其像于神侧，自是不复见。

    Explanation

    38

    Fan Yu, a man from Meizhou, passed the imperial examination and became a jinshi, serving as an observatory magistrate in Hangzhou. He had an unusual appearance, with four nipples on his chest. One day, he suddenly inscribed a poem on the door of the hall: "Three sounds of drums and horns seen in the clouds, a cluster of towers high above the sea." No one understood the meaning of the poem. A few days later, as if hundreds of soldiers came and said, "The Lord of Wu Mountain sends us to welcome you." Fan requested an extension of a few days to settle his family affairs, and the welcoming ones then left. He urgently called his colleagues to inform them of the matter, explaining his intention to arrange for the transportation of his family, who were far away. His colleagues, seeing that he was not ill but suddenly spoke in this manner, thought he had gone mad. Some questioned the details of the matter, but he never answered. After a few more days, he died, and at the time of his death, the drums were sounding. Wu Mountain is the shrine of Wu Zixu, located on a high hill in the state, with beautiful pavilions and towers. The lines about drums, horns, and towers were a self-fulfilling prophecy. Afterward, the people of the state heard the sound of armored horses patrolling, and some saw a general named Fan. The people of the state then carved his image beside the deity, and since then, he was never seen again.

    39

    ●卷四
    　　○陈省副
    　　庆历初，陈吏部洎自三司副使谪守钟离郡，比曹员外钱愚时为通ヘ。钱善数术，一日，俾其邑封具酒肴，悉召陈宅之长幼会于ヘ居。明日，钱诣陈谢曰：“昨日以菲薄奉邀贵眷者，聊示区区之意，以托后事尔。”陈大惊曰：“足下四体甚安，此言何谓也”钱曰：“明年正月某日，某当死，乞护送诸孤归京师故栖，则幸甚。”陈知钱善数术，亦不以为然。愚尝谓其妻子曰：“陈亦行尸耳，过明年复旧官，则不可矣。”明年正月，如期而卒。月余，陈徙庐州，未半岁，复召为三司副使，数月病背疽而死。越三日，陈有少女奴年十二三，忽据榻附而降语曰：“吾昨日已见王，将设酒，我辞以创痛而止。

    Explanation

    39

    ●Volume 4
    ○Chen Shengfu
    In the early years of the Xining era, Chen Liubu Ji, who had been demoted from his position as Deputy of the Three Departments, was appointed to govern Zhongli County. At the same time, Cao Yuanwai and Qian Yu were serving as Tonghe (a high-ranking official). Qian Yu was skilled in divination and numerology. One day, he instructed a local official to prepare wine and food, and he invited all the members of Chen Liubu Ji's family to a gathering at his residence. The next day, Qian Yu visited Chen Liubu Ji to thank him, saying, "Yesterday, I invited your respected family with simple offerings, just to express my humble intentions and to entrust you with my future matters." Chen Liubu Ji was greatly surprised and asked, "You are in very good health, what do you mean by this?" Qian Yu replied, "On a certain day in the first month of next year, I will die. I ask you to take care of my children and send them back to their old home in the capital." Chen Liubu Ji knew that Qian Yu was skilled in divination, but he did not believe him. Qian Yu once told his wife and children, "Chen is just a walking corpse; if he returns to his old position next year, it will be impossible." As predicted, Qian Yu died on the appointed day. A month later, Chen Liubu Ji was transferred to govern Luzhou. Less than half a year later, he was summoned back to serve as the Deputy of the Three Departments. A few months later, he died from a boil on his back. Three days after his death, a young female servant of Chen Liubu Ji, aged twelve or thirteen, suddenly sat on the bed, leaned over, and began to speak, saying, "I saw the king yesterday, and he was about to set up a feast. I declined because of my pain and stopped."
