    门外从者五十人，悉戴漆皮弁，衣皂绿绯宽衫，乌毡靴，亦无异人世，不复号慕以自苦也。”又数日，复降语，命设榻如宾主位，曰：“此前濠州同官钱比部也。吾今得知益州，复与比部同官，前日已尝宴会，相得之欢，不异平昔，可令院子传语钱家县君，言比部教善视十一郎。今再与陈吏部同事，甚乐，勿思念悲恸也。”先是二日，钱之幼女方十余岁，睡中哀号，呼之良久，乃寤，曰：“我见比部与陈吏部在一高堂上宴会，樽俎莫，无不华丽，左右侍卫甚盛，因念父已去世，不觉啼泣，被呼方省。”与陈宅女奴降语相符。昔之小说载幽冥事者多云：人间郡县，阴府悉同。若陈吏部之为益州，岂其然乎比部之子闲今为供备库副使，言之甚详。

    Explanation

    40

    Outside the door, there were fifty attendants, all wearing lacquered leather hats, dressed in broad-sleeved robes of black, green, and red, and black woolen boots, showing no difference from the world of humans, and no longer wailing and mourning to suffer themselves. After several days, a spirit descended and spoke, ordering a couch to be set up as if in the position of host and guest, saying: "This was my colleague Qian, the Director of the Department of Accounting in Huai Prefecture. I now govern Yizhou, and I will once again work with Qian, the Director of the Department of Accounting, as we did before. We had a feast together, and the joy we shared was no different from what it was in the past. Please instruct the servant to convey a message to Lady Qian, saying that Qian should kindly look after Eleven. Now, I will again work with Director Chen, and it is very enjoyable. Do not think of me with grief and sorrow." Two days prior, Qian's young daughter, who was just over ten years old, cried out in her sleep, calling out for a long time before waking up and saying: "I saw Qian, the Director of the Department of Accounting, and Chen, the Director of the Department of Personnel, feasting in a high hall. The wine and food vessels were all splendid, and the guards around were numerous. Because I thought of my father who had passed away, I could not help but cry. I was called and then realized it was a dream." The account given by the female servant from Chen's household matched this. In the past, novels that recorded matters of the underworld often said that the prefectures and counties on earth were all the same in the underworld. If Chen, the Director of the Department of Personnel, were to govern Yizhou, could it be like that? Qian's son, Xian, who is now the Deputy Director of the Supply Department, spoke of it in great detail.

    ○ Wang Dazhi
    　　When Wang Zhi, a nobleman from the state of Jin and an attendant at the Tianzhang Pavilion, was exiled to govern Haiting, there was a shooting pavilion in the western part of the governor's residence, and in front of the pavilion, there was a garden with vegetables. One morning, as he woke up, the gardener who was tending to the garden saw an old woman standing in the shooting pavilion. Her appearance was very relaxed. The gardener was surprised and asked her, "You should quickly tell the military officer that I am here." The old woman replied, "I am the mother of the military officer. You should just tell him, and don't ask too many questions." The gardener went inside to inform the military officer, who rushed out immediately. Upon seeing the old woman, he recognized her appearance, demeanor, and voice as those of his mother, and her words were filled with sorrow. The military officer wept bitterly, and all his family members came to pay their respects. The old woman quickly said, "Cover the pavilion with a curtain so that no one can see from the outside."

    42

    ”既而询其所从来，母曰：“冥中有一事，应未受生与见伏牢者皆给假五日，我独汝念，是以来耳。”监军遽谒告且白平晋公，平晋公朝服往拜，而以常所疑鬼神事质之，皆不对，曰：“幽冥事泄，其罚甚重，无以应公命。”平晋又问：“世传有阎罗王者，果有否复谁尸之”曰：“固有，然为之者亦近世之大臣也。”请其名氏，则曰：“不敢宣于口。”公乃遍索家藏自建隆以来宰辅画像以示之，其间独指寇莱公曰：“斯人是也。”复问冥间所尚与所恶事，答曰：“人有不戕害物性者，冥间崇之，而阴谋杀人，其责最重。”如是留五日遂去。或云平晋由此不复肉食。平晋尝为之记。

    42

    Soon after inquiring about her origin, the woman said, "In the underworld, there is an event where those yet to be born and those in prison are all granted five days off. I came only because of my concern for you." The military commander hurriedly sought permission to leave and reported to Duke Ping of Jin. Duke Ping of Jin went in official attire to pay respects and asked about the usual doubts regarding ghosts and spirits, but she did not respond, saying, "The secrets of the underworld are revealed, and the punishment is very severe; I dare not speak aloud." Duke Ping of Jin then asked, "It is said that there is a King of Hell, is there such a being, and who serves him?" She replied, "There certainly is, but those who serve him are also recent high officials." When asked for their names, she said, "I dare not speak them aloud." Duke Ping of Jin then searched through the family collection of portraits of chancellors since the Jianlong era and showed them to her. She pointed to Kou Zhun's portrait and said, "This is the person." He asked again about the values and taboos in the underworld, and she replied, "Those who do not harm the nature of living beings are revered in the underworld, while secretly plotting to kill someone carries the heaviest blame." After this, she stayed for five days and then left. It is said that Duke Ping of Jin thus no longer ate meat. Duke Ping of Jin once wrote a record of it.

    ○石比部
    　　比部外郎石公弁言：皇中始得大理寺丞，监并州之徐沟镇。岁余，梦一鬼朱发青肤，自中溜下瞰，垂臂ㄏ一女，女子发自地而出，谓之曰：“送汝往李专知家作女。”石惊觉心悸，遂不寐，逮晓时，有酒税场官姓李者，石因问：“尔昨夕有何事”李曰：“四更初息妇生一女子。”石叹异久之。其后婴儿有疾，召一姥视之，曰本太原人，随夫寓此仅四十年。凡官于此者，无不出入其家。此廨宇亦曩日都监之官舍，今中溜之下者尝有井，李殿直监临，日鞭一女，使不胜楚痛，投井而死，遂废不汲，仍遭大水湮焉。石愈惊骇，方省前梦之验也。

    Explanation

    43

    Stonelord of the Department of Judicial Affairs, Shi Gong Bian, says: In the first year of the Huai period, he was appointed as a Censor of the Dali Temple and stationed at the Xugou Town of Bingzhou. After a year, he dreamed of a ghost with red hair and green skin, descending from the central part of the house, pulling a girl by the arm. The girl's hair emerged from the ground, and the ghost said to him, "I am taking you to the household of Li, the supervisor, to be a girl." Shi was startled awake, his heart pounding, and could not sleep until dawn. At that time, there was an official named Li who collected taxes on alcohol. Shi asked him, "What happened to you last night?" Li replied, "My wife gave birth to a daughter at the first watch of the night." Shi was amazed and pondered this for a long time. Later, when the baby fell ill, he called an elderly woman to examine her. The woman said she was originally from Taiyuan and had lived here with her husband for nearly forty years. All officials who had served here would come and go through her home. This official residence was once the office of a former supervisor. There was a well in the central part of the house, and Li, the deputy supervisor, would whip a girl daily until she could no longer bear the pain and threw herself into the well, dying. The well was then abandoned and no longer used, and was later submerged by a flood. Shi was even more terrified and finally realized the truth of his previous dream.

    ○曹郎中
    　　曹金部元举，治平中尝为福建路转运使，廨宇中有池亭，曹朝夕止于是，家人怪其肌体日瘠，精神恍惚，讯之，即曰：“尝有李家娘子甚美，与二婢子来待我。”咸谓物怪所惑，召医巫视之，悉无效，乃涸池求之，得三鳢，一大二小，曹遽呼曰：“勿害李家娘子。”遂脔而焚之，曹亦谢病归维阳，岁余卒。

    Explanation

    44

    Translation:

    The Langzhong Cao Jinbu Yuanju, during the Zhiping era, once served as the Chief Transport Officer of Fujian. In his official residence, there was a pond and a pavilion where Cao spent most of his time. His family noticed that he was gradually becoming emaciated and appeared mentally confused. When questioned, he replied, “There was a beautiful lady named Li who came to visit me, accompanied by two maids.” Everyone believed he was bewitched by spirits, so they called in doctors and sorcerers to examine him, but none of them were effective. They then drained the pond in search of the cause and caught three loaches, one large and two small. Cao suddenly called out, “Do not harm Lady Li!” They then cut the loaches up and burned them. Cao also feigned illness and returned to Wei Yang, where he died a year later.

    ○陆龙图
    　　龙图陆公诜尹成都日，府宅堂前东南隅有大枇杷一株，其下认则如数女子聚泣者，烛之则无所见，厥后半岁，陆卒于位。熙宁六年，成都间遇夜逻卒，闻哭声呦呦然，凡数十处，就视之则无有。至七年八年大旱，饿殍盈路，继之以疾疫，死者十六七，洎至秋麦则无人收刈，至于绫罗纱锦采笺诸物，鬻者亦少。宜乎魄兆之先见也。
    　　○宋中舍
    　　太子中舍宋传庆，谏议大夫太初之子，自言其父性嗜鳖，尝一日得数鳖，付厨婢霍之，其一甚大，婢不忍杀，放之沟中。逾年，婢病疫疾，苦心烦热，殆将卒，家人舁致外舍，俾卧以俟终，翌日视之，则自户阃至婢胸胁间，皆青泥涂渍，婢亦稍闲。讯之，则云：“不究其泥之来，但烦热减差耳。”家人伺之，逮夜有一大鳖自沟中被体以泥，直登婢胸冰之。婢逾旬遂愈，询其致鳖之自，婢乃述其本末。天圣中，传庆为遂宁通守，与先君言如此。

    Final Translation

    陆龙图
    When Lu Longtu, the governor of Chengdu, was in office, there was a large loquat tree in the southeast corner of the main hall in the government office. If one looked closely, it appeared as several women gathered and weeping. When one looked more closely, nothing was seen. Half a year later, Lu died in office.

    宋中舍
    The junior official of the Office of the Crown Prince, Song Chuangqing, the son of Counselor-in-Chief Song Taiqiu, said that his father had a strong liking for soft-shelled turtles. Once, he caught several turtles and gave them to a kitchen maid to cook. One of them was particularly large, and the maid could not bring herself to kill it, so she released it into a ditch. A year later, the maid fell ill with a fever, and her condition worsened to the point of death. Her family carried her to an outer room to lie down and wait for her to die. The next day, they found that the area from the door to her chest was covered in green mud, and the maid began to feel better. When questioned, she said, "I don't know where the mud came from, but my fever has subsided." The family watched and saw that at night, a large turtle emerged from the ditch, covered in mud, and climbed onto the maid's chest to cool her. After ten days, the maid recovered. The maid then recounted the entire story. During the Tian圣 period, Song Chuangqing was the governor of Suining, and he told me this story.

    文思副使马公仲方，尚书亮之侄也，遇罢官，多寓家高邮军。细君之妹亦居是邑，尝以牝羊馈于公，未几生一羔，秣饲数月，闲居患无人牧放，乃鬻于屠肆。翌日，临格将烹之，出刀于侧，且瀹水以备Ь濯，将而亡其刀，良久见其靶于沟中，取而洗拭置于床，旋又失之，乃羊所生羔衔而投诸沟，又以足践淖，使勿见。屠者视之大感伤，后以羊归马氏，自此不复屠羊，公亦以羊施佛寺。公尝守全州，尝自书斯事于阅理堂之壁云。
    　　○陈太博
    　　太常博士陈公舜俞在明州观察推官，有二子，一男一女，皆六七岁。一日戏嬉于外，逮归，则男子面有墨规其左颊，女子朱规其右颊。家人怪问其所规之自，则云不知，家人但谓小儿戏而为之，命涤去，翌日复然，如是几月余，日日如是，而无他怪。陈虑为怪之渐也，白转运使求莅他局，遂沿牒于浙西。廨既空，郡给二皂以守舍，一日，二人相与言曰：“陈察推向以二儿面有画以为怪，而竟无他，我等当验之。

    Explanation

    46

    Deputy Minister of Literature and Thought Ma Gong Zhongfang, nephew of Secretary of the Ministry of Rites Liang, often stayed in his family home in Gaoyou Commandery when he was dismissed from office. His wife's younger sister also lived in this town and once gave a female sheep as a gift to him. Not long after, a lamb was born, and they fed and cared for it for several months. Worried about no one to herd and graze it, he sold it to a butcher's shop. The next day, on the chopping block, it was about to be cooked. He took out a knife on the side and boiled water to prepare for cleaning. Just as he was about to cut, he lost his knife. After a long time, he saw the handle of the knife in the ditch. He picked it up, washed and wiped it, and placed it on the bed. Soon after, he lost it again. It was the lamb that had picked it up and thrown it into the ditch, and then stepped in the mud to hide it. The butcher, seeing this, was deeply moved. Later, he returned the sheep to the Ma family. From then on, he no longer slaughtered sheep. The official also gave the sheep to a Buddhist temple. The official once served as the governor of Quanzhou and once wrote this story on the wall of the Yueli Hall.

    ○ Chen Taibo

    Doctor of the Imperial Academy Chen Gong Shunyu served as an Inspector's Assistant Judge in Mingzhou. He had two children, one boy and one girl, both around six or seven years old. One day, they played outside. When they returned, the boy had a black circle on his left cheek, and the girl had a red circle on her right cheek. The family was puzzled and asked where the circles came from. They said they didn't know. The family thought it was just the children playing and ordered them to wash it off. The next day, it happened again. Like this for several more months, every day like this, but there were no other strange occurrences. Chen feared that this was the beginning of something strange. He reported to the Transport Commissioner and requested to be transferred to another office. He then followed his official documents to Zhe West. The office was empty, and the county gave two servants to guard the house. One day, the two servants talked to each other. "Chen Inspector thought that the two children's faces being drawn was strange, but there was nothing else. We should investigate this," they said.

    47

    有能独入堂中自朝至暮者，醵钱若干以赏之。”一皂欣然携短剑入堂之西序，醉卧牖下，及醒日已过午，吏喜其无怪，又喜将获所赏也，徘徊伺晚而出。俄然堂扉启，有数婢从一妇人，臂鹦鹉，立堂之，若所规画然。吏熟视，默念曰：“苟怪止如是，亦何足畏”方将以刃劫之，忽心动若大悸，不知其身之所有，惊呼携剑突门以走，犯谯门，穿长街，若发狂失心者。市人睹其持剑以为有变，皆恐避之，未半里蹶踣道左，众掖起，夺剑而诘之，移刻始能言，竟不知其何怪也。”

    Explanation

    47

    There was a challenge set forth: "Anyone who can enter alone into the hall from morning till evening shall have a sum of money raised to reward them." One official, eager to accept the challenge, carried a short sword and entered the western side of the hall. He fell asleep drunk under the window. When he woke up, it was already past noon. The official was pleased that there was no strange occurrence and also pleased that he would receive the reward. He lingered and waited until evening to leave. Suddenly, the hall door opened, and several maidservants accompanied a woman, carrying a parrot, as if everything had been planned. The official looked closely and silently thought to himself, "If the strange occurrence is only this, then it is not worth fearing." Just as he was about to use the sword to confront them, he suddenly felt his heart stir as if with great fear, and he did not know what was happening to his body. He shouted in alarm, grabbed his sword, and rushed out through the door, running through the city gate and down the long street, as if he had gone mad and lost his mind. The townspeople saw him with a sword and thought there was an emergency, so they all fled in fear. He fell and tumbled to the side of the road before reaching halfway. The crowd helped him up, took his sword, and questioned him. After a while, he could speak, but he still did not know what strange thing had happened.

    48

    ○马仲载
    　　熙宁六年，开江南为郡县，既得峡州，筑为安江城，命内殿承制马公仲载统卒三百戍焉，时石鉴以兵马钤辖知辰州，总千兵亦驻城中。一夕，逻卒云：“蛮兵数千，夜当攻城。”石闻之，即欲遁去，马曰：“钤辖倘出，则谁与守”遂仗剑于门，令曰：“敢出者斩。”石遂留，蛮兵亦不至，由此石颇衔之。未数月，马忽仆地，懵然无所知，仆从乃舁辰州就医药，石乃劾其弃城戍，将以军令裁之。马病稍间，就鞠于武陵，乃具馔，遥诉司南岳。

    Explanation

    48

    In the sixth year of Xining (1073), the Song Dynasty expanded its territory in southern China by establishing new administrative divisions. After acquiring the region of Xiangzhou, they built a city named Anjiang and appointed Ma Zhongzai, a high-ranking official, to lead three hundred soldiers to garrison the city. At the time, Shi Jian, a military commander and governor of Chenzhou, also had a thousand soldiers stationed in the city. One night, a patrol soldier reported that several thousand barbarian troops were planning to attack the city at night. Upon hearing this, Shi Jian immediately wanted to flee. Ma Zhongzai responded, "If the commander leaves, who will defend the city?" He then stood guard at the gate with a sword, issuing a command that anyone who left would be executed. Shi Jian stayed, and the barbarian troops did not come. As a result, Shi Jian harbored resentment towards Ma Zhongzai. Not long after, Ma Zhongzai suddenly fell ill and became unconscious. His attendants carried him to Chenzhou for medical treatment. Shi Jian then accused Ma Zhongzai of abandoning his post and intended to punish him according to military law. Ma Zhongzai's illness improved, and he was summoned for questioning in Wuling. He prepared food and remotely reported to the Southern Yue region.

    49

    翌日，有稚子方十岁，未尝读书，忽睡中呼索纸笔，乃书曰：“南岳门下牒敕马仲载：念卿遥祭之专勤，听其诉声之怨切，据卿之罪，理当丧命，上天愍卿常行吉心，能守所职，止命降灾夺官，更宜省循，以邀福寿。懋哉幸矣！熙宁六年十一月二十四日。”复取朱笔，画一印于日月上，篆文亦不可辨。儿复睡，少选而寤，诘之，云：“有一人青巾黄衫，以黄敕付我。”亦不知其手自摹写也。仲载之事，武陵人无不知者，南岳敕好事者多录而藏之。

    Explanation

    49

    The next day, a young child of ten years old, who had never read books, suddenly called for paper and brush while asleep and wrote: "Decree from the Southern Mountain's disciples to Ma Zhongzai: Thinking of your dedicated and diligent remote sacrifices, hearing your grievance with deep sorrow, according to your crime, it is reasonable to lose your life, but Heaven pities you for always having good intentions and being able to fulfill your duties, so only orders a disaster to befall and the position to be taken away. You should reflect and follow the path, to invite blessings and longevity. Greatly fortunate indeed! Xining sixth year, November twenty-fourth day." Then he took red ink and drew a seal on the sun and moon, the seal script also being indistinguishable. The child fell asleep again and woke up shortly, and when questioned, he said, "There was a person with a blue cap and yellow robe, who gave me a yellow decree." He also did not know if it was written by his hand. The matter of Zhongzai, people of Wuling all know, and those interested in the Southern Mountain's decree often record and keep it.

    50

    ○夏著作
    　　尚书郎高公靖，蔡州人，罢官归乡里村居，尝坐垄上视农事，有耕夫于土壤得铁牌，上有大字云：“司法参军夏钧。高亦不喻。数年授知道州，相次有长沙人夏钧，调本州司法参军，高方悟铁符之前定也。钧官至著作佐郎。
    　　○冀秘丞
    　　冀秘丞膺，皇中知河南府缑氏县，代人将至，预徙家于洛城，独止于县之正寝。一夕，梦二女子再拜于榻前，问其所以，云：“妾等是前邑尹家女奴也，以过被鞭死，瘗于明府寝榻之下。向来宅眷居此，不敢妄出，恐致惊怛，今夕方敢诚告，乞迁于野，乃幸之大也。”冀可之。明日发其地，果得二枯骨，红梳绣履尚在，命裹以衣絮，祭以酒饭，加之楮钱，埋于近郊。数夕后，梦中前谢而去。

    Explanation

    50

    Translation

    The Scholar of Summer

    A high-ranking official named Gao Gongjing, a native of Cai Prefecture, retired from office and returned to live in a village. He once sat on a ridge overseeing agricultural activities when a farmer found an iron plaque in the soil. The plaque bore large characters that read: "Judicial Officer Xia Jun." Gao did not understand the significance at the time. Several years later, he was appointed as the governor of Daozhou. Shortly after, a man from Changsha named Xia Jun was transferred to serve as the judicial officer of the same state. Only then did Gao realize that the iron plaque was predestined. Xia Jun eventually attained the title of Assistant Scholar.

    The Secretariat Officer Ji

    Ji Mi, a secretariat officer during the reign of Emperor Renzong, served as the governor of Gou County in Henan Prefecture. When his successor was about to arrive, he moved his family to Luoyang in advance and stayed alone in the main hall of the county. One night, he dreamed of two women bowing twice before his bed. He asked them why they appeared, and they replied: "We are the female servants of the previous county magistrate's household. We were beaten to death for a mistake and buried beneath your bed. Previously, the family members who lived here dared not appear recklessly, fearing to cause alarm. Tonight, we dare to truly inform you. We ask to be moved to the countryside, which would be the greatest favor." Ji agreed. The next day, he excavated the site and indeed found two dried bones, along with red combs and embroidered shoes. He ordered them to be wrapped in clothing and cotton, offered wine and food as a sacrifice, added paper money, and buried them near the outskirts. Several nights later, in his dream, the women thanked him and left.

    51

    ○梁寺丞
    　　梁寺丞彦昌，相国之长子也，嘉中知汝之梁县，其内子尝梦一少年，黄衣、束带、纱帽，神彩俊爽，谓之曰：“君宜事我，不尔且致礻周。”既寤白梁，梁不之信。既而窃其衣冠簪珥，挂于竹木之杪，变怪万状，梁伺其啸，拔剑击之。鬼曰：“嘻！汝安能中我”又命道士设醮以禳之，始敕坛，夺道士剑，舞于空，无如之何。谓梁曰：“立庙祀我，我当福汝。”既困其扰，不得已立祠于廨舍之侧。又曰：“人不识吾面，可召画工来，我自教之绘事。”既毕，乃内子梦中所见者。会家人有疾，鬼投药与之服，辄愈归之；政事有不合于理者洎民间利害隐匿，亦密以告。梁解官，庙为后政所毁，鬼亦不灵。

    Explanation

    51

    梁寺丞

    梁寺丞彦昌是相国的长子，在嘉祐年间担任汝州梁县的县令。他的妻子曾梦见一个少年，身穿黄衣，束带，头戴纱帽，神采俊爽。少年对她说：“你应该侍奉我，否则我将带来灾难。”醒来后，她告诉了彦昌，彦昌并不相信。随后，少年偷走了他的衣冠簪珥，挂在竹木的枝梢上，变化出无数奇怪的形态。彦昌等待他发出呼啸声时，拔剑击打他。鬼说：“嘻！你怎么能打中我？”又让道士设醮来禳灾，道士开始主持仪式，鬼夺走了道士的剑，在空中舞动，彦昌无可奈何。鬼对彦昌说：“你建一座庙来祭祀我，我将保佑你。”被鬼的骚扰所困扰，彦昌不得已在官舍旁边建了一座祠堂。鬼又说：“人们不认识我的脸，可以叫画工来，我自己教他绘画。”画完后，正是彦昌妻子梦中所见的样子。每当家人有病，鬼会投药给他们服用，总是痊愈归功于鬼；对于政事不合情理或民间隐匿的利害关系，鬼也会秘密告知彦昌。彦昌卸任后，祠堂被后任官员毁坏，鬼也不再灵验了。

    52

    ○杨郎中
    　　郎中杨公异，性好洁静过甚，不近人情。寓居荆南，对门民家有子数岁，肤发悉白，俗谓社公儿，异恶焉，屡呼其父，与五缗令杀之，民得镪，潜徙去。杨止一子，俄病癞，肌溃而卒。近时有人死而复生，云：“阴府新立速报司，”若杨氏之报信哉。

    Explanation

    52

    The Medical Officer Yang
    Medical Officer Yang, whose surname was Yang and whose courtesy name was Yi, had a nature that loved cleanliness excessively, to the point of being unnatural. He was residing temporarily in Jingnan. In the house opposite, there was a child a few years old with white skin and hair, commonly called the child of the land god. Yang hated it and often called his father, giving him five strings of cash to kill it. The people got the money and secretly moved away. Yang had only one son, who soon fell ill with leprosy, his flesh rotted, and he died. Recently, someone died and came back to life, saying: "The underworld has newly established a quick retribution office." Is this the kind of retribution for the Yang family?

    53

    ○张太博
    　　治平三年，太常博士张知兖州奉符县，太山庙据县之中，令兼主庙事，岁三月，天下奉神者悉持奇器珍玩来献，公往往窃取之。既解官，寓家于东平，一夕，闻中阖外如数十人语，声杂乔不可辨，晨兴视之，其所盗莫器皿之类悉次第罗列于厅庑间，视橐箧封宛然，如是者凡数夜。张大怖骇，悉取燔之，越三日，奉符旧事发，兖州狱吏持檄来捕，既就捕，左验明白，竟置牢户。
    　　○杨从先
    　　殿直杨从先，至和初监大名马监，其冬梦授枢密院子，云：千里重行行，右札付从先，准此。既觉，不喻其旨。明年春大雪，牧马多死，监牧使臣冲替者数人，乃悟千里重字也，以配行，冲字也，再言之者，皆被责也。

    Explanation

    53

    Translation

    Zhang Taibo

    In the third year of the Zhiping era, Zhang, a Taiboshi (a high-ranking official) from the Taichang Bureau, served as the magistrate of Fufu County in Yanzhou. The Temple of Mount Tai was located in the center of the county, and the magistrate was also responsible for temple affairs. Every March, people from all over the country brought unusual and precious objects to the temple as offerings, and Zhang often stole these items. After resigning from his official post, he lived in Dongping. One night, he heard voices outside the inner gate, as if many people were speaking, with mixed and indistinct sounds. In the morning, he checked to see what had happened and found the stolen items, such as vessels and utensils, neatly arranged in the hall and corridors. The bags and boxes were still sealed as before, and this happened for several nights. Zhang was greatly frightened and burned all the items. Three days later, an old case in Fufu County came to light, and officials from Yanzhou came to arrest him. After being arrested, the evidence was clear, and he was ultimately imprisoned.

    Yang Congxian

    Yang Congxian, a palace attendant, was appointed to oversee the horse stables in Daming in the early years of the Zhihe era. That winter, he dreamed of being given a document by the Chumi Yuan (the Privy Council), which read: "Travel a thousand miles, go again." On the right, it was noted to be delivered to Yang, according to this. Upon waking, he did not understand the meaning. The following spring, there was a heavy snowfall, and many of the horses in the stables died. Several supervisors were replaced. He then realized that "thousand miles" referred to the distance, and "go again" meant to continue, and the word "冲" (chong) meant to replace. Those who were replaced were all held accountable.

    54

    ●卷五
    　　○李参政
    　　李参政至，性修洁夷淡，年几强壮，尚为布衣。开宝中，有省郎典齐安郡，至依门下为学，读书著文，夜分不寐。一夕，有二女子盛冠服，鸣，揖李而坐，容态殊丽，风度婉约，李恍不知其所从来，因定神肃容，熟视而问曰：“鬼邪仙邪”答曰：“奴非鬼也，乃仙之流亚也。”少时，出户不见。自此月三至，或饮之以酒，或啜茗而去，谈幽显之事，辞简而理明。守将受代，二女复来，谓李曰：“与君款奉三年于兹矣，见君居常以礼自持，未省一言及乱，器识洪厚，终当远到。然君前世曾为商贾，负人息钱甚夥，以贫不能偿，故今世俾君羁蹇于壮岁。”因出书一封与至，曰：“俟改元太平乃启，不尔当有祸。”既而太宗践祚，改元太平兴国，启其封，见“太平兴国二年，李至第二人及第”，既而果然。后历清显，入参大政，拥旄巨镇而终。

    Explanation

    54

    Chapter 5
    ○Li Zhen, the Censor-in-Chief

    Li Zhen, the Censor-in-Chief, was a man of pure and unworldly character, nearly reaching adulthood but still a commoner. During the Kai Bao era, there was a high-ranking official who governed the Qi'an prefecture. Li studied under this official, reading and writing until late at night. One evening, two women dressed in fine attire and adorned with jade pendants greeted Li and sat down. They were exceptionally beautiful and had a graceful demeanor. Li was momentarily bewildered by their sudden appearance, so he composed himself and asked, "Are you ghosts or immortals?" They replied, "We are not ghosts, but lesser immortals." After a while, they left through the door and were no longer seen. From then on, they visited once a month, sometimes offering him wine or tea, and they would discuss both earthly and otherworldly matters, speaking concisely but clearly. When the official was replaced by a new governor, the two women returned and said to Li, "We have been in close association with you for three years. We see that you always uphold propriety and never speak of disorder. Your intellect and character are broad and deep, and you will ultimately achieve great things. However, in your past life, you were a merchant who owed a lot of interest-bearing money and could not repay it due to poverty, which is why you are in a difficult situation in your prime years." They then gave him a letter and said, "Wait until the era name is changed to Taiping to open it; otherwise, there will be disaster." Later, when Emperor Taizong ascended the throne and the era name was changed to Taiping Xingguo, Li opened the letter and found it written, "In the second year of Taiping Xingguo, Li Zhen became the second-place winner in the imperial examination." Indeed, this came to pass. Afterward, Li held high-ranking positions, entered into major government roles, and held a significant military command until the end of his life.

    55

    ○梅侍读
    　　侍读梅公询，端拱二年第进士，清裕有才，早厕文馆，坐在人洎滞者数十年。景德中，尝梦与一士人，年甚少，共射一石牛，梅中胁，少年者中首。至祥符中，真宗东封，询被选于太平顶行事，宿斋其上。是夕，燔香再拜，默祈将来通塞之事，既寝，梦牛马羊布野，有二牛斗于前，一人被冠服，前谓牛曰：“伺吕公再入中书斗亦未晚。”牛遂解去。其后自尚书郎带职知濠州，吕申公以太常博士通守郡事，仪状酷似向梦中所见，又守ヘ之居花圃中，各有一小石牛，梅因省前梦，厚结于申公。宝元中吕公入相，擢梅为天章阁待制，其后申公自北都再持政柄，梅已为枢密直学士判审官院，又迁为侍读学士郡牧使。是岁十二月得疾，出守许州，以至捐馆。梦中所见牛马，乃郡牧使也；二牛斗者，其年岁值丑，十二月又丑也；二牛者，逢二丑而疾作也。神先告之矣。

    Explanation

    55

    Ma the Reader

    Ma Gong Xun, the Reader, passed the imperial examination in the second year of the Duan Gong era. He was clear, generous, and talented, and was appointed early in his career to a literary office. However, he was delayed or stuck in his career for several decades due to the influence of others. During the Jingde era, he once dreamed of shooting a stone ox with a young scholar, who was much younger than him. In the dream, Ma hit the ox's side, while the young scholar hit its head. By the time of the Xiangfu era, when Emperor Zhenzong conducted an eastern sacrifice, Ma was selected to perform duties at Tai Ping Peak and stayed there for the night. That evening, he burned incense and prayed silently for future success or obstacles. After falling asleep, he dreamed of a field filled with cows, horses, and sheep, and two oxen fighting in front of him. A man in formal attire approached the oxen and said, "It's not too late for Lu Gong to re-enter the Zhongshu Sheng (Chancellery) and fight." The oxen then stopped fighting. Later, Ma was appointed as the governor of Haozhou while holding the rank of Shangshu Lang. Lu Shen Gong, serving as the deputy governor of the same region, had an appearance that closely resembled the man in Ma's dream. Both lived in a garden with a small stone ox. Ma remembered his dream and formed a close relationship with Lu. When Lu became a chancellor during the Bao Yuan era, Ma was promoted to the position of Tian Zhang Ge Dai Zhi. Later, when Lu returned to power after being away from the capital, Ma was already appointed as the head of the Shenyuan Office while holding the rank of Shu Mi Zhi Xue Shi. He was further promoted to the position of Shi Du Xue Shi Jun Mu Shi. In December of that year, Ma fell ill and was sent to Xu Zhou, where he eventually passed away. The cows and horses in the dream were symbolic of his new position. The two oxen fighting represented the Year of the Ox, and the fact that it was December, another Year of the Ox, symbolized that his illness occurred in the Year of the Ox. The dream was a divine warning.

    56

    评曰：君子居易以俟命。语曰：“富而可求也，虽执鞭之士吾亦为之。明富贵贫贱以时而来，不可规图而取。梅公早预俊选，屯蹇不振，年始从欲，方遇知己，官历两省，职居禁近，拥旄巨镇，克享遐龄。始否终泰，岂非命耶
    　　○韩宗绪
    　　韩宗绪龙图贽之子，以父任补将作监主簿，皇秋镇厅预荐，偶于相国寺资圣阁前见其家旧使老仆，呼谓曰；“若非某乙乎死久矣，何得在此”曰：“某今从送春榜使者。”又问：“榜可见乎”曰：“有司收掌甚密，不可得而见也。”又谓曰：“汝能密询有我姓名乎苟无，亦可料理否”仆许诺试为尽力，又问：“复于何处为约”仆云：“复期于此，他处难庇某之迹，此地杂沓，人鬼可得参处。”他日如期而往，仆果在焉，遂开掌，见己之名在片纸上，揭其下，乃田宝邻也。仆曰：“此人明年当登第，官甚卑。郎君亦自有科名，但差晚耳。况身已有官，故得而易之，若白身则不可。”因忽不见。

    Explanation

    56

    Commentary:
    A gentleman remains at ease while awaiting his destiny. It is said, "If wealth can be obtained, even a lowly position like holding a whip would be acceptable to me." This reflects the understanding that wealth, nobility, poverty, and lowliness come at their appointed times and cannot be sought or obtained through scheming. Mei Gong was early in his career, facing adversity and stagnation. He began to encounter his destiny at the age of forty, meeting a patron who recognized his talent. He served in two high offices, held positions close to the emperor, and was appointed as a governor of a major region. He lived to an advanced age, experiencing adversity in his early years and prosperity in his later years. Is this not fate?

    ○ Han Zongxu
    Han Zongxu, son of Han Zongzhi, was appointed as a clerk in the Office of Works due to his father's position. During the autumn of the Xuanhe era, he was recommended for a position. He happened to meet an old servant of his family at the Zizheng Pavilion in the Xiangguo Temple. The servant called out, "If it's not me, then how could you be here?" The servant replied, "I am now accompanying the messenger who delivers the spring examination results." Han Zongxu asked, "Can the list of successful candidates be seen?" The servant replied, "The officials keep it very closely guarded, so it cannot be seen." Han Zongxu then asked, "Can you discreetly inquire if my name is on the list? If not, can it be arranged?" The servant agreed and promised to try his best. Han Zongxu asked, "Where should we meet again?" The servant said, "We will meet here again; elsewhere it would be difficult to hide my presence. This place is crowded, and both humans and spirits can be found here." The next day, as agreed, Han Zongxu went to the same place, and the servant was indeed there. The servant then opened the palm of his hand, revealing a piece of paper with Han Zongxu's name on it. Below his name was the name of Tian Baolin. The servant said, "This person will pass the examination next year, but he will hold a very low position. Your name is also on the list, but it is a bit later. Since you already have an official position, it can be changed, but if you were a commoner, it would not be possible." After saying this, the servant suddenly disappeared.

    57

    明年韩登第，曾以兹事说于亲旧间。治平中，韩玉汝龙图与供备库使段继文同使契丹，至雄州，段尝为雄之监军，雄之举人皆上谒。田宝邻刺字厕焉。韩见之大惊，与段尽道所以，段复以韩事本末语之，曰遂齐戒夜醮，作奏诉于帝。木炎尝侍父官瓦桥，备知之。熙宁中，炎登第，为岳州巴陵簿，县令王泽尝谈怪异，王云：“应举时，闻州东有一人常入冥，言人吉凶甚验，遂率同人数辈就问之。其人在小邸暗室中，既见，遂以将来得失，叩之再三，不语，俄又面壁而坐，云：‘田宝邻公事至今未了，安敢有他科场事。’不知田宝邻何人也。”炎方省向者韩段之言。宝邻以累举特奏名其后，官甚卑。

    Explanation

    57

    The following year, Han passed the imperial examination and once told this story to his close relatives and old acquaintances. During the Zhiping era, Han Yuru, a high-ranking official, and Duan Jiwen, an envoy to the Khitan, were sent together to Xiongzhou. Duan had previously served as a military supervisor in Xiongzhou, and all the candidates in the prefecture came to pay their respects. Among them was Tian Baolin, who had tattoos. Han was greatly surprised upon seeing him and discussed the matter with Duan. Duan then recounted the entire story of Han's encounter, saying that they had fasted and purified themselves, performed a ritual offering at night, and submitted a memorial to the emperor. Mu Yan had served with his father at the Wabridge checkpoint and was fully aware of the events. During the Xining era, Yan passed the imperial examination and became a county magistrate in Balin County, Yue Prefecture. The county magistrate Wang Ze once spoke about strange occurrences, saying, "When I was preparing for the examination, I heard that there was a person in the eastern part of the prefecture who often entered the underworld and could accurately predict people's fortunes and misfortunes. So I led several companions to ask him. The person was in a small room in a dark house. After meeting him, we asked about our future gains and losses repeatedly, but he did not speak. Soon, he sat facing the wall and said, 'The affairs concerning Tian Baolin have not been resolved yet, how could I have any other matters related to the examination?' I did not know who Tian Baolin was." Yan then realized the connection to Han and Duan's words. Tian Baolin, after multiple attempts, was eventually given a special nomination but held a very low-ranking position.

    58

    ○南州壬子
    　　虞部员外郎杜公彬，罢滁ヘ，至阙奉朝请。一日游景德寺，访朝客不值，方假笔札以志门，偶狂僧严法华者自庑下直揖杜君。杜雅闻法华言事多中，因以平生未然之事谘之。僧夺笔索纸，杜以刺字之余授之，大书云：南州壬子。杜不测其旨。后数月，授知漳州，到州阅《图经》，则陈氏伪据日，目漳为南州，杜叹讶之。自揆以为壬子者有土之号，岂隐其为州之意邪后岁余，杜终于任，其子煜用浮屠法作七斋，饭僧次，煜因言及法华之事，取其书以示群僧，因观其壬字中一书差长，若壬子，遂以甲子推杜君卒之日，正壬子也。其子煜言之于魏泰并出其书。

    Explanation

    58

    The Southern State and the Year Renzi

    Du Gongbin, an official of the Yubu Yuanwailang rank, was dismissed from his position as the Administrator of Chu Prefecture and arrived in the capital to attend court. One day, he visited Jingde Temple to see a court official but failed to meet them. He then borrowed writing materials to inscribe something on the door. Suddenly, a mad monk named Yan Fahua approached him from the side and greeted him. Du Gongbin had heard that Yan Fahua's predictions were often accurate, so he consulted the monk about matters that had not yet happened. The monk seized the pen and asked for paper. Du Gongbin gave him the remaining writing materials, and the monk wrote "Nan Zhou Ren Zi" on the paper. Du Gongbin did not understand the monk's meaning.

    Several months later, Du Gongbin was appointed as the Administrator of Zhangzhou. Upon arriving in Zhangzhou, he read the geographical and historical record, which mentioned that Chen Shu regarded Zhangzhou as Southern State. Du Gongbin was surprised and amazed by this. He reflected upon himself and thought that "Nan Zhou Ren Zi" might be a title related to land, possibly hinting at the official being a state.

    Several years later, Du Gongbin died in office. His son, Yu, performed Buddhist rituals and fed the monks. During this occasion, he mentioned Yan Fahua's prediction and showed the writing to the monks. The monks noticed that the character "壬" in the writing was slightly longer, resembling "Nan Zhou Ren Zi." They deduced that Du Gongbin died on the day "Nan Zhou Ren Zi." Yu spoke about this to Wei Tai and also presented the writing to him.

    59

    ○李侍禁
    　　李侍禁齐善袁许之术，士大夫多喜之，有别业在华阴之东郊。其妻先卒，买一妾，生二子，一男一女，李既死，二子始髫龀。长男年二十余，乃嫡室所出，与其妻谋曰：“二子长立，当有婚嫁之费，且分我资产，能致之死地，家资悉我有也。”自此二子衣不得完，食不得饱，笞骂挫辱无日无之，俄得疾疫，遂绝其药膳，虽杯水亦不与，相继皆物故。妾不胜怨愤，日走伏齐垄号哭以诉，数月妾亦死。

    Explanation

    59

    Translation:

    Li, the Court Official

    Li, the court official, excelled in the techniques of Qi, Yan, and Xu, which were highly favored by the scholar-officials. He owned a secondary residence in the eastern suburbs of Huayin. After his wife's death, he took a concubine who bore him two children, a boy and a girl. Upon Li's death, the two children were just beginning to enter their early childhood years. The eldest son, in his twenties, was the legitimate offspring of the principal wife. He conspired with his wife, saying, "When the two children grow up, they will require expenses for marriage, and they will also divide my assets. If I can manage to have them killed, all the family wealth will be mine." From then on, the two children were poorly clothed and fed, and they were constantly subjected to beatings, cursing, and humiliation. Soon, they fell ill, and their medical care and food were cut off. Even a cup of water was denied to them. They died one after another. The concubine, overwhelmed with anger and grief, went to a specific location to cry and wail in complaint. After several months, she too died.

    60

    有邻家子于阒巷见齐手携二子，妾亦侍侧，顾谓邻家子曰：“我长男不孝不友，虐杀弟妹，又令此妾衔恨而殁，若可语之，吾亦诉于阴府不汝置也。”邻家子知是鬼，将走避，因忽不见，邻家子遽来告之，亦不之信。一旦，其妻具酒肴，会亲旧女客于中堂，厥良独坐书阁下，乃父自外至，数其罪，以杖击之。坐客闻其号呼，悉往视，但见仆地叩头服罪，言虐杀二子状，数日乃死，其妻后数月亦死，田宅家赀悉籍没。噫！李齐之事不诬矣。世之人父死而谋害幼稚，以图资贿者多矣，目睹数族，虽不若李为鬼灵，但见其身夭折，子孙沦胥，以至无立锥之地。李齐之事足使狠子庸妇闻之少警其心。

    Explanation

    60

    A neighbor's son saw Li Qi in a quiet alley, holding two children by the hand, with a concubine serving beside him. Turning to the neighbor's son, he said, "My eldest son is unfilial and unfriendly, cruelly killing his younger siblings, and also causing this concubine to die with a grudge. If you can tell others, I will also appeal to the underworld and not leave you alone." The neighbor's son knew it was a ghost and was about to flee, but suddenly disappeared. The neighbor's son quickly came to report it, but no one believed him. One day, Li Qi's wife prepared wine and food, hosting relatives and old friends in the main hall, while his wife sat alone in the study. His father came from outside, counted his crimes, and beat him with a stick. The guests heard his cries and all went to see. They only saw him fall to the ground, bowing and admitting his guilt, describing the cruelty in killing his two sons. He died after several days, and his wife died several months later. All his land, houses, and property were confiscated. Alas! The story of Li Qi is not false. In the world, there are many people who plot to harm the young and gain wealth and bribes after their father's death. Having seen several families, though not as ghostly as Li Qi, one sees their premature deaths, descendants perishing, and ending up with no place to stand. The story of Li Qi is enough to make cruel sons and foolish wives heed their hearts.

    61

    ○李氏婢
    　　贾国傅大冲尝说：有李某屡典郡，既卒，家人归京师借居，有老婢凡京城巷陌无不知者，家之贸易饮膳衣着洎亲家传导往来悉赖焉，邑君爱之如儿侄。明道春，方淘沟，俾至亲家通起居，抵幕不归，数日寻访无迹。邑君曰：“是媪苦风眩疾作，坠沟死矣。”即命诸婢设灵座祭焉，家之吉凶亦来报，邑君泣曰：“是媪虽死，不忘吾家。”明年春，自外来，家人皆以为鬼也。媪拜曰：“去岁令妾传语某人至某处，风眩作堕沟中，某人宅主姥见之令人拯出，涤去秽污，加以药饵，得不死。某誓佣一年以报，今既期，即辞归。”往询某氏果然。是夕有青巾男子见邑君梦，曰：“我清卫卒也，向死于巷左，昨闻宅上失女使，设位以祭，遂假其名窃享焉。今闻已归。”乃拜辞而去。

    Explanation

    61

    ○李氏婢
    　　贾国傅大冲尝说：有李某屡典郡，既卒，家人归京师借居，有老婢凡京城巷陌无不知者，家之贸易饮膳衣着洎亲家传导往来悉赖焉，邑君爱之如儿侄。明道春，方淘沟，俾至亲家通起居，抵幕不归，数日寻访无迹。邑君曰：“是媪苦风眩疾作，坠沟死矣。”即命诸婢设灵座祭焉，家之吉凶亦来报，邑君泣曰：“是媪虽死，不忘吾家。”明年春，自外来，家人皆以为鬼也。媪拜曰：“去岁令妾传语某人至某处，风眩作堕沟中，某人宅主姥见之令人拯出，涤去秽污，加以药饵，得不死。某誓佣一年以报，今既期，即辞归。”往询某氏果然。是夕有青巾男子见邑君梦，曰：“我清卫卒也，向死于巷左，昨闻宅上失女使，设位以祭，遂假其名窃享焉。今闻已归。”乃拜辞而去。

    Translation:

    ○Li's Servant Girl
    Jia Guo Fu Dachong once said: There was a Mr. Li who had served in several prefectures. After his death, his family returned to the capital and rented a place to live. They had an old servant girl who knew everything about the alleys and streets of the capital, and was responsible for all household trade, food preparation, clothing, and communication with relatives. The local lord loved her like a nephew or niece. In the spring of the Mingdao era, while they were cleaning a ditch, she was sent to the relatives to convey greetings. She did not return until evening, and after several days of searching, she could not be found. The local lord said, "This old woman suffered from a severe dizziness attack and fell into the ditch, where she died." He then ordered the other servants to set up an altar to worship her, and the family's good and bad fortunes came to him in dreams. The local lord wept and said, "This old woman, even though she died, did not forget our family." The following spring, she returned from outside, and the family all thought she was a ghost. The old woman bowed and said, "Last year, I was sent to deliver a message to someone at a certain place. I had a dizziness attack and fell into the ditch. The elderly lady of the house saw me and had someone rescue me, clean me, and give me medicine, so I did not die. I swore to serve for a year in return, and now that the time has come, I will depart." They went to verify with the certain family, and it was true. That night, a man with a blue cap appeared in the dream of the local lord and said, "I am a guard of the Qing dynasty, and I died in the alley to the left. Yesterday, I heard that the house lost a female servant and set up an altar to worship her, so I impersonated her and took part in the worship. Now I hear that she has returned." He then bowed and left.

    62

    ○李比部
    　　李比部从周，景四年随乡书来京师，与数同人僦舍于麻秸巷。尝五鼓而兴，将谒亲知于远坊者，始启寝户，即踣于地。奴仆扶视，气息殆绝，至巳午间，始惺然，曰：“初启关，见一鬼戴短巾，衣绿宽衫，黝面于囟，状若祠庙中所谓判官者，以气嘘之，如霜风之切骨，遂昏然，亦不知委顿于地也。”明年校艺不利于南宫。

    Explanation

    62

    Li Bi Bu

    Li Bi Bu, surnamed Li and named Zhou, came to the capital in the fourth year of Jingyou (1037) with letters from his hometown. He rented a room in Ma Jie Lane and lived there with several others. One morning, he got up at the fifth drumbeat and was about to visit friends in a distant district. As soon as he opened the door to his bedroom, he suddenly fell to the ground. His servants helped and looked after him, and his breath was nearly gone. By the time it was between the hours of巳 (9-11 AM) and午 (11 AM-1 PM), he regained consciousness. He said, "When I first opened the door, I saw a ghost wearing a short cap and a green loose robe, with a dark face at the fontanelle. It resembled the judge in a temple. The ghost breathed on me, and it felt like the cold wind cutting through my bones, so I became dazed and did not even realize I had fallen to the ground." The following year, when he took the examination, he was not favorable in the results at the South Palace.

    63

    ○胡殿丞
    　　胡殿丞偃，潭州人，至和中授峡州签判，待阙荆州，僦居于公安门内，暇则坐于厅所。间尝有持刀镊者比日过门，植足注视，良久乃去，胡异之。一日，呼与小儿剃发，因问曰：“汝常顾吾门内何也”曰：“有一亲识姓某在峡州为吏，兼管冥曹，事多而身劳，欲公垂庇，是以日踵门而不敢言。”胡未之信。及至任，聚群胥，出姓名问之，有一人前曰：“刀镊汉竟多口。”胡屡询以冥司所职，但云未可轻泄。居无何，胡以先人忌晨，饭僧课经，具疏焚楮泉。迨明日，其吏至案前，以手就怀探昨日所焚疏示，若新写者。已而灰灭，且曰：“殿丞见迫，不敢隐，然某已得罪，而殿丞亦不免减禄矣。”数日吏暴卒，期年，胡以病废于家。

    Explanation

    63

    Hú Diànchéng Yǎn, a person from Tánzhōu, was appointed as a signatory judge of Xiázhōu during the Zhìhé period. He waited for an appointment in Jīngzhōu and rented a residence inside Gōng'ān Gate. When he had leisure time, he would sit in the hall. Sometimes, there was a person with scissors who passed by the door every day, standing and staring for a long time before leaving. Hú was surprised by this. One day, he called the person and had his children get their hair cut, and then asked, "Why do you often look at my door?" The person replied, "There is a relative named someone who serves as an official in Xiázhōu, and he also manages the underworld department. He has many tasks and physical labor, and he wants your protection, so he comes to the door every day but dares not speak." Hú did not believe him. When he took office, he gathered a group of clerks and asked them about their names. One person stepped forward and said, "The scissors man is indeed talkative." Hú repeatedly asked about the duties of the underworld, but they only said it could not be easily disclosed. Not long after, Hú, because of the ancestor's忌晨, fed monks and recited scriptures, wrote a memorial, and burned paper money. The next day, the official came to the desk, with his hand in his chest, he took out the memorial burned yesterday and showed it, as if newly written. Then the ashes disappeared, and he said, "The signatory judge is being pressured, dare not hide, but I have already offended, and the signatory judge will also not avoid a reduction in salary." A few days later, the official died suddenly. A year later, Hú became ill and retired to his home.

    64

    ○谢判官
    　　谢判官，平原人，宝元中尝为曹州观察推官，视事未几，一夕梦老父引之入大第中，家颇豪盛，奶媪抱婴儿饰以文绣，指谓谢曰：“此君之后身也。”谢问：“此何郡复谁氏之家”老父曰：“成都府陈郎中宅也，赀产甚丰，君心乐乎”谢亦颔之。既寤，甚不怿，谓妻子曰：“吾其死矣。日处致后事。既而秩满，复调棣州判官，到官数月，又梦前老父复引至昔之第，有小儿衣纨绮戏阶下，指谓谢曰：“此前日之婴儿也，今始五岁，尚未语。”既寤，谓家人曰：“今日之事，必不可免。”居常戚戚不恰。考满又将赴调，复梦老父导之入门，见昔日之儿冠绯帽，紫袍银带，立于堂。顾谓谢曰：“此子已读书矣，若其谢我。”觉，大恶之，月余病卒。其子讷，庆历六年登进士第，亲说如此。

    Explanation

    64

    Xie, the Magistrate, was from the Plain region. During the reign of Emperor Renzong's Baoyuan era, he once served as an observer magistrate in Cao Prefecture. After taking office for a short time, one night he dreamed of an old man leading him into a grand mansion. The family was quite prosperous, and a wet nurse was holding an infant adorned with embroidered clothes. The old man pointed to the infant and said to Xie, "This is your reincarnation." Xie asked, "What city is this, and whose family is it?" The old man replied, "It is the residence of Magistrate Chen in Chengdu, and the wealth is very abundant. Are you happy with this?" Xie nodded in agreement. Upon waking, he was very unhappy and told his wife and children, "I will die soon. Prepare for the afterlife daily." After his term ended, he was then transferred to the position of magistrate in Di Prefecture. After serving for several months, he dreamed again of the old man leading him back to the mansion. There was a child dressed in fine silk playing at the steps. The old man pointed to the child and said to Xie, "This is the infant from before, now five years old, but still not speaking." Upon waking, he told his family, "Today's matter cannot be avoided." He always felt uneasy and discontented. After his term ended again and he was about to be transferred, he dreamed once more of the old man leading him into the mansion. He saw the child from before wearing a red hat, purple robe, and silver belt, standing in the hall. The old man turned and said to Xie, "This child has already started reading, so you should thank me." Upon waking, he was greatly displeased and died of illness after a month. His son, Na, passed the imperial examination in the sixth year of Qingli, as he personally recounted.

    65

    ○刘观察宅
    　　京师保康门有刘观察之别第，每僦于人。翰林学士曾布，嘉丙申之冬以乡贡将试礼部，僦此第以居。一夕不寐，闻厅中有人呼曰：“太尉来。”既而又有若往来问讯，切切细语，或如传授指令，皆以太尉为称，历历可审，甚讶之。翌日，究其宅之坊曲地里，则韩通之故第也，通尝为王彦族于斯第之下。

    Explanation

    65

    The Distinguished Residence of Observer Liu

    In the capital city, at the Baokang Gate, there was a secondary residence of Observer Liu, which was often rented out. During the winter of the year Jia Shen (1056) in the Xianfeng era, the scholar-official Zeng Bu, who was a local candidate for the imperial examinations and about to take the Ministry of Rites exam, rented this residence to live in. One night, unable to sleep, he heard someone calling from the hall, "The Grand Marshal is coming." Soon after, there were more voices, whispering and asking questions, or passing on orders and instructions, all referring to the Grand Marshal. The words were clear and distinct, and he was greatly surprised by this. The next day, he investigated the specific neighborhood and location of the residence and found that it was the former residence of Han Tong. Han Tong had once served as a relative of Wang Yanyi under this very residence.

    66

    ○柴氏枯枣
    　　邢州城东十余里，周世宗之祖庄也，门侧有井，上有大枣一株，世宗时柯叶茂盛，垂荫一亩，恭帝既禅，枣遂枯死。明道中，枯卉复生一枝，长一丈余，蔚然可爱，井中水如覆锦绣，柴氏惧，遂塞井伐木。明年，诏求五代帝王之后，柴氏自邢、蔡、虢等州诸族被甄叙入官者，三十余人，井枣之祥，亦非虚应。
    　　○僧缘新
    　　武陵郡西，有佛庙曰栗园，院主僧畜一犬，几十年。一夕，梦犬语云：“累岁荷畜养之恩，今当与堤头杜翁家为男，故来奉辞。”僧既觉，不以为意。黎明，侍者以犬毙闻，因大惊，乃策杖至堤头，杜迎门谓曰：“何出之早也”延僧坐，僧曰：“昨夕檀越家岂有子孙之庆乎”翁对以媳妇夜生一男，及询以何由而知，僧遂以梦告。翁亦骇异，因许之为浮屠，令以披缁剪发，法名缘新，鼎人率知之。

    Explanation

    66

    The Withered Jujube Tree of the Zhao Family

    East of Xing Prefecture, about ten li away, lies the ancestral temple of Emperor Shizong of Zhou. Beside the temple gate, there is a well with a large jujube tree growing above it. During the reign of Emperor Shizong, the tree was lush with branches and leaves, casting shade over an area of one acre. After Emperor Guo of Later Zhou abdicated, the jujube tree withered and died. During the Mingdao era, a new branch grew from the withered plant, reaching over ten feet in length, lush and attractive. The water in the well was clear and beautiful, like a patterned fabric. Afraid of this, the Zhao family blocked the well and cut down the tree. The following year, an imperial edict was issued to seek descendants of the emperors of the Five Dynasties. More than thirty people from various clans in Xing, Cai, and Guo Prefectures were appointed to official positions. The well and jujube tree were indeed signs of good fortune, not false.

    The Monk Yuanxin

    West of Wuling Prefecture, there is a Buddhist temple called Lishan Garden. The abbot of the temple kept a dog for several decades. One night, the abbot had a dream in which the dog spoke: "I have been grateful for your care over many years. Today, I will be reborn as a son in the family of Du Weng at Diti, so I come to bid farewell." Upon waking, the abbot did not think much of it. At dawn, the attendant informed him that the dog had died, and he was greatly surprised. The abbot then went to Diti with a staff. Du Weng greeted him at the door and asked, "Why did you come so early?" He invited the abbot to sit and said, "Did your family have any joy last night?" Du Weng replied that his daughter-in-law had given birth to a son the previous night. When asked how he knew, the abbot told him about the dream. Du Weng was also surprised and agreed to let the son become a monk. The son was made to wear monastic robes and shave his head, and his Buddhist name was Yuanxin. The people of Ding Prefecture generally knew about this.

    67

    ●卷六
    　　○王少保
    　　少保王公明，开宝八年乙亥拜秘书少监、黄州刺史，时王师问罪金陵，公帅师入豫章，市不易肆。至戊寅岁，受代徙传舍，有黄衣来谒，延之坐，乃曰：“公总兵入州洎解任，不戮一人，惠及物者大矣，阴骘垂无疆。”袖中出一通青纸，朱篆数幅，曰：“他日舟至大孤山，当有黄衣来谒，必能识之。”才出门即不见。及至大孤山，果有黄衣□止。公大喜，亟召见，即以篆文示之，乃曰：“请纸笔易为真字。”即乌犀丸方，书毕而去。公神其事，遂依方合之，服者无不效。盛太尉乃太保之孙女婿，得黄衣亲书本，盛疾作，服之亦愈。

    Explanation

    67

    Volume Six

    Wang Shao Bao

    Wang Shao Bao, also known as Wang Ming, was appointed as the Secretary of the Imperial Secretariat and Governor of Huangzhou in the eighth year of Kai Bao (975 AD). During this time, the imperial forces were engaged in a military campaign against Jinling (present-day Nanjing). Wang Ming led his troops into Yuzhang (present-day Nanchang), and the markets remained orderly, with business continuing as usual.

    In the fifth year of Kai Bao (978 AD), Wang Ming was relieved of his duties and moved to a temporary residence. A person dressed in yellow robes came to visit him. Wang Ming invited the visitor to sit and said, "When I led my troops into the state and then left my position, I did not harm a single person. My benevolent actions have brought great benefits to the people, and they will bring long-lasting blessings."

    The visitor pulled out a piece of blue paper with red seal script from his sleeve and said, "One day, when you sail to Dagu Mountain, there will be a person dressed in yellow robes who will come to visit you. You will certainly recognize him." As soon as the visitor left, he disappeared.

    When Wang Ming eventually sailed to Dagu Mountain, a person dressed in yellow robes indeed came to visit him. Wang Ming was delighted and quickly summoned the visitor. He showed the visitor the seal script and said, "Please write it in a more legible form." The visitor wrote the formula on an ivory tablet and then left.

    Wang Ming was amazed by this event and followed the formula to prepare the medicine. Those who took it were all cured. Sheng Taifu, the son-in-law of Wang Ming's grandson, received the original formula written by the visitor. When Sheng Taifu fell ill, he took the medicine and was cured.

    68

    ○范参政
    　　文正范公仲淹，字希文，天圣中以帖职通判陈州。时郡守以太夫人疾病，召一道士俾奏章祈，筑坛于正寝。郡守召公预其事，公窃笑曰：“庸鄙小人，安能达章帝所耶”但郡守以太夫人之故，多方以图安耳。既而复谓道士曰：“仲淹将来休咎可得知之否”道士曰：“唯俟至天曹问之。”既而秉简贽章伏于坛，自乙夜至四鼓，凝然不动，试扪其体，则僵矣。殆五更，手足微动，遽扶坐于床，饮以茶药，良久谓郡守曰：“奉贺太夫人，尚有六年寿，所苦不足忧也。”又谓：“公禄寿甚盛，必入政府。”郡守问：“今夕奏章何其久也”道士曰：“方出天阍，遇放明年进士春榜，观者骈道不得出，是以稽留。”公益不以为然，问曰：“状元何姓”曰：“姓王，二名，下一字墨涂之，旁注一字，远不可辨。”既而郡守之母疾苦寻平，明年春榜，状头乃王拱寿，御笔改为拱辰，公始叹道士之通神。

    Explanation

    68

    Fan Zhongyan, posthumously known as Wenzheng, with the courtesy name Xiwen, was appointed as the deputy governor of Chen Prefecture through a promotion from a lower position during the Tian圣 era. At the time, the prefect, concerned about his mother-in-law's illness, invited a Daoist priest to submit a petition for blessings and built a platform in the main hall. The prefect also invited Fan Zhongyan to participate in the event. Fan Zhongyan secretly laughed and said, "How could a vulgar and lowly person reach the emperor's presence with such a petition?" However, the prefect acted out of concern for his mother-in-law, seeking to ensure her comfort in various ways. Later, the prefect asked the Daoist priest, "Can you tell me about Fan Zhongyan's future fortune and misfortune?" The priest replied, "I will wait until I reach the heavenly bureaucracy to ask." The priest then held a tablet and bowed before the platform, remaining motionless from the second watch until the fourth watch. When they touched his body, he was found to be stiff. By the fifth watch, his hands and feet began to move slightly, and they quickly helped him sit up in bed, giving him tea and medicine. After a while, the priest said to the prefect, "Congratulations to your mother-in-law; she will live for another six years, and her illness is not something to worry about." He also said, "Your official career and longevity will be very prosperous, and you will certainly enter the central government." The prefect asked, "Why did the petition take so long?" The priest replied, "I was just leaving the heavenly gate when I encountered the release of the next year's spring imperial examination list. The crowd was so dense that I could not proceed, causing the delay." Fan Zhongyan was even more skeptical and asked, "What is the surname of the top scorer?" The priest replied, "He has the surname Wang, with two characters. The last character is covered in ink, and there is a note next to it, but it is far away and cannot be seen clearly." Later, the prefect's mother-in-law's illness improved, and the following year, the top scorer in the spring imperial examination was Wang Gongshou, whose name was changed to Gongchen by the emperor. Fan Zhongyan then marveled at the Daoist priest's supernatural abilities.

    69

    ○麦道录
    　　麦道录本宦者，尝为入内供奉官勾当事材场，一日出西水门，有丐者死于汴河，岸之侧有败席短杖。时方大雪，独不积其身，麦异之，为市衫裤麻履故巾，瘗之于隙地。他日奉使延，至薄坂北一邮置，有一贫人诣门请见，仍云：“尝受恩，故来致谢。”麦召见，询其由，曰：“自顶至踵皆君所赐也。”麦罔然，良久方省瘗丐者事，乃延坐与语，屏左右，移时而去。麦既回京，发瘗，但见席杖而已。麦遂弃官为道士，为左街道录，年九十余卒。

    Explanation

    69

    Mc Dao Lu, originally a eunuch, once served as the chief official overseeing the imperial timber yard. One day, he passed through the western water gate and saw a beggar who had died by the Bian River, with rotten mats and short sticks beside him. It was snowing heavily, but the beggar's body was not covered in snow. Mc found this strange and bought clothes, trousers, hemp shoes, and an old headscarf, then buried the beggar in a secluded spot. Later, while on a mission to Yanmen, he reached a post station to the north of a thin slope, where a poor man came to his door to request an audience, saying, "I have received a favor from you and come to express my gratitude." Mc called him in and asked about the reason for his gratitude. The poor man replied, "Everything from head to toe was given by you." Mc was puzzled but, after a long while, recalled burying the beggar. He then invited him to sit and spoke privately, dismissing his attendants, and they talked for a while before the man left. After Mc returned to the capital, he dug up the burial site and found only the mats and sticks. He then resigned from his official position to become a Taoist priest, serving as a Left Street Daoist priest, and lived to be over ninety years old.

    70

    ○杨道人
    　　杨道人者，不知何许人也，往来郢之京山县、丰国范顿市中，好与小儿戏狎，虽大寒甚暑而未尝巾帻衣裳，惟裸露，而或以衣服赠人，旋即施与丐者，故人尤恶视之，往往逆知人中心事。复州苏绎寺丞得一烧朱砂银法，试之有验，往见之，杨即前曰：“涩涩酸朱砂，烧尽水银干。”更不复语。又，彭长官者，欲求地葬其母，以纸干之乞数字，直书云：翻车二十五千。既而果于翻车村得其地，以二十五贯市之。熙宁癸丑岁，辛子仪令京山，杨每来谒之，赠以衫帽，或留宿外斋，虽设衾榻，密视之，已安寝于地矣。未几，索纸笔横作二画，自一二三四书讫，授子仪，谛视之，乃四字也。果至四月，而乃父弃世。道途商贩皆云：“见其死于数处矣，而形状不改。”熙宁七年，卒于范顿豪民张绛家，为买棺，埋于市侧。市民朱如玉方客京师，是日见杨来访，不交一言，后朱自京师回，白县，开其藏，惟空棺耳。其异迹甚多，能记其一二也。

    Explanation

    70

    Translation:

    Yang Dao Ren

    Yang Dao Ren, a man of unknown origin, traveled between Jing County in Ying and Fandun Market in Fengguo. He enjoyed playing and interacting with children, and even in extreme cold or heat, he never wore a head covering, hat, or clothing, remaining only naked. Sometimes he would give clothes to others, only to immediately give them to beggars, which made people particularly dislike him. He often could predict people's inner thoughts. Su Yi, the official in charge of Fuzhou, discovered a method for smelting silver with cinnabar, which proved effective. He went to see Yang Dao Ren, who immediately said, "Sour cinnabar, burn until the mercury dries." He then said nothing more. Another time, a local official named Peng sought land to bury his mother and asked Yang Dao Ren for some numbers written on paper. Yang wrote directly: "Flipcart for twenty-five thousand." Soon after, Peng indeed found the land in Flipcart Village and bought it for twenty-five thousand. In the year 1073 during the reign of Emperor Shenzong, Xin Ziyi, the magistrate of Jing County, often received visits from Yang Dao Ren, who would be given shirts and hats, or sometimes invited to stay overnight in an outer study. Even though beds and quilts were provided, when closely observed, Yang Dao Ren was already sleeping on the ground. Soon after, he asked for paper and a pen, drew two horizontal lines, and wrote the numbers one, two, three, and four, then gave the paper to Xin Ziyi. Upon close inspection, it was clear that the numbers formed the word "four." Indeed, by April, Xin Ziyi's father had passed away. Traders and merchants all said, "We saw him die in several places, but his appearance did not change." In the seventh year of the Xining era, Yang Dao Ren died at the home of the wealthy Zhang Jie in Fandun, and a coffin was bought for him, and he was buried beside the market. A citizen named Zhu Ruyu, who was traveling in the capital, saw Yang Dao Ren visiting that day and did not speak to him. Later, when Zhu returned to the county, he reported to the authorities, and upon opening the tomb, only an empty coffin was found. There were many strange occurrences, and some of them can be recorded here.

    71

    ○李芝
    　　广州新会县道士李芝，性和厚简默，居常若愚者，间为两韵诗，飘飘非尘俗语。常读史传，善吐纳辟谷之术。肤体不屡濯，自然洁清，发有绿光，立则委地。所居房室不施关键。邑人崇向，施与金钱衣服无算，人取去，未尝有言。或召设祠醮，一夜有数处见者。至和中多虎暴，芝持策入山，月余方出，谓之曰：“已戒之矣。”自此虎暴亦息。余至和中亲见之，今则尸解矣。
    　　○张白
    　　张白字虚白，自称白云子，清河人，性沉静，博学能文，两举进士不第。会亲丧，乃泣而自谓曰：“禄以养亲，今亲不逮于禄，何为”遂辟谷不食，以养气全神为事，道家之书无不研赜。开宝中，南游荆渚，时乡人韩可比为通守，延纳甚欢，会朝廷吊伐江吴，军府多事，因褫儒服为道士，适武陵寓龙兴观。郡守刘公侍郎犀、监兵张延福深加礼重，尝以方鉴遗张，曰：“收之，可以辟邪。

    Explanation

    71

    ○Li Zhi
    　　Li Zhi, a Daoist practitioner from Xinhui County in Guangzhou, was kind, generous, reserved, and quiet. He often appeared simple, but occasionally composed two-line poems that were ethereal and not of the mundane world. He frequently read historical records and was skilled in breathing exercises and fasting techniques. His body did not need frequent washing; it was naturally clean and pure. His hair had a greenish glow, and when he stood, it reached the ground. His dwelling did not have locks or keys. The people of the county revered him, and he received countless gifts of money and clothes, which people took without him ever complaining. If he was summoned to perform rituals, he could be seen at multiple places in one night. During the Zhonghe period, there were many tiger attacks, and Li Zhi carried a staff into the mountains, not returning for over a month. When he came out, he said, "I have already warned them." From then on, the tiger attacks ceased. I personally saw him during the Zhonghe period, and he has now achieved spiritual transformation (shi jie).

    ○Zhang Bai
    　　Zhang Bai, whose courtesy name was Xubai and who called himself Baiyunzi, was from Qinghe. He was calm and reserved, well-learned, and skilled in writing. He took the imperial examinations twice but did not pass. When his parents died, he wept and said to himself, "Salary is meant to support one's parents, but now my parents did not live to enjoy my salary, what is the point?" He then stopped eating and began fasting to cultivate his qi and preserve his spirit. He studied all Daoist texts thoroughly. During the Kaibao period, he traveled south to Jingzhou. At the time, a fellow townsman named Han Kebi was the governor, and he welcomed Zhang Bai warmly. Coincidentally, the court was engaged in military campaigns against Jiang and Wu, and there was much activity in the military headquarters. Zhang Bai then discarded his scholar's robes and became a Daoist, traveling to Wuling and staying at Longxing Temple. The local official, Liu Gong, a high-ranking civil servant, and the military official, Zhang Yanfu, treated him with great respect. Once, Zhang Yanfu gave Zhang Bai a mirror and said, "Keep it, it can ward off evil."

    72

    ”白韬真自晦，日以沉湎为事，傲乎其不可得而亲者。往往入廛市中，多所诟骂，切中人微隐之事，众皆异之。每遇风雪苦寒，则必破冰深入，安坐水中，永日方出，衣襦沔湿，气如蒸炊，指顾之间，悉以干燥。或与人为戏，仰视正立，令恶少数辈尽力推曳，略不少偃。又或仰卧舒一足，令三四人举之，众但面，其足不动。居常饮崔氏酒肆，崔未尝讨其直，家人每云：此道士来则酒客辐凑。尝题其壁云：武陵溪畔崔家酒，地上应无天上有。南来道士饮一斗，卧在白云深洞口。

    Explanation

    72

    White Tao Zhen concealed his true nature, daily indulging in drunkenness as a matter, and was arrogantly unapproachable. He often entered the marketplaces, where he was frequently cursed and insulted, but his insults were particularly revealing and incisive, striking at people's hidden secrets, and everyone found it strange. Whenever he encountered severe cold and snow, he would break through the ice and dive deep, sitting calmly in the water, remaining there for a whole day before emerging. His clothes were soaked, and his breath was like steam, but in the blink of an eye, they all dried up. Sometimes he would play games with people, looking up while standing upright, ordering a few bad people to push and pull with all their might, but he barely bent at all. Or sometimes he would lie on his back with one leg stretched out, ordering three or four people to lift him, and the crowd just looked embarrassed, but his foot did not move. He usually drank at Cui's tavern, and Cui never asked for payment. The family always said: whenever this Taoist comes, customers gather like spokes around a hub. He once wrote on the wall: "Cui's wine at the Wuling Creek, there should be none on earth as there is in heaven. A southern Taoist drinks a dou, lying in the deep cave entrance of white clouds."

    自是沽者尤倍。南岳道士唐允升、魏应时，亦当时有道之士也。慕其人，常与之游。白天才敏赡，思如涌泉，数日闻赋《武陵春色》诗三百首，皆以“武陵春色里”为题。一旦称疾，亟语观主曰：“我固不起，慎勿燔吾尸，恐乡亲寻访。”言讫而绝，身体润泽，异香满室，倾城士女观瞻累日，为买棺葬于西门外。逾年，监兵罢归，其仆遇白于扬州开明桥，问：“方鉴在否为我语汝郎，斯鉴亦不久留。

    Explanation

    73

    Since then, the price of wine doubled. Taoist priests Tang Yunsheng and Wei Yingshi from Mount Heng were also virtuous men of their time. Admiring him, they often associated with him. He was naturally gifted and had a sharp mind, his thoughts flowed like a fountain. In a few days, he composed 300 poems titled "The Spring Colors of Wu Ling," all of which were titled "In the Spring Colors of Wu Ling." One day, he claimed to be ill and urgently told the monk, saying, "I will not rise again, be careful not to burn my body, I fear that my hometown relatives will come to look for me." After he finished speaking, he died, his body remained moist, and a strange fragrance filled the room. The entire city's men and women came to pay their respects for several days, and they bought a coffin to bury him outside the west gate. After a year, the military officer returned home, and his servant met Bai at the Kai Ming Bridge in Yangzhou, asking, "Is Fang Jian still there? Tell my son, this mirror will not stay long."

    ”仆归具道，张骇曰：“渠死久矣，汝何见邪”寻索鉴熟视，随手而碎。又，鼎之步奏官余安者，以公事至扬州，亦遇白携大葫芦货药，亟召安饮于酒肆，话武陵旧游。数日安告行，白曰：“为我附书谢崔氏。”余归致书，崔氏览之大惊，遽掘所埋棺，已空矣。白注《护命经》，穷极微旨，又著《指玄篇》，五七言杂诗，唐魏集而名为《丹台》，并传于时。大抵神仙之事，见于传记，若白之解去，此耳目相接，年祀未甚远。今室而祠之，不惟众所瞻仰，抑将传信于永世也。
    　　○静长官

    Explanation

    74

    Upon returning, I recounted the story to Zhang, who was startled and said, "He has been dead for a long time. How could you have seen him?" He searched for and examined the mirror closely, and it broke with a touch. Another time, the minor official named Yu An, responsible for steps and procedures, traveled to Yangzhou on official business and also encountered Bai carrying a large gourd selling medicine. Bai quickly summoned Yu An to drink at an inn, reminiscing about their old travels in Wuling. After several days, Yu An informed Bai that he was about to leave. Bai said, "Write a letter for me to thank Cui's family." Upon returning, I delivered the letter, and Cui's family, upon reading it, were greatly astonished. They immediately dug up the buried coffin, which was already empty. Bai annotated the Sutra of Protecting Life, exhaustively exploring its subtle meanings, and also wrote The Chapter of Pointing to the Mysteries, mixed poems of five and seven characters, and a collection named The Red Terrace, all of which were circulated during his time. Generally speaking, matters of immortals are recorded in biographies. If Bai had disappeared, these events would be recent and well-documented. Now, if we build a shrine and worship him, not only will people look up to him, but his story will also be transmitted to future generations.

    ○ Tranquil Official

    75

    静长官，真定人，登明经第，寡嗜欲，好道家修摄事，一旦，弃妻子，游名山，数年不归。天圣中，先君与亲旧杜获、向知古会于磁州慕容太保之第，始然烛，叩门颇急，启之，乃静也，袍皂条布巾芒ハ，把臂甚喜。询其所往，曰：“自别，浪迹于山水间，良惟素志。今将归真定视妻孥，闻诸君会此，故来相见。”既饮，静曰：“方道旧为乐而酒薄不可饮，某有药以资酒味。”于小囊中出药一粒如弹丸，投瓶中，复幂口，良久饮之，气味极醇烈。夜漏上四鼓，诸公皆酩酊就寝，鸡既鸣，静独谓仆夫曰：“或诸公睡起，报云我且归真定也。”既晓，相与叹静药之为神，亟命健仆走真定问其家，云：“未尝暂归。”余前年寓洛下，有医助教靳袭者，于其家常帷一榻，枕蓐甚洁，人问其故，曰：“以待静长官。”静今隐嵩少间，岁或一至、或再至，靳氏以神仙事之。尝以方书授靳，由是医术大行，家赀数千万。静今年逾百岁，状貌止如四五十人，洛人多知之。

    Explanation

    75

    Master Jing, a native of Zhending, passed the Mingjing examination and had few worldly desires. He was fond of Taoist practices of cultivation and self-discipline. One day, he abandoned his wife and children and began wandering in the mountains, not returning for several years. During the Tian圣 period, my father and old acquaintances Du Hui and Xiang Zhigu met at the residence of the Duke of Murong in Cizhou. As they were just lighting the candles, the door was knocked on quite urgently. When they opened it, it was Master Jing, dressed in a coarse robe, a black cloth cap, and wearing simple sandals. He clasped arms with great joy. When asked about his whereabouts, he said, "Since we parted ways, I have been wandering aimlessly in the mountains and rivers, truly in line with my long-held aspirations. Now I am returning to Zhending to see my family. Hearing that you all are gathered here, I came to see you." After drinking, Master Jing said, "While reminiscing about old times is joyful, the wine is too weak to drink. I have a medicine to enhance the flavor of the wine." He took out a pill the size of a bullet from a small bag, placed it in the wine bottle, and covered the mouth. After a long time, they drank it, and the wine had an extremely rich and strong flavor. It was past the fourth watch of the night, and all the guests were drunk and went to bed. When the rooster crowed, Master Jing alone told the servant, "If the guests wake up, tell them I will return to Zhending." By morning, everyone marveled at the miraculous effect of Master Jing's medicine and quickly sent a strong servant to Zhending to inquire about his family, who said, "He has never returned for even a moment." Last year, while staying in Luoyang, there was a medical instructor named Jin Xi. At his home, he often had a bed prepared, with clean pillows and bedding. People asked him why, and he said, "In anticipation of the arrival of Master Jing." Master Jing now lives in seclusion in the Shang Mountains, visiting once or twice a year. The Jin family treats him as a divine being. He once gave medical texts to Jin, as a result of which his medical skills became widely known, and his family's wealth amounted to several million. Master Jing is now over a hundred years old, but his appearance is that of someone in their forties or fifties. Many people in Luoyang know of him.

    76

    ○率子廉
    　　衡岳道士率子廉，落魄无他能，嗜酒性狠，悖于事，多不通易，辱人以言，人亦少与之接，故以牛呼焉。居山之魏阁，景甚幽邃，而子廉慵惰，致芜秽委积，而弗加芟扫，以是景趣湮没，阁宇圮坏，游者以其境污人陋，亦罕到焉。故礼部侍郎王公，以中书舍人守潭州，立夏将命祀祝融，至衡岳游览佛寺道庙殆遍，因访所谓魏阁者。群道士告以摧陋无足观，而王公坚欲一视，及至，则子廉犹醉寝。王公入其室，左右呼索之，而子廉酲未解，徐下榻，拭目瞪视王公，久之乃曰：“穷山道士，遇酒即醉，幸公不以为罪。”左右皆股栗，而王公欣然无忤。其应答之言虽甚俚野，而气貌自若。

    Explanation

    76

    ○Rate Zilean
    　　The Taoist priest Rate Zilean, a disheveled and unskilled man, loves drinking and has a fierce nature, often acting contrary to reason. He is difficult to understand and tends to insult others with his words, so people rarely interact with him, and he is called "Cow" as a nickname. He lives in the Wei Pavilion in the mountains, where the scenery is very secluded and deep. However, Zilean is lazy and idle, leading to weeds and debris accumulating, and the place is not cleaned up. As a result, the scenery and interest are lost, and the pavilion is in ruins. Visitors find the environment dirty and the people unsightly, and they rarely visit.

    The Counselor of the Ministry of Rites, Wang Gong, served as a Secretary of the Central Secretariat in Changsha. On the day of the summer solstice, he was ordered to perform a sacrifice to Zhurong and visited almost all the Buddhist temples and Taoist shrines in Hengshan. He then visited the so-called Wei Pavilion. The group of Taoist priests told him that it was dilapidated and not worth seeing, but Wang Gong insisted on seeing it once. When he arrived, Zilean was still drunk and sleeping. Wang Gong's attendants called out to him, but Zilean was still not fully awake. Slowly, he got off the bed, wiped his eyes, and stared at Wang Gong. After a long time, he said, "A poor mountain Taoist, who gets drunk immediately upon drinking, thankfully you do not hold it against me." Everyone around him was trembling with fear, but Wang Gong was pleased and not offended. His responses were very crude and rustic, but his demeanor remained calm and composed.

    77

    王公异之，遂载与还郡，日与之饮酒，所以顾待之甚渥，人亦莫谕何以致然也。间辞归山，复止魏阁者又半年，然王公问遗时时至山，复作诗二章寄之。一日，忽谓人曰：“我将远行，当一别舍人。”即日扁舟下潭，谒王公，且曰：“将有所适，先来告别。”公曰：“往何地”则曰：“未有所止，缘某一念所诣，则翩然径行，恐尔时不复得别，故预耳。”王公留与之饮，居二日辞归魏阁。至之日，以书别衡山观主李公，盥浴，饰服，焚香，秉简即中堂而蜕去。闻者惊异，李为买棺厚葬之。殆半岁，有衡岳寺僧自京至，于安上门外见子廉，云：“来看京师即还，时蒙李观主厚有赆行。”怀中出一书附僧为谢。李发其封，真子廉之书也。人皆叹王公之默识。

    77

    The prince found the person extraordinary and took him back to the prefecture, where he drank with him every day, treating him with great favor. No one could understand why it was so. The person would occasionally leave to return to the mountains, staying at the Wei Pavilion for another half a year. Yet, the prince would often send gifts to the mountains and composed two poems to send to him. One day, the person suddenly said to someone, "I am going on a long journey, so I should bid farewell to you." On that day, he took a small boat down to the lake, paying a visit to the prince, and said, "I am going somewhere, so I came to say goodbye first." The prince asked, "Where are you going?" The person replied, "I have no fixed destination. Following a sudden inspiration, I would depart suddenly, fearing I will not have the chance to say goodbye again, so I am doing so now." The prince kept him and drank with him, and after two days, he bid farewell and returned to the Wei Pavilion. On the day he arrived, he wrote a letter to bid farewell to Master Li, the head of a Taoist temple in Hengshan, washed, dressed, burned incense, held a tablet, and passed away in the central hall. Those who heard were astonished, and Master Li bought a coffin and gave him a grand burial. Almost half a year later, a monk from Hengshan Temple came from the capital and saw Zilian outside the Anmen Gate, saying, "I came to see the capital and then returned. He was often given generous gifts by Master Li when he traveled." He took out a letter and asked the monk to deliver it as a thank-you. Master Li opened the envelope, and it was truly a letter from Zilian. Everyone admired the prince's intuitive understanding.

    ○许偏头
    　　成都府画师许偏头者，忘其名，善传神，开画肆于观街。一日，有贫人弊衣憔悴、约四十许，负布囊诣许，求传神，许笑曰：“君容状若此而求传神，得非有所禀而召仆也邪”曰：“非也。闻君笔妙，故来耳，幸无见鄙。”即解布囊，出黄道服一袭，又出一鹿皮冠、白玉簪，遂顶矣，引其须，应手而黑且长矣，乃一美丈夫也。许大惊，谢曰：“不知神仙降临，前言戏渎，诚负愧惕。

    Explanation

    78

    A Man with a Unique Appearance

    In the city of Chengdu, there was a painter named Xu Biantou, whose name has been forgotten, but who was skilled in capturing the essence of a person. He opened a painting shop on Guan Street. One day, a poor man, dressed in tattered clothes and looking weary, about forty years old, carrying a cloth bag, came to visit Xu, seeking a portrait. Xu smiled and said, "With such an appearance, you seek a portrait? Isn't it that you have something to request and summoned me?" The man replied, "No, I have heard of your skill with the brush and have come to you, please do not look down on me." He then opened the cloth bag, revealing a yellow robe, a deer-skin cap, and a white jade hairpin. He put on the cap, and as he touched his beard, it immediately turned black and grew long, transforming him into a handsome man. Xu was greatly surprised and apologized, saying, "I did not know that a divine being had descended. My previous words were playful and disrespectful, truly I feel ashamed and anxious."

    79

    ”道人笑曰：“君可传吾像置肆中，后当有识者或求售者，止取一千钱，不可逾也。”许如命写讫，未及语，携囊而出，许拜谢，已不见。许遂陈所传像于肆，有识之者曰：“此灵泉朱真人也。”求售者日十数，许家赀遂日益。后以贪直，画且不给，每像辄云二千。是夕，梦道人谓曰：“汝福有限，吾尝戒汝不可妄取厚直，安得忽吾言促其寿也。”遂掌其左颊。既寤，头遂偏，自是呼为许偏头。庆历中，许年八十余方卒。朱真人者，乃朱居士□□也。见《唐书》列传、杜光庭《列仙传》。

    Explanation

    79

    The Taoist smiled and said, "You may have my portrait placed in your shop. Later, there will be those who recognize it or wish to buy it. Only take one thousand coins, and do not exceed that." Xu followed the command and finished the painting. Before he could speak, the Taoist left with his bag. Xu bowed and thanked him, but he was already gone. Xu then displayed the portrait in his shop. Those who recognized it said, "This is the Immortal Zhu of Lingquan." Those who wanted to buy it came daily in dozens, and Xu's wealth gradually increased. Later, because of greed, he raised the price and could barely keep up with the demand. For each portrait, he would say two thousand coins. That night, Xu dreamed that the Taoist told him, "Your fortune is limited. I once warned you not to take an excessive price. How could you ignore my words and shorten your life?" He then slapped his left cheek. After waking, his head became crooked, and from then on, he was called Xu the Crooked-Headed. During the Qingli era, Xu died at over eighty years old. The Immortal Zhu was actually Master Zhu □□. See Tangshu Biographies and Du Guangting's Records of the Immortals.

    ○张翰
    　　张翰，江陵人，业进士，其父前妻生三子而亡，父再娶窦氏，翰窦出也。窦之生，岁月日时不利于夫，遂减岁，迁就吉辰，而归于张氏。间与厥夫祷嗣于归真观之三清殿，祝辞以所减之齿告焉，继育数子，而翰父物故。会归真观火，窦密以镪五十万与道士修殿宇，少时窦亦死。后数岁，翰忽为神所凭，以手执髻，鞠躬曰：“听圣语：窦氏以诈伪之岁诬罔上真，又弗询于子，私用家赀，已受考于阴府，今则为异类矣。”事皆秘密，众所不知者，如是不一，由是荆人率闻之。噫！女子增减其年以利适人者，为过虽小，妄以告神则罪大也。专取家帑以用构祠堂，不俾子知，神尚责怒，矧非理而用者乎

    Explanation

    80

    Zhang Han, a man from Jiangling, pursued the path of a jinshi. His father's first wife gave birth to three sons and then passed away. The father remarried a woman from the Dòu family, and Zhang Han was born to her. At the time of the Dòu wife's birth, the date and time were considered unfavorable for her husband. Therefore, the age was reduced, and the birth date was adjusted to a more auspicious one, and she returned to the Zhang family. Occasionally, she and her husband prayed for offspring at the Sanqing Hall in the Guizhen Temple, stating the reduced age in their prayers. Later, she gave birth to several more children, and then Zhang Han's father passed away. Coincidentally, the Guizhen Temple caught fire. The Dòu wife secretly gave 500,000 units of money to the Taoist priests to repair the temple. After a short time, the Dòu wife also died. Several years later, Zhang Han suddenly became possessed by a deity. With his hand holding his hair, he bowed and said, "Listen to the divine words: the Dòu wife deceived the true deity with a false and deceitful age, did not consult her children, and used family wealth secretly. She has already been judged in the underworld and is now an otherworldly being." All these matters are secret and unknown to the public, such cases are not uncommon, and therefore, people from Jing generally became aware of them. Alas! Women who add or subtract their age to benefit their marriage, even if the mistake is small, to falsely report to the deity is a great sin. Specifically taking family wealth to build a shrine without informing the children, the deity still holds a grudge. How much more so if it is used unjustly.
