    ●卷七
    　　○张龙图
    　　龙图张公焘，即枢密直学士奎之子也，枢直为殿中丞日，奉朝请在京师，税宅于汴河南小巷中，居常闭关。一日，有人叩门颇急，大呼曰：“小师入去，何故便不放出”张起视之，乃一老道士也，疑其狂且醉，不复与之校量，良久乃去。邑君先妊娠，是夕生焘，焘景元年第进士甲科，后尝误食犬肉，梦黄衣使者逮至一府，宏丽如宫阙，见一道士谓曰：“何故食厌物”张自辨，致曰：“非敢故食，误耳。”道士曰：“若然者，且止此，吾为若言。”少选复出，谓张曰：“可谢恩。”乃引至一殿前，通曰：“张焘误食厌物。”谢既再拜而悟，汗流浃体。景元神骨清粹，襟怀夷旷，岂非仙曹之被谪者欤。

    Explanation

    81

    Volume Seven
    Mr. Zhang, the Dragon Diagram

    Mr. Zhang, known as the Dragon Diagram, was the son of Kuí, the Grand Councillor and Academician. When Kuí served as the Palace Attendant, he performed ceremonial duties in the capital. Mr. Zhang rented a residence in a small alley south of the Bian River and usually kept the doors closed. One day, someone knocked on the door very urgently and shouted, "The little master went in, why did you not let them out immediately?" Zhang looked out and saw an old Taoist priest. Suspecting that the man was either mad or drunk, Zhang did not argue with him and the man eventually left.

    Before the local lord was pregnant, that night Zhang was born. In the first year of the Jingyou era, Zhang passed the imperial examination and ranked first in the highest category. Later, he mistakenly ate dog meat and had a dream where a yellow-robed messenger brought him to a magnificent government office. He saw a Taoist priest who said to him, "Why did you eat taboo food?" Zhang defended himself, saying, "I did not intentionally eat it; it was a mistake." The priest replied, "If that is the case, for now, let it be, I will speak on your behalf." A short while later, the priest came out and said to Zhang, "You can express your gratitude." He then led Zhang to the front of a hall and said, "Zhang, you mistakenly ate taboo food." After bowing twice, Zhang came to understand and sweated profusely.

    During the Jingyou era, Zhang's spirit and bones were pure and refined, and his heart was broad and open. Was he a deity who was demoted to a mortal?

    82

    ○孙副枢
    　　宝元中，副枢孙公沔，自小谏以言事左迁监永州市征，尝梦一道士喻以牵复之期，又曰：“吾有少田在部下，为人所盗，可为正之。”俄而孙移ヘ长沙，因祠岳庙，遍游道观佛寺，至九仙观，见王真人像，克肖梦中之见者，询其公财岁入，则云：“有田数百亩，为邻畔有力者所侵。”遂檄县穷究，尽取故田还之。观乃梁天监中建，后废，唐刺史张觌复加营构，庭有磐石如坛，上可坐三十人。九仙者皆轻举于是地，晋道士陈兴明、施存、尹道全，宋徐灵期，齐陈惠度、张昙要，梁张始珍、王灵舆、邓郁之也。
    　　○芙蓉观主
    　　庆历中，有朝士冒辰赴起居，至通衢，见美妇三十余人，靓妆丽服，两两并马而行，若前导，俄见丁观文度拥徒按辔，继之而去。朝士惊曰：“丁素俭约，何姬侍之众多邪”有一人最后行，朝士问曰：“观文洎宅眷将游何处”对曰：“非也。诸女御迎芙容馆主耳。”时丁巳在告，顷之闻丁卒。（辛都官子言云）

    Explanation

    82

    ○孙副枢
    During the Baoyuan era, Vice-Chancellor Sun Gong Mian, who had been demoted from a minor official position due to his outspokenness, was appointed as the supervisor of Yongzhou. He once dreamed of a Taoist who explained to him the period of his restoration. The Taoist also said, "I have some land under my jurisdiction that has been stolen by someone; it can be reclaimed." Soon after, Sun was transferred to Changsha, where he visited the Temple of the Five Great Mountains and toured various Daoist and Buddhist temples. He reached the Nine Immortals Temple and saw an image of Master Wang that closely resembled what he had seen in his dream. When he inquired about the temple's annual revenue, he was told, "There are several hundred acres of land that have been encroached upon by a powerful neighbor." Sun then issued an order to investigate the matter thoroughly and reclaimed the land. The temple was originally built during the Tianjian period of the Liang Dynasty, later fell into disuse, and was restored by Governor Zhang Di of the Tang Dynasty. The courtyard had a large stone platform that could seat thirty people. The nine immortals were said to have ascended to immortality in this place. They include Taoists Chen Xingming, Shi Cun, Yin Daquan from the Jin Dynasty; Xu Lingqi from the Song Dynasty; Chen Huidu and Zhang Tanyao from the Qi Dynasty; Zhang Shizhen, Wang Lingyu, and Deng Yuzhi from the Liang Dynasty.

    ○芙蓉观主
    During the Qingli era, a scholar-official hurried to attend the court audience and reached a main street where he saw more than thirty beautiful women dressed in elegant and luxurious attire, riding side by side as if leading the way. Soon, he saw Ding Guanwende, accompanied by his followers, controlling his horse and following them. The scholar-official was surprised and said, "Ding is usually frugal; why does he have so many concubines?" One person walking behind said, "He doesn't. These ladies are going to meet the Lady of the Lotus Pavilion." At that time, Ding was on leave, and shortly after, the scholar-official heard of Ding's death. (According to Xin Duanguanziyan)

    ○曾屯田
    　　屯田外郎曾公奉先，嘉中知惠州，守居有蔬圃，役老卒守之，灌时尤力，凡曾所欲之物必先致之，呼而问之：“汝常逆知吾意，何也”老卒曰：“偶然耳。”再三诘之，但唯唯而已，曾自此善待之，时赉之以酒食。一日薄暮，老卒白曾曰：“荷使君厚顾，某非碌碌者，今夜三鼓，乞使君一到园中，有秘术上闻。”曾欣然许诺。及期，将具公服诣之，家人皆曰：“岂有郡守夜半公裳，谒一老卒哉”遽止。黎明，报园子物故，仍于腰下得白金数千两，曾惋叹不已，买棺殡于野。数月，有人自广州来，园卒附书为谢。视其墓，四周摧陷，柩悉破露，发之，但袍巾屦在焉。曾以谓尸解也，追悔自咎者累月，因而颇失心。

    Explanation

    83

    ○曾屯田
    　　Zeng Fengxian, a prefectural official in charge of land management, served as the governor of Huizhou during the middle of the Jia You era. His residence had a vegetable garden, which was tended by an elderly soldier. This soldier was particularly diligent in watering the plants and would always provide whatever Zeng desired first. One day, Zeng called the soldier and asked, "You always seem to anticipate my intentions. Why is that?" The soldier replied, "It's just by chance." Zeng questioned him repeatedly, but the soldier merely nodded in agreement. From then on, Zeng treated the soldier kindly and often gave him wine and food. One evening, the soldier approached Zeng and said, "I appreciate your kindness, Lord. I am not an ordinary person. Tonight, at the third watch, I would like you to come to the garden. I have a secret method to report." Zeng happily agreed. When the time came, Zeng was about to dress in official attire and go to the garden, but his family objected, saying, "How could a prefect wear official robes at midnight to visit an old soldier?" Zeng hastily canceled the plan. The next morning, it was reported that the soldier had died. When his body was examined, several thousand taels of silver were found in his waist. Zeng regretted and lamented endlessly, buying a coffin and burying the soldier in the wild. Several months later, someone from Guangzhou arrived with a letter from the soldier, thanking Zeng. When they examined the tomb, they found it had collapsed on all sides, and the coffin was completely broken and exposed. Upon opening it, only the soldier's robe, cap, and shoes remained. Zeng believed this was a form of spiritual transformation. He regretted and blamed himself for months, and consequently became somewhat deranged.

    ○郭上灶
    　　郭上灶者，不知何许人，天禧中，尝以备雇瀹汤涤器于州桥茶肆间。一日，有青巾布袍而啜茶者，形貌环伟，神彩凛然，屡目于郭，郭亦既疑其异人，又窃觇，于袖间引出利剑。郭私念曰：“必吕先生也。”伺其出，即走拜于前曰：“际遇先生，愿为仆厮。”吕不顾东去，郭乃尾后至一阒处，吕回顾曰：“若真欲事我耶可受吾一剑。”郭唯唯，延颈以俟，引剑将击，郭大呼，已失吕所在，乃在百万仓中。巡卒擒送官，杖而遣去，自此京城里外，幽僻之所无不至，见人必熟视良久方去，问之，则曰：“我寻先生。

    Explanation

    84

    Guo Shangzao was a man of unknown origin. During the Tianxi era, he was hired to boil water and clean dishes in the tea shops near the State Bridge. One day, a man wearing a blue headband and a plain robe, sipping tea, frequently looked at Guo Shangzao. Guo Shangzao, suspecting the man was someone extraordinary, secretly observed him and noticed him pulling out a sharp sword from his sleeve. Guo Shangzao thought to himself, "This must be Mr. Lü." He waited for the man to leave and then rushed forward to bow before him, saying, "I hope to meet Mr. Lü and be your servant." Mr. Lü did not look back and went east. Guo Shangzao followed him to a quiet place. Mr. Lü turned back and said, "If you truly want to serve me, you can accept my sword." Guo Shangzao nodded in agreement and stretched his neck to wait. Mr. Lü was about to strike with the sword when Guo Shangzao shouted loudly. By then, Mr. Lü was nowhere to be seen, and Guo Shangzao found himself inside the million-grain granary. Patrol soldiers captured him and sent him to the authorities, who beat him and dismissed him. From then on, Guo Shangzao went everywhere in the capital, even the most secluded places. When he saw people, he would stare at them for a long time before leaving. When asked, he would say, "I am looking for Mr. Lü."

    85

    ”自此十年余，不知所在，天圣末，有赵长官者，家居磁州邑城镇之别业，忽有丐者袍而来，见赵再拜曰：“某郭上灶也。”赵亦尝识之，遂问：“见先生否”郭曰：“周天下不之见，今为大数垂尽，故来求一小棺以藏遗骸。”赵大以为妄，问曰：“何日当尽”曰：“来日午时。”赵曰：“若然，当为汝买棺。”仍告曰：“棺首开一穴，将一竹竿通其节插穴中，庶得通气。”赵虽唯之，殊谓不然。明日午时，汲水浣身，卧槐下遂绝。赵大异之，为造棺，河朔乏竹，取故伞柄通其中，插棺首，瘗之于河岸，仍恐为狐犬所发，植棘累石以固焉。其年秋，大雨，河水泛涨，数日乃退，赵虑其柩为水所漂，策杖临视其棺，果露而四际亦开，以杖拨之，但见败絮，是亦尸解矣。

    Explanation

    85

    For ten years or so, no one knew where he was. In the late period of the Tian Sheng era, there was a man named Zhao who lived in a branch residence in the town of Yizhou, Cizhou. Suddenly, a beggar came with a ragged coat and saw Zhao, bowing twice and saying, "I am De Guo, the stove operator." Zhao had also known him before, so he asked, "Have you seen Master?" De Guo replied, "I have not seen you around the world, now my life is coming to an end, so I have come to ask for a small coffin to bury my remains." Zhao considered it very unlikely and asked, "On what day will your life end?" De Guo said, "Tomorrow at noon." Zhao said, "If that is the case, I will buy a coffin for you." He then instructed, "Cut an opening at the head of the coffin, insert a bamboo pole through the joints and place it in the opening, so that it can breathe." Although Zhao agreed, he still did not believe it. The next day at noon, De Guo washed himself with water, lay down under a槐tree, and died. Zhao was greatly surprised, so he made a coffin for him. In the northern region, there was a lack of bamboo, so he took an old umbrella handle, hollowed it out, and inserted it into the head of the coffin. He buried it by the riverbank, and still feared that it might be dug up by foxes or dogs, so he planted thorns and piled stones to secure it. That autumn, there was a heavy rain, and the river water flooded, taking several days to recede. Zhao was worried that the coffin might be washed away by the water, so he went to check on it with his cane. Indeed, the coffin lid was open and the sides were also open. He poked it with his cane, and saw only some old rags, which indicated that De Guo had undergone a transformation of the body.

    ○牛用之
    　　道士牛用之，真定人，幼逮事常铁冠（常铁冠，邢州人，有道术，祥符中得召见），后隐泰山，复游天台，颇得考召符禁之术，自余杭游姑苏，落魄不事仪检，好饮酒啖葫蒜犬肉。或传其有道术者，人不之信。庆历中，薛公纯中舍监苏州市征，尝外嬖一官妓，其妻李氏性悍妒，不胜忿怒，谋害其夫，俟薛醉归，以刃贼其要害，家人救之获免。会李之父母过姑苏，闻之，俾其弟持药饮之而毙。即夕，为厉于薛氏，击户牖，碎器皿，或灭其灯烛，或啸于堂庑。遂召巫觋辟除之，不能去，不得已乃告。牛曰：“此细事，今夜可除之。

    Explanation

    Final Translation

    牛用之

    The Taoist priest Niuyongzhi was from Zhen Ding. In his youth, he served under Chang Tieguan (Chang Tieguan was from Xingzhou and possessed magical abilities; he was summoned by the emperor during the Xiangfu era). Later, Niuyongzhi retreated to Mount Tai and traveled again to the Tian Tai Mountains, where he learned a considerable amount of divination and exorcism techniques. He then traveled from Yuhang to Suzhou, living a life of debauchery and disregarding social norms. He enjoyed drinking, eating garlic, and consuming dog meat. Some people said he had magical abilities, but others did not believe it.

    During the Qingli era, Xue Gong Chun, a local official in Suzhou, had an official concubine. His wife, Li Shi, was fierce and jealous, unable to bear her anger, and plotted to harm her husband. She waited for Xue to return drunk, stabbed him in the vital parts, but family members saved him and he escaped unharmed. When Li's parents passed through Suzhou, they heard about the incident and had her brother give Xue poison to drink, which killed him. That night, the spirit of Xue began haunting the Xue family, striking the doors and windows, breaking utensils, sometimes extinguishing the lights, and sometimes howling in the hallways. The family then summoned shamans to exorcise the spirit, but they could not drive it away. Having no choice, they told Niuyongzhi. Niuyongzhi said, "This is a minor matter; I can get rid of it tonight."

    ”乃设酒馔于正寝，召数客共饮。既夕，牛设一案于下，上置铜铎，始乙夜铎忽鸣，沿案足而下，去地尺余，如人携持，鸣振而去，久乃不闻。牛曰：“俾追捕女厉耳。”逮四鼓，铎声自南来，俄顷入门，坐客如负冰雪，毛发尽植。牛乃取一榻，临案而坐，如有所诘。问曰：“汝谋杀夫，死实其分，得不弃市，乃大幸也，安得更为崇厉以扰其家”少选，又曰：“汝若不见听，吾当请帝锢汝于石室中，如止要冠珥襦之类，翌日当与汝。”遂丁宁诫励遣去。明日，遂具其所要洎楮镪数十万燔之城外，女厉自兹不至，牛后亦不知所在。郁林州推官崔迪，其夕与牛同饮于薛氏之馆，目睹斯事。

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    ○毕道人
    　　毕水部田，潭州人，有季父幼嗜酒不治生，尝游江湖间，衣弊褐，携一扇，怀袖间置沙数合，偶有所适，则藉地取沙，写风云草木、蛟龙禽兽之字，以扇扇之，殆尽乃欣然而去。尝有贾姓者过洞庭，方离岸，为暴风所漂，几至沉溺，忽见一人循岸以扇招之入舟，渐逼岸遂获免。贾德之，默记其形状，及舣舟寻之，不复见矣。旬日，贾到长沙，偶于见之，邀归酣饮，出金帛衣物为谢。毕曰：“汝舟免溺，余何力焉”固辞不受。强之，乃取衣服数事，旋以施贫者，一无所留，其后竟不知所在。

    Explanation

    88

    Bì Dào Rén
    Bì Shuǐbù Tián, a man from Tán Prefecture, had a younger brother who was a drunkard and did not manage his own life. He often traveled between the rivers and lakes, wearing tattered coarse clothing and carrying a fan. In his sleeves, he kept a few handfuls of sand. Occasionally when he went somewhere, he would lay down and take sand from the ground, writing characters of wind, clouds, grass, trees, dragons, and beasts, then using the fan to blow on it until it was almost gone, at which point he would happily leave.

    Once, a man surnamed Ji passed by Dongting Lake. As he was leaving the shore, he was swept away by a strong wind and nearly drowned. Suddenly, he saw a person by the shore waving a fan to invite him onto a boat. Gradually approaching the shore, he was saved. The man was grateful and silently remembered the person’s appearance. After mooring the boat, he searched for him, but he was no longer seen. Ten days later, the man arrived in Changsha and accidentally saw him at a tavern. He invited him to drink heartily and offered gold, silk, and clothes as a gift. Bì said, “Your boat was saved from sinking; what did I do?” He firmly refused to accept the gift. When pressured, he took a few items of clothing and quickly gave them to the poor, leaving nothing for himself. After that, his whereabouts were unknown.

    89

    ○段
    　　段者，许州人，累举进士，家丰于财，后忽如狂，日夕冠帻，衣布袍白银带，行游廛市中，讴吟云：“一间茅屋，尚自修治，信任风吹，连檐破碎，斗ㄆ邪歌，看看倒也。墙壁作散土一堆，主人永不来归。”遇其出入，则有闾巷小儿数十随而和焉，人以狂待之，不以为异。庆历末，病死，权厝于野，后数年营葬，发视，但空棺耳。
    　　○方道士
    　　方道士，失其名，不知何许人，隐于涂阳之西山。磁州有护国灵应公祠，每岁二三月，天下之事神者四集，所献奇禽异兽、巧工妙技、珍肴异果，无所不有。至期，邻郡之事人多会于祠下，游览宴聚，以至夏初社人罢去乃归。方道士无岁不来，常以九蒸黄菁以遗交旧，一岁忽不至，皆谓徙居他山，或以为物故。明年春，城隍庙神座后有死人，埃尘厚且寸余，官吏将检视，忽振衣而起，乃方道士也，复陪诸君酣饮月余乃去，自是不复来。

    Explanation

    89

    Final Translation

    Segment 1: Duan Su

    Duan Su was from Xuzhou. He repeatedly failed to pass the imperial examinations, but his family was wealthy. Later, he suddenly became as if mad, wearing a hat and headband day and night, and dressed in a coarse robe with a silver belt. He wandered through the markets, singing and reciting:
    "Even a thatched hut should be maintained,
    Trusting the wind to blow, the eaves will break.
    Singing a song of evil, it will collapse soon.
    The walls turn into a pile of loose earth,
    The owner will never return."
    Whenever he appeared, dozens of children from the neighborhood followed and echoed him. People regarded him as mad but did not find it unusual. At the end of the Qingli era, he died of illness and was temporarily buried in the wilderness. Several years later, when his tomb was opened for burial, there was only an empty coffin.

    Segment 2: The Taoist Priest Fang

    The Taoist priest Fang, whose name is unknown, was an enigmatic figure hidden in the West Mountain of Tuyang. In Cizhou, there is a temple dedicated to the National Guardian Spirit. Every year in February or March, people from all over the country gather to worship the spirit, bringing exotic birds and beasts, skilled artisans and their wondrous crafts, rare delicacies, and exotic fruits—nothing is lacking. By the time of the festival, people from neighboring prefectures often gather at the temple, touring and feasting, until early summer when the worshippers disperse and return home. The Taoist priest Fang came every year, often giving nine-steamed yellow chrysanthemum to his friends. One year, he suddenly did not come, and everyone speculated that he had moved to another mountain or had passed away. The following spring, a dead person was found behind the seat of the city god, with dust thick, more than an inch deep. Officials were about to inspect the situation when the dead person suddenly stood up and dressed, revealing himself to be the Taoist priest Fang. He then joined the guests in drinking for more than a month before leaving. From then on, he never came back.

    90

    ○高阆
    　　高阆，蜀人也，本姓向，名良少，为郡吏抵罪亡命，遂易姓名焉。虽眇一目，而神检高爽，善诗，来往江湖间，深得养生之术，饮酒至数斗不乱。许郎中申为江东转运使，每按部必拉之同行。尝舣舟贵池亭，有九华李山人者，与高有旧，因谒，许延之使饮，各尽二斗余，殊无醉态。高取钓竿，谓李曰：“各钓一鱼，以资语笑，然不得取蟹。”乃钩饵投坐前甓罅中。俄顷，李引一蟹出，高笑曰：“始约钓鱼，今果取蟹，可罚以酒也。”后死于滁之琅琊山僧寺，将终，以玉笛授僧曰：“此开元中宁王所吹者。”然不知是否时已几百岁矣。

    90

    Gao Lang, a native of Shu, originally surnamed Xiang and named Liangshao, was a county official who fled after committing a crime and thus changed his name. Although he had lost one eye, his spirit was high and noble. He was skilled in poetry and traveled among the rivers and lakes, deeply understanding the art of preserving life. He could drink several dou of wine without getting drunk. Xu Langzhong, who was appointed as the Transport Commissioner of Jiangdong, invited him, and whenever he inspected his jurisdiction, he would bring him along. Once, they moored their boat at the Guichi Pavilion, and there was a recluse from Jiuhua Mountain who had known Gao since before. Xu invited him to drink, and they each consumed more than two dou, showing no signs of intoxication. Gao took a fishing rod and said to Li, "Let's each catch a fish to provide amusement, but we cannot catch crabs." They then cast their lines into the gaps between the bricks in front of them. Soon, Li caught a crab. Gao laughed and said, "We started by agreeing to catch fish, but now you caught a crab. You should be punished with more wine." Later, he died in a temple on Langya Mountain in Chuzhou. As he was about to die, he gave a jade flute to the monk and said, "This was the jade flute blown by Prince Ning during the Kaiyuan period." However, it is uncertain whether it is truly from that time, as it has been hundreds of years.

    ○孙锴
    　　孙锴，不知何许人也，祥符末，尝读书于镇州西山之书院。一日，采药迷入深山，见茅茨数间，有道士据榻而坐。孙再拜问归路，道士俾坐，熟视曰：“穷薄人也，今既遇我，当使汝足于衣食。”既而与丹砂一块如拳，又授以一符，曰：“可以召鬼。”及教以符传，谓曰：“今岁河朔大疫，汝以此砂书符售之，一符止取百钱，不可过也；召鬼之符，止可一用，盖救汝之祸也，再用则不灵，汝其志之。”既出山，鬻符于市，果能愈疾。锴遂市一牛骑之，戴铁冠，披绛服，流转至大名府。时太尉王公嗣宗守魏，擒而械于狱，将以妖诞惑众，黥配之。锴谓狱官曰：“锴非造妖者，间遇神人见教耳，乞乘间白之，言锴能令人见鬼及其祖先。”王闻之乃曰：“昔刘根尝有此术。”命释缚试之，果然。遂送阙下补司天监保章正，专主符禁事。后砂尽术衰，遂逃去。宝元中，尝诏天下捕之。

    Explanation

    91

    孙锴，他的出身不详，在祥符末年，曾在镇州西山的书院读书。有一天，他采药时迷失在深山中，看到几间茅草屋，里面有一位道士坐在榻上。孙锴再次拜见，询问归途，道士让他坐下，仔细看了看他说：“你是个贫穷卑微的人，既然遇到了我，我会让你衣食无忧。”随后，道士给了他一块拳头大小的丹砂，又给了他一个符咒，说：“这可以用来召唤鬼魂。”接着，道士教给他使用符咒的方法，并告诉他：“今年河朔地区大疫流行，你可以用这些丹砂书写符咒出售，每张符只收一百钱，不能多收；召唤鬼魂的符咒只能用一次，因为这是为了救你的命，如果再用就不灵了，你要记住这一点。”孙锴离开山中后，在市场上卖符咒，果然能够治病。于是，孙锴买了一头牛骑着它，戴着铁冠，穿着红袍，四处游荡到了大名府。当时，太尉王嗣宗镇守魏地，将孙锴逮捕并关入监狱，准备以妖言惑众的罪名对他进行黥面流放。孙锴对狱官说：“我不是制造妖术的人，只是偶然遇到了神人，得到了他的教导，请您找个机会向王公说明，说我能够让人看到鬼魂及其祖先。”王嗣宗听说后说：“过去刘根也有这样的法术。”于是命令释放孙锴的束缚，测试他的能力，结果果然有效。于是，孙锴被送往京城，补任司天监保章正，专门负责符禁之事。后来，丹砂用尽，法术衰退，孙锴便逃走了。宝元年间，朝廷曾下令天下捉拿他。

    ○杨贯
    　　杨贯，开封府宁陵县人也，尝两举进士不预荐送，即改业明法。人或笑之，曰：“我诵法令，苟得入仕，则官业己精熟矣。”一夕，梦五色光来自西南，入寝室，光中有一道士，叱贯令起，谓之曰：“汝逮今三为人矣。始为屠，次为人女，既笄而自缢，今乃得为士人尔。顶有戴笄，颈有投缳之痕尚在，可视也。”贯曰：“人之肤理万状，安可便以屠者洎女子相诬乎”道士曰：“尔以为不然耶”遂怀中探一鉴，令视之，则鼓刀施朱之状宛然。贯即再拜谢，又乞谕向去休咎，道士曰：“尔寿过中年，官至令。”既寤，而大异之。明年遂得明法出身，治平二年，调邛州录事参军。今沆州推官吕昭吉，时任司冠，屡与之饮，数爵之后，则颈上绠迹甚明。询其故，贯具言梦之本末。及披发，见肉胝圆五六寸，若窭数然。年逾五十，授潞州潞城县令，到任而终。

    Explanation

    92

    Yang Guan, a native of Ningling County, Kaifeng Prefecture, once failed to be recommended twice for the jinshi examination, and thus changed his career to study legal matters. Some people laughed at him, saying, "I recite legal codes, and if I can enter officialdom, my duties will already be well-versed." One night, he dreamed of a five-colored light coming from the southwest, entering his bedroom. In the light, there was a Taoist priest who shouted at Guan to get up and said to him, "You have been reborn three times. First as a butcher, then as a woman, who hanged herself after reaching adulthood, and now you have become a scholar. You still have the mark of a hairpin on your head and the scar of a hanging on your neck, which can be seen." Guan said, "Human skin has countless variations, how can one simply accuse me of being a butcher or a woman?" The Taoist priest said, "Do you think this is not true?" He then took a mirror from his chest and made Guan look into it, revealing the image of a butcher wielding a knife and applying rouge. Guan immediately bowed twice and thanked him, then asked for a prediction of his future fortune. The Taoist priest said, "You will live past middle age and become a magistrate." After waking up, he was greatly astonished. The following year, he passed the legal examination and was appointed as a recorder in Qiong Prefecture in the second year of Zhiping. Now, Judge Lü Zhaoji of Hanghai Prefecture, who was serving as a magistrate at the time, often drank with him. After several cups, the marks of the hanging on his neck became very clear. When asked about it, Guan explained the details of his dream. Upon parting his hair, he saw a round lump of flesh about five or six inches in diameter, resembling a few knots. He was appointed as the magistrate of Lucheng County in Lü Prefecture when he was over fifty and died upon taking office.

    ○张酒酒
    　　道士张酒酒，失其名，不知何许人。天圣中，主西都张水县之天禧观，善淬，鉴经其手，则光照洞澈，他工不可及。或时童稚持鉴来治者，遇醉则或抵破之，或引之长三尺。小儿惊呼，乃笑曰：“吾与若戏。”乃取药傅其上，以败毡覆之，摩拭良久，清莹如故。得钱唯买酒，未尝一日不醉。一旦，拂衣入王屋山，立而尸解于药柜山中。始村人见有人立于岩石之上，久而不去，经旬往视之，故在，遂闻于乡。啬夫就而察之，乃一道士拱立且僵也，啬夫以为不祥，推仆之。邑尉检视，顶有一窍如鸡卵大，殊无血渍，面色如生。尉闻啬夫推仆，鞭之，即瘗放于解化之地。

    93

    The Taoist Zhang Jiujiu, whose name is unknown and whose origins are also unknown, was in charge of the Tianxi Temple in Zhangshui County, Western Capital, during the Tian Sheng era. He was skilled in polishing mirrors, and those polished by his hands would shine brightly and clearly, a quality unmatched by others. Sometimes, children would bring mirrors to him for polishing, and when he was drunk, he would sometimes break them or stretch them to three feet long. The children would cry out in surprise, and he would laugh and say, "I am playing with you." Then he would take medicine and apply it to the surface, cover it with a worn-out mat, rub and polish it for a long time, and it would become as clear and bright as before. He would only use the money to buy alcohol and never went a day without being drunk. One day, he put on his robe and entered Wangwu Mountain, where he stood and underwent a transformation in the mountain of the medicine cabinet. At first, villagers saw someone standing on a rock, and he stayed there for a long time. After ten days, they went to see him, and he was still there, and the news spread in the village. The village official went to examine him and found that he was a Taoist standing with his hands clasped and stiff. The village official thought it was unlucky and pushed him down. The county magistrate examined him and found that there was a hole on his head as big as an egg, with no blood on it, and his face was as fresh as if he were alive. The county magistrate heard that the village official had pushed him down and whipped him, and immediately buried him in the place of his transformation.

    Chapter 8
    The Minister of State Hao

    Minister Hao of the Ming Dynasty was a man of broad and agile intellect and character, highly talented and well-versed in learning. He passed the imperial examination as a Jinshi and served in the central government, holding several high-ranking offices. During the middle period of the Qingli era, he rose from the position of Prefect of the capital to participate in major state affairs. Soon after, he developed a severe boil on his back and sent an envoy to offer a sacrifice at Mount Tai, seeking divine protection. The envoy rushed to the temple, completed the sacrifice, and stayed at the temple that night. While sleeping, he had a terrible nightmare, and his attendants woke him up. He said, "I dreamed that a deity called me to stand in the courtyard of the hall. I saw over a hundred people surrounding someone wearing shackles. Upon closer inspection, it was the Minister of State. They then beat his back twenty times and drove me out. I could not help but cry out." He then rode back in haste. The Minister was already seriously ill and summoned the envoy to ask, "What did you see in your dream during the sacrifice?" The envoy described everything he saw. The Minister said, "Yes."

    95

    ”又云：明始病数日，即似荒乱，有郎官某人，乃明之同年进士，素相厚善，明俾召至，谓曰：“何以不来相视”郎官曰：“比为参政，暂请服药假，不意实抱疾耳。”明曰：“曾见无头鬼语否”郎官大骇曰：“岂未朝餐乎”曰：“已食矣。”又曰：“岂未饵汤剂乎”曰：“已屡进矣。”曰：“然则斯言何谓也”明曰：“召同年正欲说此事。”又曰：“来矣，可听之。”郎官使闻，如游蜂苍蝇鸣地下，明曰：“语乃胸中出。向者妖贼据甘陵，奉朝命攻讨。外围既固，攻具备设，平在旦夕，不意文相国来抚师，将坐而收功，心实忿之，遂妄杀数人，今实称冤于我。病其不起乎”数日遂卒。夫为将三世，道家所忌，谓攻城野战，玉石难分耳。明以己之私忿杀无罪者，宜乎见厉于垂死，嗣续汩而不振也。

    Explanation

    95

    Ming began to be ill for several days, and immediately seemed disoriented. There was a certain official from the same year of the imperial examination as Ming, who had always been close friends with him. Ming ordered him to be summoned and said to him, "Why haven't you come to visit?" The official replied, "Recently, I served as a vice-minister and temporarily requested leave to take medicine. I did not expect to actually fall ill." Ming asked, "Have you seen the ghost without a head speak?" The official was greatly startled and said, "Have you not had breakfast yet?" Ming replied, "I have already eaten." The official then asked, "Have you not taken any medicine?" Ming said, "I have taken it several times already." The official asked, "Then what do these words mean?" Ming said, "I summoned my colleague to discuss this matter." The official came and listened. Ming said, "The words come from within my chest. Previously, the bandits occupied Ganling, and following the imperial command, we were to attack. The outer defenses were already strong, and the attack preparations were in place. Victory was imminent. Unexpectantly, Wen Xiangguo came to pacify the troops, and was about to sit back and take credit for the victory. My heart was truly filled with resentment, so I mistakenly killed several people. Now they are truly calling out in my name. Will the illness not resolve?" Several days later, Ming died. Serving as a general for three generations is something that Daoists avoid, meaning that in attacking cities and fighting in the wild, it is difficult to distinguish between the good and the bad. Ming killed innocent people out of personal resentment, and it is appropriate that he be punished even in his dying moments, and his descendants will be in turmoil and unable to recover.

    ○徐学士
    　　熙宁中，徐学士禧始受职，官中书习学公事，自豫章侍亲之阙下。舟行次彭蠡湖，昧爽而行，期早抵南康军。俄而水面白雾四起，始虑风作，促舟人疾棹。未四五里，雾稍开，见二朱漆万斛巨舰，旌旗赫奕，摇橹者肃而不哗，相去百余丈，东南而逝。未二三里又见朱舰，间以金碧幡旆，尤鲜华，亦相踵而去。少时，又逢二白舰，载甲士数千，戈戟森列，尾三舟而行。徐之舟人既见，俯不敢正视。然望其船远而益小，洎抵他岸，皆若一履。宫庭湖庙，水经具载其灵。近传有小龙者多出处其中，岂其灵变耶

    Explanation

    96

    Translation:

    During the Xining era, Xu Xue Shi, a scholar-official, began his duties in the Office of the Secretariat, learning official affairs, and traveled from Yuzhang to attend to his parents in the capital. As he sailed along Poyang Lake, he set out at dawn, hoping to arrive early at Nankang Commandery. Soon after, white mist began to rise all around the water surface, and he started to worry about the wind starting. He urged the boatman to row quickly. After not more than four or five miles, the fog began to lift, and he saw two large ships painted red, each holding ten thousand dou, with banners and flags flying brightly. The rowers were solemn and silent, separated by about a hundred zhang, heading southeast and disappearing. After not more than two or three miles, another red-painted ship was seen, interspersed with golden and green banners and flags, especially bright and splendid, also following one another and disappearing. A short while later, he encountered two white-painted ships, carrying several thousand armored soldiers, with spears and halberds arranged in a dense formation, following the three boats. Xu’s boatman, upon seeing these ships, bent down and did not dare to look straight. However, looking at the ships, they became smaller as they moved further away, and when they reached the other shore, all seemed like a single footprint. The palaces, temples, and shrines along the lake are recorded in the Shui Jing (Water Classic) as having spiritual significance. Recently, it is said that many small dragons often appear there. Is this due to its spiritual transformation?

    ○鱼中丞
    　　中丞鱼公周询，天圣四年第进士甲等，初命大理评事，知济州金乡县。尝昼卧书阁中，有守阁老卒入白事，但见乌蛇蟠于榻，矫首冠帻，叱声甚厉。卒走出呼侍吏共视之，乃见熟寝未寤。后至御史中丞而卒。
    　　○祖龙图
    　　祖龙图无择，始登第，ヘ通齐州。岁余，得告归蔡州营葬，事毕复任。后春季，检视官物于禹城县，过石河滩沙中，得片石，上有数十字，乃葬其先君之志也。遣人视坟垄，无一А之缺，竟不测其所从来。

    Fish Censor-in-Chancellor

    The Censor-in-Chancellor, Fish Gong Zhou Xun, was among the top-ranking Jinshi (imperial scholars) in the Tian Sheng fourth year (1026 AD). He was initially appointed as a Judicial Officer of the Imperial Court of Justice and served as the magistrate of Jinxiang County in Jizhou. Once, while napping in the book pavilion during the day, a guard at the pavilion entered to report an urgent matter. He saw a black snake coiled on the bed, its head raised as if wearing a cap, and he shouted loudly to drive it away. The guard ran out and called for the servants to come and see. They found Fish Gong Zhou Xun deeply asleep and not yet awake. Later, he rose to the position of Censor-in-Chancellor and passed away.

    Ancestor Lord Wu

    Ancestor Lord Wu Wu Ze, after passing the imperial examination, was appointed as the governor of Qizhou. After more than a year, he received permission to return to Pizhou for the purpose of burying his ancestors. After completing the burial, he resumed his duties. In the following spring, while inspecting official property in Yucheng County, he passed through a sandy area along the Stone River and found a small stone with several dozen characters inscribed on it. The stone turned out to be a memorial to his deceased father. He sent someone to check the tomb, which showed no signs of disturbance, and the origin of the stone remained unknown.

    ○尚寺丞
    　　司勋外郎尚公霖，祥符末以殿中丞知夔州巫山县。有尉李某者，山东人，颇干敏，一旦疾病。尚闻其委顿，日往临问，曰：“万一不起，可以后事告也。”尉曰：“愿以老母幼女为托，公倘垂仁恻，某虽死，敢忘结草之义乎”尚泫然愍之。既死，出俸钱送其母及骨函还乡里，嫁其女于士族。一夕，梦李如平昔，拜且泣曰：“某恳求于阴官，今得为公之子，以此为谢耳。”是月，邑君妊娠。明年解官，沿流赴关，或遇滩险，隐约见尉在岸上指呼。将抵荆渚，又梦李报曰：“某明日当生，府中必送一合来，宜收之。”翌日，果诞一男子，府尹以合贮粟米遗尚，曰：“闻邑君育子，以为糜粥之具。”因字颖，曰合儿。颖性纯厚，敏于行而笃于学，官至大理丞。

    The Chief Justice Shang Gong Lin

    Shang Gong Lin, an Outer Lang of the Imperial Stables, was appointed as the magistrate of Wushan County in Kui Prefecture at the end of the Xiangfu era. There was a county officer named Li, who was from Shandong and was very capable and intelligent. One day, he fell ill. Shang Gong Lin heard of his condition and visited him daily, saying, "If you cannot recover, you may tell me your final wishes." The officer replied, "I wish to entrust my elderly mother and young daughter to you. If you show compassion, I will never forget the debt of gratitude, even if I die." Shang Gong Lin shed tears out of compassion for him. After the officer's death, Shang Gong Lin used his salary to send the officer's mother and his coffin back to their hometown and arranged for his daughter to marry into a noble family. One night, Shang Gong Lin dreamed of Li as he had been before, bowing and weeping, saying, "I have pleaded with the officials of the underworld, and now I can be your son. This is my way of thanking you." That month, Shang Gong Lin's wife became pregnant. The following year, he resigned from his post and traveled along the river to the pass. Sometimes, he encountered dangerous rapids, and he faintly saw the officer on the shore pointing and calling out. As they approached Jingzhou, Shang Gong Lin dreamed again, and Li reported, "I will be born tomorrow, and the governor's office will send a container. You should receive it." The next day, a boy was indeed born, and the governor sent a container filled with rice to Shang Gong Lin, saying, "I heard that your wife has given birth to a son, so this is for making porridge." They named the child Ying, calling him He'er. Ying was pure and kind-hearted, quick in action and diligent in learning, and he eventually became a Chief Justice.

    ○高舜臣
    　　大名府进士高舜臣尝言：其从兄祥符中为衙校，董卒数百人伐木于西山。一日，入山督役迷路，闻乐声合作于山谷间，寻声视之，见妇人数十，衣服华丽，执笙竽会饮于石上。居席首者召高坐其侧，亦及以酒肴，谓曰：“吾欲妇汝，何如”高但愧谢。又曰：“汝今归寨中，吾将继至。”是夜果往，高亦恍然不测。自此遇夜即至，室中帐枕褥之具备设，晓复失之，若此者逮一月。役兵取材既毕，与高同归。高之父母闻之，大惊曰：“此子为石妖木魅所惑也。”因即东庑而居，家人视之，则装寝之具、冠衣之类悉已张陈。

    Explanation

    99

    High Shunchen, a scholar from Daming Prefecture, once said: His older brother, during the Xiangfu era, served as an official in charge of a group of soldiers who were cutting down trees in the Western Hills. One day, while he was in the mountains overseeing the work, he lost his way and heard the sound of music playing harmoniously in the valleys. Following the sound, he saw several women dressed in beautiful clothes, playing musical instruments, and drinking together on a flat stone. The woman sitting at the head of the seat invited him to sit beside her and also offered him food and drink. She said, "I want to marry you, what do you think?" High Shunchen felt ashamed and apologized. She then said, "You should return to the camp now, and I will come later." That night, she indeed came, and high Shunchen felt dazed and confused. From then on, she came every night, and the room was prepared with bedding and other necessities, but he would lose consciousness in the morning. This continued for about a month. After the soldiers had completed their task, they returned together with high Shunchen. When high Shunchen's parents heard about this, they were shocked and said, "This son has been bewitched by a rock demon or tree spirit." Therefore, they moved to live in an eastern hall. When family members visited him, they found that the preparations for sleep, including bedding and personal attire, were all set up.

    100

    高氏家人亦罕见其面，或见其冠，或见其裙襦而已。家属相与忧惧，虑久而致礻周，乃召巫觋，具符水禳诅之术。女子笑谓高曰：“我岂妖怪害人者何见疑之深也”俨然殊不顾，高氏家亦无奈之何。居半岁，高氏会客烹牛为馔，女子见而大骇曰：“我以君积善之家，故愿奉巾栉于子，亦将福汝家，不意暴恶之如是。君家固不当留，亟送我归也。”高白其父母，闻而大喜，立俾其子送之，去西山数舍。其夜不至，高亦不敢复前，但望山怅恨而归。高氏子竟亦无恙。大名进士陈伦因言神怪而及之，亦未以为信。治平初，予为大名铃兵，进士王詹亦道其事，与陈说正同。舜臣后以累举推恩得州长史。

    Explanation

    100

    The family of Gao rarely saw her face, sometimes catching a glimpse of her headdress, sometimes her skirt and blouse. The family was filled with fear and anxiety, fearing that it might lead to harm, and so they summoned sorcerers and prepared talismans, water, and exorcism rituals. The girl smiled and told Gao, "Am I a harmful spirit? Why are you so suspicious of me?" She remained indifferent and paid no heed, and the Gao family could do nothing about it. After half a year, the Gao family prepared a feast with roasted ox meat. The girl was greatly shocked and said, "I thought your family had accumulated good deeds, so I wanted to serve you and bring blessings to your family. I did not expect such cruelty. Your family should not keep me; quickly send me back." Gao informed his parents, who were greatly pleased to hear this and immediately sent their son to escort her to a place several villages away from the Western Mountains. That night, she did not arrive, and Gao also dared not proceed further, only looking at the mountains, filled with regret, and returning. Gao's son eventually returned unharmed. The Jinshi Chen Lun of Daming mentioned the supernatural and referred to this incident, but he did not believe it. In the early years of Zhiping, I was the military officer of Daming, and the Jinshi Wang Zhan also recounted this story, which was the same as what Chen had said. After being repeatedly recommended, Shunchen was granted the position of State Historian.

    ○ Wang Qing
    　　Wang Qing, the Deputy of Various Departments, was appointed to govern Fengzhou during the reign of Emperor Renzong (1022-1063 AD). He was stern and violent, harsh and lacking in kindness. One day while attending to official duties, he suddenly felt a severe headache that was unbearable. Touching his head, he discovered that he had grown two horns, each about two inches long. After several days, he screamed and died. There was also a person named Li Zhen, who passed the imperial examination as a Jinshi at the beginning of the reign of Emperor Zhenzong (997-1022 AD). He was reckless and undisciplined. The Inspectorate Judge of Xing Prefecture died of an epidemic disease. After his burial, his hair on the top of his head looked like pearls, and he had two horns over an inch long.

    　　○ Sun Hanlin
    　　During the reign of Emperor Renzong (1041-1048 AD), Yang Neihan Wei, the Prefect of Jun Prefecture, was sitting in his hall when he saw an old woman with disheveled hair and tattered clothes. She directly entered the inner chambers, and he asked where she was going, but she did not respond. After a while, she came out again and said, "The young master sent me. The old servant dared not act on her own." Yang immediately called the attendants to chase her away, and as soon as she left the inner chambers, she disappeared. He then called his wife to question her, and she said, "The old woman said that the young master wanted to have a banquet in the wife's room tomorrow. Just as I was scolding her for lying, she immediately left." The whole family was shocked. The next day, the house was filled with thick fog, especially in the inner chambers. The fog burned and stung the mouth and nose, making it impossible to approach, and the doors could not be opened. After a long time, they heard sounds of conversation, laughter, music, and flute playing. From morning till evening, the fog gradually cleared. They pushed open the door and entered, asking what had happened. She said, "There was a young man who drank with me. The utensils were precious and beautiful, the banquet was splendid, and the food, drink, and music were all exquisite."

    我亦忘身为杨氏妇也。”然精神颇亦失常。即召刘捉鬼者禁劾之，不能已。闻翰林孙郎中专主符禁，亟俾视之，曰：“此鬼庙在东南三十里，将为神矣，何敢为如此事”遂书二符致妇寝室之门，又曰：“知某今日到宅，明日定不来，更一日必至，宜令其夫洎女使二三人守之。鬼若不得入妇室，当变怪于外，盖欲诱之出也，出则不可治矣。”越一日果至，虽昏雾如初，独不入子舍。俄而郡封中恶，妇欲奔视，制之不得出，少时雾气解散，郡封亦复故。孙乃与杨公假静宅作坛奏章，自兹不复来，孙云已囚海上石室矣。

    ○黄遵
    　　黄遵者，家兴国军，性疏放，颇知书而能丹青，善传人之形神，曲尽其妙。事母笃孝，凡得画值未尝私蓄，供甘旨外，悉归于母。庆历中，遵忽感疾而死，凡三日心尚暖，母不敢敛。是夕遵复苏，家人扶坐，问皆不语，遽索纸，笔图一人形容，良久乃语：始入一公府，见廊庑肃静，皆垂帘，阍吏通曰：“兴国军黄遵今追到。”有吏问遵曰：“尔黄遵耶”遵曰：“唯。”前谓吏曰：“遵未尝有过，何以见速”吏曰：“尔算尽乃至此。”遵方知身死，遂号泣，拜曰：“母老无兄弟，乞终母寿。”吏曰：“此不敢与闻。”遵拜泣不已，吏哀其诚，乃曰：“俟主者来，若自告之。”移刻两庑吏喧然，曰：“至矣。”一吏升堂轴帘，东北隅有户洞开，朱吏数人前导，见一人紫衣金带者升堂坐。

    Huang Zun

    Huang Zun was a native of Xingguo Jun, known for his unrestrained and free-spirited nature. He was well-versed in literature and skilled in painting, particularly adept at capturing the form and spirit of people, fully expressing their subtleties. He was deeply filial to his mother, never keeping any money earned from his paintings for himself, but instead using it to provide food and drink for her, and any surplus he gave to her. During the reign of Emperor Renzong of Song, Huang Zun suddenly fell ill and died. For three days after his death, his heart was still warm, and his mother dared not prepare his body for burial. On that night, Huang Zun revived, and his family helped him sit up. When asked, he did not speak, but immediately asked for paper and began to draw a person's likeness. After a long time, he spoke: "I first entered a public office, where I saw the hallways and corridors quiet, with all curtains hanging. The gatekeeper announced, 'Huang Zun of Xingguo Jun is now being summoned.'" An official asked, "Are you Huang Zun?" He replied, "Yes." He then said to the official, "I have never committed any wrong, why am I being summoned so quickly?" The official replied, "Your life span has ended, so you have come here." Huang Zun realized he was dead and began to weep, bowing and saying, "My mother is old and I have no brothers; I ask to live out her remaining years." The official said, "This is not within my power to grant." Huang Zun continued to bow and weep, and the official, moved by his sincerity, said, "Wait for the chief official to arrive, and I will inform him of your request." After a short while, the officials in the side halls exclaimed, "He has arrived!" One official ascended the hall, drew the curtains, and opened a door in the northeast corner. Several officials in red robes led the way, and they saw a high-ranking official in purple robes and a gold belt ascend the hall and sit.

    104

    诸吏仅百人列阶下，致恭毕，分入诸局。始见领数十人荷校者、露首者，至紫衣前，讯讫，驱出。已而呼遵，问里姓名，遵号恸叩头，拜曰：“念母老无兄弟，遵若死，母必饿殍，乞终母寿。”遵叩阶，额血溅地。紫衣顾左右索籍视之，久乃谓曰：“汝母寿尚有十余年，念尔至孝，许终母寿。”紫衣以笔注其籍，命左右速奏覆。遵拜而出，复呼之，命俯阶，问曰：“汝在人间，与人传神者是乎”遵曰：“愚昧无能，仅成其形耳。”又曰：“尔识我否”遵曰：“凡目岂识神仪”曰：“我乃人间所谓崔府君也。尔熟视吾貌，归人间写之，然慎勿多传，若所传惟肖恐人间祭祀不常，返昏吾虚，记之勿忘。”自后遵在兴国凡所写者三本，正一画于地藏院，二为好事者所取。厥后十年，母以寿终，既葬服除，遵一日遍辞亲识，因大醉数日而卒。

    104

    A hundred officials lined up at the bottom of the steps, paid their respects, and then entered their respective bureaus. At first, dozens of people with shackles and bare heads were seen. They were brought before the purple-clad official, questioned, and then driven out. Afterward, he called out to Zun and asked for the names of the village officials. Zun wept bitterly, knelt, and bowed, saying, "Thinking of my old mother who has no brothers, if I die, my mother will surely starve to death. I beg to live out my mother's remaining years." Zun knelt at the bottom of the steps, and his forehead bled onto the ground. The purple-clad official turned to his attendants to look up the records. After a long while, he said, "Your mother's lifespan still has more than ten years left. Considering your filial piety, I allow you to live out your mother's remaining years." The purple-clad official made a note in the records and ordered his attendants to quickly report back. Zun bowed and left, but was called back. He ordered Zun to kneel at the bottom of the steps and asked, "Are you the one who transmits divine images in the human world?" Zun replied, "I am foolish and incapable, only able to create the form." The official then asked, "Do you recognize me?" Zun said, "How could ordinary eyes recognize the divine appearance?" The official replied, "I am the fabled Cui Fu Jun in the human world. Look closely at my appearance and when you return to the human world, depict it. But be careful not to spread it widely. If it is depicted too accurately, the sacrifices in the human world may become irregular, causing my spirit to be forgotten. Remember this and do not forget." Afterward, Zun wrote three copies in Xingguo. One was drawn at the Dizang Temple, and two were taken by well-meaning people. Ten years later, his mother passed away at the end of her life. After the burial and the mourning period ended, one day Zun bid farewell to all his relatives and acquaintances. He then drank himself to death over several days.

    105

    ○刘德妙
    　　宝元中，夏英公为陕西路安抚招讨使，驻兵。尝与僚属言：向自知制诰出守安陆郡，有羁管妇人刘德妙言事颇中，因呼而问之：“尔有何能为丁晋公所知”刘曰：“某本捧日军之营妇也。尝出诣亲家，憩于汴上柳荫，忽一人巾帻紫袍，就己而坐，云是扶沟县隶事，有事之府，溺水而死，诉于阴官，俾我复生，至则身已坏，然尚得处于阳间，今欲凭附于汝。我能知人未萌之休咎，言既验，人必以愍谢，汝若事我，以此为报。

    Explanation

    105

    In the second year of the Baoyuan era, Xiao Yanyan, the Marquis of Xia, served as the Governor and Military Commander of Shaanxi, with his troops stationed in Yan and Jiao. He once spoke to his subordinates: "Previously, as a censor, I was appointed to govern Anlu Prefecture. There was a woman under supervision named Liu Dezhao, whose predictions were often accurate. I called her to ask, 'What skills or abilities made you known to Ding Wenjie?' She replied, 'I was originally a camp woman of the Pounding Army. Once, I visited my in-laws and rested under the willow shade by the Bian River. Suddenly, a man in a hat and purple robe sat beside me, saying he was an official from Fugou County who drowned and died, complained to the underworld officials, and was ordered to be reborn. When he returned, his body was already ruined, but he still lived in the world of the living. Now, he wants to rely on me. I can predict the good and bad fortunes before they manifest. When my predictions prove true, people will certainly show compassion and gratitude. If you serve me, I will reward you with this knowledge.'"

    106

    某惧不敢答，洎归，鬼亦随至，他人不见也。夫亦不信，则夫妇皆若寒热，呕泄不得已。事始，则火伍中人来，占事悉验，俄而里巷皆知，既而公卿之家呼召相继。晋公不欲营妇出入卿相之门，遂度为女冠。丁公南迁，某亦连坐编致斯郡，实无他术，但萌于心，则鬼知之。”夏曰：“吾心有一事，尔知之否”刘曰：“知之，但乞先书而糊其外，方敢言也。”某是时苦家贫，干执政求知益州，遂屏左右，书毕封置于案，刘言如所书，仍云：“事亦不谐。”既而果然。予榷酒于阴，具闻其说。
    　　○税道士

    Explanation

    106

    I was afraid and dared not answer. Upon returning home, the ghost also followed, but others did not see it. The man also did not believe, and as a result, both husband and wife suffered from chills and fever, vomiting and diarrhea, unable to help it. When the matter began, people from the fire brigade came, and all predictions were verified. Soon, everyone in the neighborhood knew, and later, the families of high officials called for them one after another. Duke Jin did not want his wife to enter the gates of high officials, so he had her become a nun. Duke Ding was exiled to the south, and I was also implicated and exiled to this prefecture. In truth, I had no other skills, but if something was conceived in my heart, the ghost knew it. "Summer said, 'I have something in my mind, do you know it?' Liu replied, 'I know it, but I ask you to write it down first and cover it up before I dare to speak.' At that time, I was struggling with poverty and approached the ruling authorities to request knowledge of Yizhou. So I dismissed the attendants, wrote it down, sealed it, and placed it on the table. Liu spoke as written, and still said, 'The matter will not go well.' And indeed, it turned out that way. I was in charge of wine taxation in Yinxian and heard the whole story.

    107

    景中，利州道士税其善妖幻洎符禁之术。利之富民或有所求不与者，即为坛于密室，置大桶于前，被发仗剑，追其鬼神入桶，覆之以石，其人乃病。然后假以符水或祠醮，谢以财，乃去石遣之，其人遂愈。市井有鬻笼饼洎诸肉者，求之即愈，不尔遂化为白鸽飞去，或即虫出，利人皆神而畏之。尝怒一僧，遇野外作法叱之。僧足如植，手亦不能举，恣行鞭。僧密讼于官，命贼曹擒捕，先沃以犬彘之血，术无所施，狱具遂斩于市。
    　　○寇莱公
    　　寇忠愍初登第，授大理评事，知归州巴东县。时唐郎中渭方为郡，夕梦有告云：“宰相至。”唐思之，不闻有宰相出镇者，晨兴视事，而疆吏报寇延评入界，唐公惊愕，出郡迓劳，见其风神秀伟，便以公辅待之，仍出诸子罗拜。唐新饬鞯勺致厅之左，寇既归，其子拯白其父曰：“适者寇屡目此，宜即送之。”寇果询牙校：“何人知我欲此”遂对以十四秀才，既而力为延誉。拯于孙汉公榜等甲成名。

    Explanation

    107

    During the Jingyou era, a Taoist priest in Lichou Prefecture was skilled in magic and exorcism. Wealthy commoners in Li Prefecture who did not grant his requests would have him set up a shrine in a secret room, placing a large bucket in front, with his hair loose and a sword in hand, summoning ghosts and deities into the bucket and covering it with stones, causing the person to fall ill. He would then use talismanic water or perform rituals, demanding payment, and remove the stones to release the person, who would then recover. In the marketplace, those selling steamed buns and various meats would be healed if they were sought after; otherwise, they would transform into white doves and fly away, or insects would emerge. People in Li Prefecture all revered and feared him. Once, he became angry with a monk and confronted him in the wilderness, using his magic to shout at him. The monk's feet were rooted to the ground, and he could not lift his hands, allowing the Taoist to freely whip him. The monk secretly reported to the authorities, who ordered the local officials to capture him. They first washed him with dog and pig blood, rendering his magic ineffective, and the case was finalized, leading to his beheading in the marketplace.

    ○ Kou Zhun

    Kou Zhun, posthumously honored as the Duke Zhongmin, initially passed the imperial examinations and was appointed as a Judicial Censor, serving as the magistrate of Badong County in Guizhou Prefecture. At the time, Tang Lanchong, a Tang Dynasty official, was serving as the prefect of the region. One night, Tang had a dream in which someone told him, "The Prime Minister has arrived." Tang pondered this, as he had not heard of any prime minister being sent to govern the region. In the morning, he went to work and was informed by the border officials that Kou Zhun had entered the area. Tang was startled and went out to welcome and entertain him. Seeing Kou's noble and impressive appearance, Tang treated him as a high-ranking official and had his sons bow in a row. Tang had recently prepared saddles and horse equipment and placed them to the left of his hall. After Kou returned, his son, Kou Zheng, told his father, "The person we saw earlier kept looking at these saddles and horse equipment; it would be best to send them to him immediately." Kou indeed inquired of the military officers, "Who knows that I want these?" They replied that they were the fourteen talented scholars, and Kou then strongly promoted their reputation. Kou Zheng passed the imperial examination and achieved a high rank under the list of successful candidates named after Sun Han Gong.

    108

    ○魏进士
    　　建州进士魏某者，富有词学，履行温愍，家亦颇丰。天圣中，屡寇乡书。既预计偕，梦一衣绯衣人，命徒执之弃市，始谓必捷科第，既而不利于春闱，凡三举皆然。后归乡闾，有邻里少年对语不逊，因掌之，即仆地死，警卒捕送于官。时裴郎中守是郡，闻其学行为众所推，欲法脱之，阖郡官吏亦为之言。而魏白郡守曰：“某杀人偿死，职也。安敢仰累明公某三预荐书，必梦绯衣人，命徒执赴市就刑。今明公姓裴，乃绯衣也。某邂逅一掌，致人于死，市死乃前定也。”将刑，一郡士庶无不为之嗟惜。

    Explanation

    108

    A Scholar-Official from Jianzhou

    There was a scholar-official named Wei from Jianzhou, who was highly talented in literature, known for his warm and compassionate conduct, and whose family was also relatively wealthy. During the Tian Sheng period, he frequently failed in the local examinations. He had been expected to succeed, but in a dream, he saw a person dressed in red official robes, ordering the executioner to take him to the market for public execution. Initially, he believed he would surely pass the imperial examinations, but he was unsuccessful in the spring metropolitan examination, and this happened three times in a row. After returning to his hometown, he encountered a young neighbor who spoke disrespectfully to him. In response, Wei struck the youth, who immediately fell to the ground and died. The patrol soldiers arrested Wei and sent him to the authorities. At that time, Pei Langzhong, the prefect of the region, heard that Wei was highly regarded for his scholarship and conduct and wanted to find a way to release him. All the officials in the region also spoke on his behalf. Wei then reported to the prefect, saying, "I killed someone and deserve to die. How dare I burden the honorable official? I was recommended three times for the examination and always dreamed of a person in red robes, ordering the executioner to take me to the market for execution. Now, the honorable official's surname is Pei, which is the same as the red-robed person. I accidentally struck someone, leading to his death, and this execution was predestined." As he was about to be executed, all the scholars and common people in the region mourned for him.

    109

    ○德州民
    　　德州德平县民某氏者，父子数人耕田甚力，家颇丰厚，其弟素贫，佣以养母，兄未尝有甘旨之助也。庆历中，新构瓦室三楹，所居前后植柳数百株，枝如拱把。一夕大雷电，野火数头相逐绕其居，折柳尽髡，牙击屋瓦。明日视之，无一瓦全者，泥淖中足迹长二尺余。柳悉长三四尺，皮尽剥，莹滑如削，远近居民悉取而藏之。予尝亲至平原，人说如此，亦见其所折柳枝。

    Explanation

    109

    A Man from Dezhou
    A man from Dezhou, in the county of Deping, with his father and several sons, worked very hard at farming, and their family was quite wealthy. His younger brother, who was always poor, worked as a hired laborer to support his mother, but the elder brother never provided any help with food or delicacies. During the year 1045, they had newly built a three-bay tile-roofed house, and in front of and behind their residence, they planted hundreds of willow trees, whose branches were as thick as a man's arm. One night there was a fierce thunderstorm, and several wild fires chased each other around their residence, breaking all the willow trees and stripping them of leaves, while the lightning struck the tiles. The next day when they looked at it, not a single tile remained intact. There were footprints in the mud that were over two feet long. The willow branches were all three or four feet long, the bark was all stripped off, and they were smooth and polished like they had been cut. People from far and near all took and kept them. I once personally went to Pingyuan, and people said it was like this; I also saw the broken willow branches.

    110

    ●卷九
    　　○毛郎中
    　　毛郎中晦，熙宁初年惟一妻一子处，家于荆州。常有一女厉朝夕在其家，语言历历可辨，自称田芙蓉，家人出入动静无不察也。言与邑君有宿冤，或问：“何不遂报之”渠尚有数年寿耳。”然所须之物往往应索而至。久之厌苦，邑君谓曰：“吾为汝修功果，能他适乎”鬼曰：“善。”因赂二僧，俾诵佛书，具疏燔之。鬼去数日复来，曰：“僧之诵经妄矣，止诵一卷，余则未尝读也，是以复来。”诘其僧，果然。邻家毁之曰：“此邪魅也，何足畏”鬼大骂，发其帷幕之私，曰：“此乃邪尔。”常曰：“我今往瓦市游看。”毛密遣仆使探其伎艺者，归而询之，一皆符合。其后，毛之子中庸调补永之祈阳簿，舟行次石首县，鬼继至，曰：“解缆何故不相告俾我昼夜奔赴百余里，足今趼矣。”至零陵二岁，邑君卒，鬼自是而绝。余在荆州亲见。

    Explanation

    110

    Chapter Nine
    Mao the Attendant

    Mao the Attendant, in the early years of the Xining era (1068-1077), lived with only one wife and one son in Jingzhou. There was often a woman named Li who was present in the house day and night. Her words were clear and distinct, and she called herself Tian Furong. She observed the comings and goings and movements of the family without fail. She said she had an old grudge with the local magistrate. Someone asked, "Why don't you just take revenge?" She replied, "He still has several years of life left." However, the things she needed often arrived when requested. After a while, they grew tired of her. The local magistrate said to her, "I will perform good deeds for you, can you leave us?" The spirit replied, "Good." He bribed two monks to recite Buddhist scriptures and burned the prayer scrolls. The spirit left but returned after several days. When questioned, the monks confirmed that they only recited one scroll, the rest they never read. That is why she came back. A neighbor criticized them, saying, "This is a demon, what is there to be afraid of?" The spirit shouted loudly and revealed their private affairs, saying, "This is evil." She often said, "I will now go to the tile market to watch." Mao secretly sent his servants to investigate her skills. Upon returning and asking, everything matched. Later, Mao's son Zhongyong was appointed as the magistrate of Qiyang in Yong Prefecture. When traveling by boat, they stopped at Shishou County. The spirit followed, saying, "Why didn't you tell me when you untied the boat, making me run day and night for over a hundred miles, my feet are now blistered." After two years in Lingling, the local magistrate died. The spirit disappeared after that. I personally witnessed this in Jingzhou.

    111

    ○崔禹臣
    　　崔禹臣，熙宁初以职官知潍州北海县，冬夜坐书阁中，窗外有小圃，闻若环声，又如往来诵佛书者。月色微亮，穴窗视之，见一物长七尺余，周身白毛熠耀，口中咄咄不已，遽呼从人擒之，乃鬼也。面黝发蓬，身萦藻荇，水乳四垂，行则丁冬。遂以挺殴之，大呼曰：“我为若有灾来此念经消禳，何谓捶我也”即命左右互以臣挝痛击，终不能毙，刃之不伤，火之不灼，但觉缩小长三尺许。遂锢缚，既晓，投之大水，良久跃高丈余，已复如旧，少选遂没。是年崔以公事失官。崔亦自有传。

    Explanation

    111

    Cui Yuchen, during the early years of the Xining era, served as an official in charge of the county of Beihai in Weizhou. One winter night, he sat in the book pavilion, and outside the window, there was a small garden. He heard a sound like jade bracelets, and it was also like someone reciting Buddhist scriptures. The moonlight was dimly bright. He looked through the window and saw something about seven feet long, with white, glowing hair all over its body, making continuous sounds. He quickly called for servants to catch it, and it turned out to be a ghost. The ghost had a dark face and disheveled hair, its body entangled in algae and water plants, dripping water and milk, and making a clinking sound when it moved. Then he struck it with a stick, and the ghost shouted loudly, saying, "I came here to recite scriptures to ward off calamity. Why are you hitting me?" Cui then ordered the attendants to beat it with sticks, but it could not be killed. It was not injured by blades, nor burned by fire. It only felt smaller, about three feet long. They then bound it. After dawn, they threw it into the water. After a long time, it jumped high, over ten feet, and returned to its original form. Soon it disappeared. That year, Cui lost his office due to official matters. Cui also has his own biography.

    112

    ○张郎中
    　　张郎中荐，高密人，登明经第。山东风俗，遇正月，取五姓处女年十余岁者，共卧一榻，覆之以衾，四面以箕扇之。良久，有一女子如梦寐，或若刺文绣，或若事笔砚，或若理管弦，俄顷乃寤，谓之扇天卜以乞巧。荐有女十余岁，因卜有一仙女日来教之，遇其去，即留一女童为伴，他人弗见，自此，凡女工、音律、书札，不学而自能。岁余，女昼寝，忽惊呼而觉，曰：“仙女今日上天赴会，令我与童子偕在园中嬉游，园有一井，覆以巨石，戒童子曰：‘勿令此女窥井也。’仙女既去，我遂发石观之，见群鬼异形怪状，攀缘争出，我惊呼，童子遽取乱捶，鬼复入，取石窒之。”自此仙女怒而去，既笄而嫁，生数子。先君与荐善，熟闻其事。

    Explanation

    112

    Translation:

    Zhang Langzhong

    Zhang Langzhong, from Gao Mi, passed the Mingjing examination. In the customs of Shandong, during the first month, young girls from five different families, around ten or eleven years old, would lie together on a bed, covered with a quilt, and fans would be used to create a breeze around them. After a while, one of the girls would fall into a dream-like state, sometimes as if embroidering, sometimes as if handling writing implements, and sometimes as if playing musical instruments. She would wake up after a short while, and this ritual was called "fan tian bo" to seek skill. Zhang had a daughter around the same age, and through this ritual, a fairy visited daily to teach her. When the fairy left, she would leave behind a young girl to accompany her, but others could not see her. From then on, the girl became proficient in needlework, music theory, and letter writing without formal instruction. After a year, one day while she was sleeping, she suddenly woke up in a panic and said, "The fairy went to heaven today for a meeting and told me to play with a boy in the garden. There is a well in the garden covered by a large stone, and she warned the boy, 'Do not let this girl look into the well.' After the fairy left, I removed the stone and saw many ghosts with strange and terrifying forms trying to climb out. I screamed, and the boy quickly took a stick and chased them away. The ghosts went back inside, and the boy put the stone back." After this, the fairy became angry and left. The girl grew up, married, and had several children. My late father had a good relationship with Zhang and was well-informed about this matter.

    113

    ○张司封
    　　建州有张氏，夫妇俱四十余，无子，居近城隍庙，屡祷于神，以求继嗣。岁余，梦神告曰：“汝夫妇分当无子，我念汝告祷之虔，今以庙中判官与若为嗣。”既而其妻妊娠，生一子，名伯玉，第进士，举书判拨萃，历台省，仕至主爵正郎，典数郡而卒。其才藻廉劲，为当世所尚，而嗜酒，不修饬，垢貌蓬鬓，如土偶判官焉。
    　　○薛比部
    　　薛比部周，至和中以殿中丞知益州成都县，其妻卧疾，二婢致药以杀之。薛执二婢送官，劾之伏罪，一婢妊娠已数月，薛以牒诉其诈，遂俱就戮。既而婢与所妊之子形见其室，诉于薛曰：“儿不当死，何以枉害我”昼夜聆其语，然家有吉凶鬼亦以报。薛后监凤翔府太平宫，则鬼不至，他所则来。嘉中，薛自尚书外郎出典涪州，行至始平县，鬼曰：“公将死，无用往。”即乞分司归长安，不逾年遂卒。

    Explanation

    113

    ○ Zhang Shifeng
    In Jianzhou, there was a family named Zhang, whose husband and wife were both in their forties and had no children. They lived near a city god temple and prayed to the deity repeatedly, seeking to continue their family line. After a year, they dreamed that the god told them, "Your couple are fated not to have children, but I have seen your sincere prayers. Now, I will give you the temple's judge as your heir." Soon after, his wife became pregnant and gave birth to a son named Boyu. Boyu passed the imperial examination to become a Jinshi, excelled in specialized examinations in bookkeeping and legal judgment, served in various central government positions, and eventually rose to the rank of Director of the Ministry of Personnel, governing several prefectures before his death. He was known for his literary talent and incorruptibility, highly esteemed in his time, but he also enjoyed drinking and neglected his appearance, looking disheveled and unkempt, much like a clay figure of a judge.

    ○ Xue Bijiao
    Xue Bijiao, whose full name was Zhou, served as the magistrate of Chengdu County in Yizhou during the reign of Emperor Renzong (至和中). His wife fell ill, and two female servants administered poison to kill her. Xue arrested the two servants and handed them over to the authorities, who prosecuted them and they confessed to the crime. One of the servants was pregnant for several months, and Xue submitted a petition claiming she was lying, leading to the execution of both. Soon after, the ghost of the servant and the unborn child appeared in Xue's room, accusing him, "The child should not die; why have you wrongfully harmed us?" Xue heard their voices day and night, and it was said that ghosts would appear to report good or bad omens in the household. Later, when Xue served as the supervisor of the Taiping Palace in Fengxiang Prefecture, the ghosts did not appear, but they would come to other places. During the reign of Emperor Renzong (嘉祐中), Xue was transferred from the position of a mid-level official in the Ministry of Personnel to govern Fuzhou. On his way to Shiping County, a ghost appeared to him and said, "You are going to die; there is no need to go." Xue then requested to be transferred to a position in Chang'an and returned home. He died within a year.

    114

    评曰：“父母杀子，于官理置而不论，矧在胞中形气未具者乎而遽有冤死之诉，岂释氏所谓冤宿世者如是耶
    　　○陈良卿
    　　进士陈良卿，景四年自永州随乡书赴礼部试。十月至长沙，梦一人引导入巨舰中，见一道士，自称清精先生，与之谈论，辞语高古，而义理邃博。谓陈曰：“吾已荐子于尧为直言极谏。”陈曰：“尧今何在”曰：“见司南岳。”陈曰：“尧乃古圣君也，安司在公侯之列”先生曰：“尧，人间之帝也，秉火德而王，弃天下而神位乎南方，子何疑焉”陈辞以名宦未立，俟他日应。乃许以十年为期。既寤，甚恶之，为《异梦录》以自宽。明年，登甲第，调全州判官，道出岳州南一驿。偶昼寝，梦使者持檄来召，遽惊觉，喟曰：“岂尧命乎”同行相勉以梦不足信，复执书帙卧读之，晚食具，呼之，已卒矣。梦中约以十年，乃自得梦至卒，正周十月耳。岂鬼神不欲明言，以一月为一年乎

    114

    Commentary says: "Parents killing their children, the authorities ignore and leave unaddressed. How much more so for those in the womb, not yet fully formed, and suddenly have complaints of wrongful death? Could this be what the Buddhists call the karmic retribution of past lives?"

    ○陈良卿

    Chen Liangqing, a jinshi (imperial examination candidate), traveled from Yongzhou in the year Jingshuo (1037) to take the Ministry of Rites' examination. In October, he reached Changsha, where he dreamed of being led by someone into a large ship. Inside, he met a Taoist priest who introduced himself as Master Qingjing. They engaged in a conversation, with the priest speaking in lofty and ancient terms, his words profound and extensive. The priest told Chen, "I have recommended you to Yao as one who speaks frankly and offers bold advice." Chen asked, "Where is Yao now?" The priest replied, "He is seen by the Lord of the Southern Peak." Chen said, "Yao is an ancient sage king; how can he be among the ranks of dukes and marquises?" The priest responded, "Yao is the emperor of the human world, holding the virtue of fire and reigning. He abandoned the world and became a divine being in the south. Why do you doubt this?" Chen, hesitant due to his lack of established official status, said he would wait for a future opportunity. The priest agreed to wait ten years. Upon waking, Chen found the dream very unpleasant and wrote Record of Strange Dreams to console himself. The following year, he passed the highest rank in the examination and was appointed as a judge in Quanzhou. While traveling through a station south of Yue Prefecture, he happened to take a daytime nap. He dreamed of an official with a summons coming to call him. He suddenly woke up, sighing, "Could this be the command of Yao?" His colleagues encouraged him by saying that dreams are not to be trusted. He again held books and read them while lying down. When dinner was prepared and they called him, he had already died. The dream had promised ten years, but from the time he had the dream until his death, it was only ten months. Could it be that the spirits did not wish to speak plainly, equating one month to one year?

    115

    ○罗著作
    　　著作罗绍，汉阳人，居府五通神祠。其邻家岁畜一豕，以为祀神之具，豕无栏豢，多坏罗之藩篱，入其宅且秽污之。罗屡诫其邻，殊不少听，绍父擒其豕，截去一耳。邻人见之，不胜其愤，曰：“夕诉于神。”且云：“此豕本是神所享，今为罗某所损，岁己乏祀，愿神速报之。”既而生绍与其弟，各无一耳，余亲见之。五通神能祸福于人，立有应验，其可骇哉！绍进士及第，终著作佐郎云。又，公安富民邓氏者，少时因见二犬交，即戏以刃断其势，后生二子俱阉，初为荆南牙校，其状貌真阉也。事与罗绍相近，故附之。

    Explanation

    115

    ○ Luo Shao, the Assistant Zhuozuo
    Luo Shao, an Assistant Zhuozuo from Han Yang, lived near a temple dedicated to the Wutong God. His neighbor annually raised a pig, which was used as an offering for the god. The pig, without a pen, often broke through Luo's fence and entered his house, causing dirt and mess. Luo repeatedly warned his neighbor, but the neighbor completely ignored him. One day, Luo caught the pig and cut off one of its ears. The neighbor, upon seeing this, was furious and said, "I will complain to the god at night." He also said, "This pig was originally an offering for the god, but it has been damaged by Luo, and now there is no offering left. I wish the god to quickly punish him." Later, Luo Shao and his younger brother were born, each lacking one ear. I have personally witnessed this. The Wutong God can bring both blessings and misfortunes, and its effects are instantly verified, how terrifying! Luo Shao passed the imperial examination as a Jinshi and finally became an Assistant Zhuozuo.

    Another story involves a wealthy person named Deng from Gong'an, who, when young, saw two dogs mating and playfully cut off their genitalia with a knife. Later, he had two sons who were both castrated, and they initially served as military officers in Jingnan, their appearance being truly that of eunuchs. The story is similar to that of Luo Shao, so it is appended here.

    ○陆长绪　目录作长孺
    　　陆长绪，吴郡人，第进士，以职官知襄州城县。其为政务疾恶，而遂至外暴，察苛急，视群吏若仇仇，扑挞殆无虚日。一日晚坐厅，有黑犬自门直入，怒目狂吠，跃而升厅。陆号呼，群吏竞持梃逐之，入吏舍，忽不见。既而陆妻死，遂百鬼进其舍，陆子幼，有数婢，往往白昼见少年入婢室。陆大怒，缚群婢，掠至髡钛烙炮以迅其奸，而终不得状。又，堂前旧作盆池植莲，一日，盆出于外，而无发掘之迹，遽命理之，越宿复然。陆自临视，照水见其形冠服非常，而立侍皆群鬼，陆大怖。又有声于梁栋间，渐与陆语，索纸作诗。始见数字在纸，每读毕一句，则一句出，而前句旋灭，其语大略皆讥戏陆也。如是二年，解官，怪始绝。长绪自为人言如此。

    Explanation

    116

    ○Lu Changxu　Catalogue records as Changru
    Lu Changxu, a native of Wu Commandery, passed the imperial examination and served as the governor of Xiangzhou Shacheng County in his official capacity. In his governance, he was quick to punish evil, which led to external violence. He was harsh and hasty in his investigations, regarding the officials as enemies, and almost every day he beat them. One evening, while sitting in the hall, a black dog entered straight from the door, barking wildly with angry eyes, and leaped into the hall. Lu shouted, and the officials rushed in with sticks to chase it, but it suddenly disappeared into the officials' quarters. Soon after, Lu's wife died, and many ghosts entered his house. Lu's son was young, and he had several maids, who often saw a young man entering the maids' rooms during the daytime. Lu became very angry, bound the maids, and beat them to the point of shaving, branding, and burning, in an attempt to punish their wickedness, but he could not determine the situation. Additionally, in front of the hall, there was a previously made basin-shaped pond with lotus flowers planted in it. One day, the basin appeared outside, with no signs of digging. He immediately ordered it to be dealt with, and the next day, it happened again. Lu personally inspected it, seeing its unusual appearance and attire in the water, and found that the standing attendants were all ghosts. Lu was greatly frightened. There was a sound between the beams and rafters, gradually conversing with Lu, asking for paper to write a poem. Initially, numbers appeared on the paper; each time a line was read, a new line appeared, while the previous line disappeared. The general content of the words were all mocking Lu. For two years, this continued until Lu resigned from office, and the strange occurrences finally ceased. Lu Changxu himself told people about this.

    117

    ○寇侍禁
    　　寇侍禁立，尝为三司大将，与同列李某者皇中部督香药往广信军，纳毕回京，宿于定州永乐驿之堂。时苦寒，乃炽炭炷灯拥炉而坐，夜将二鼓，李某先寝。堂后呦呦然如小豚相逐，亦不以为异。俄顷，门轰然大辟，一媪长二尺许，蓬鬓伛偻而前，以口嘘灯，焰碧而将灭。寇大惊，以杖击之，媪走，寇逐之，颡抵门扉，偃仆于地。即开堂之前门，将走外厅呼其从者，忘厅后之有屏也，头又触之而踣。因大呼，驿吏与仆厮秉火而至，见寇颡破血流，灯檠且折，门闭如故。李以被蒙首伏床下。询之，驿吏云：“尝有斯妖出自堂后右城小穴中。”寇自说如此耳。

    Explanation

    A Tale of the Guardian of the Gate

    Kou Shibi, a former high-ranking official of the Three Departments, was once stationed at Guangxin Army with his colleague Li, who served as the supervisor of incense and herbs in the middle district of Huangjiao. After completing their mission, they returned to the capital and stayed at the hall of Yongle Post Station in Dingzhou. It was bitterly cold, so they lit charcoal, lit lamps, and huddled around the stove to keep warm. Around midnight, Li retired to bed first. Suddenly, a soft, gentle sound like that of little pigs chasing each other came from behind the hall, but they did not find it unusual. Soon after, there was a loud bang, and the door burst open wide. An old woman, about two feet tall, with disheveled hair and a stooped posture, stepped forward. She blew on the lamp with her mouth, causing the blue flame to flicker and nearly go out. Kou was greatly startled and struck her with a stick. The old woman ran away, and Kou chased after her, hitting his forehead against the door and falling to the ground. He immediately opened the front door of the hall, intending to go to the outer hall to call for his attendants, but forgot that there was a screen behind the hall. His head hit the screen, and he fell again. He shouted for help, and the post station official and the attendants came with torches. They found Kou with a broken forehead, bleeding, the lamp stand broken, and the door still closed. Li was lying under the bed, covering his head with a quilt. When they asked him about it, the post station official said, "There was once a similar monster that came out of a small hole in the right side of the wall behind the hall." Kou confirmed that this was what happened.

    ○张尚书
    　　张尚书存，冀州人，家富于财，策进士第，累历台省馆阁清要之职，致政归乡闾。一夕，圉人见一犊盗食马粟，逐而捶之，但见白光奔宅门，遂失之，门闭如故。翌日，张病，肌骨痛者数日，间策杖诣马厩，问圉人云：“旬日前夜见何物”圉人曰：“见一犊窃啖马粟，击之，化为白光而去。”张曰：“后或见，不可击也。”圉人颇疑之。岁余病亟，阍者见一犊自宅门出，追视，乃不见。俄闻宅中哭，乃尚书也。

    Zhang Shangshu

    Zhang Shangshu, from Jizhou, was a wealthy man who passed the imperial examination and held various high-ranking positions in the central government before retiring to his hometown. One evening, the stablemaster saw a calf stealing horse feed and chased it, hitting it with a stick. Instead of a calf, he saw a white light rush to the main gate and disappear, leaving the gate closed as if nothing had happened. The next day, Zhang fell ill and suffered pain in his muscles and bones for several days. One day, he went to the stable with a walking stick and asked the stablemaster, "What did you see several nights ago?" The stablemaster replied, "I saw a calf stealing horse feed. When I hit it, it transformed into a white light and disappeared." Zhang said, "If you see it again, do not strike it." The stablemaster was quite suspicious. More than a year later, Zhang's illness worsened. The gatekeeper saw a calf come out from the main gate of the house and pursued it, but saw nothing. Soon after, he heard crying from within the house, and it was Zhang.

    ○姜定国
    　　高密姜定国业九经，一夕，寝于家塾，梦二人身长而貌狠，怒气勃勃然，谓定国曰：“吾身长丈八，可杀汝，可噬汝。”定国惊魇，号呼拒之而退。明夜复梦如初。大惧，乃徙其寝具，与门下客同榻。客取刀断之，少顷，一蛇复至，客又杀之。明日度二蛇，果长三寻。定国后登九经第，今为幕职官。
    　　○傅文秀
    　　礼宾副使傅公文秀，尝自京挈家归凤翔府阳平镇之故居。既而其兄之女为物所凭，暮则靓妆丽服，处帷帐中切切如与人语，家人问之，不对，若是者殆半岁。有善制鬼者罗禁，以其能符禁，乡人呼为罗禁，傅召使视之，遂以法劾其女。乃云：“吾韩魏公之子也，昔侍父镇关中，以病死于长安驿舍，昨日傅族经由，悦其女美，因而婿之。”罗再三讯诘，辞颇屈伏，遂去。后数夜号呼于堂下曰：“汝虽绝我婚，当归吾子也。”再饮之以药，下块肉如拳，自此不复至。

    ○姜定国
    　　Gao Mi's Jiang Dingguo specialized in the Nine Classics. One night, while sleeping in his family school, he dreamed of two tall and fierce-looking people with intense anger, who told him, "I am eight feet tall and can kill you, devour you." Jiang was terrified and shouted in his nightmare, resisting them until they retreated. The next night, he dreamed the same thing again. Greatly fearing this, he moved his sleeping equipment and shared a bed with a guest. The guest took a knife and cut it. A short while later, one snake returned, and the guest killed it again. The next day, when measuring the two snakes, they turned out to be three zhen long. Jiang later passed the Nine Classics examination and is now an official in the government.

    ○傅文秀
    　　Li Bin Deputy Envoy Fu Wenxiu once moved his family from the capital back to his former home in Yangping Town, Fengxiang Prefecture. Later, his sister-in-law was possessed by a spirit. In the evening, she would dress up beautifully and sit in the curtains, talking to herself as if speaking to someone. When family members asked her, she did not respond. This continued for almost half a year. There was a skilled exorcist named Luo Jin, who was known for his ability to use talismans and spells. The villagers called him Luo Jin. Fu summoned him to examine the situation. Luo then used his methods to interrogate her. She said, "I am the son of Duke Huan of Wei. I once served my father in Guanzhong and died of illness in a hostel in Chang'an. Yesterday, the Fu clan passed by and were attracted to my sister-in-law's beauty, so they married her." Luo asked her repeatedly, and her words were somewhat submissive. She then left. Later, she cried out several nights in the hall, saying, "Even if you break off our marriage, you should return my son." She was given medicine again and spat out a piece of meat the size of a fist. From then on, she did not come again.

    ○胡郎中
    　　胡郎中楷，庆历中偶会于真州，尝言：有亲旧赴官湖湘，舟行至鄂岳间，舟忽不进，舟人亦无以施力。其人焚香奠酒披秉再拜，恳诚以祷，良久舟寂然而逝。他船见其舟后有枯木查牙，跃高数丈复沉于水，不知何物。岂蛟龙之变化乎
    　　○僧行悦
    　　长白山醴泉寺，乃景德寺西禅院之下院也，岁久颓圮，僧行悦志欲营葺。因灵市岩川董将军庄大木百余章，有大榆，其上巨枝岐分，向因雷雨，枝间有大足迹，长仅二尺。僧伐视之，上下如一，因断为数十百片，俾其徒伪称佛所践履，持之化诱诸郡，三岁得钱五千万，寺宇一新，颇极壮丽。事在天禧中，李省山人目睹。
