    ○胡郎中
    　　胡郎中楷，庆历中偶会于真州，尝言：有亲旧赴官湖湘，舟行至鄂岳间，舟忽不进，舟人亦无以施力。其人焚香奠酒披秉再拜，恳诚以祷，良久舟寂然而逝。他船见其舟后有枯木查牙，跃高数丈复沉于水，不知何物。岂蛟龙之变化乎

    ○胡郎中楷
    　　During the Qingli era, Censorate Official Hu Kai accidentally met someone in Zhenzhou. He once said: "A relative of mine was traveling to Hu and Xiang to take up an official post. When the boat reached the area between Ezhou and Yueyang, it suddenly stopped, and the boatmen could not move it. The person burned incense, offered wine, and performed two bows with deep sincerity, praying earnestly. After a long time, the boat quietly moved on. Other boats saw a withered tree branch with jagged edges following the boat, leaping high into the air and then sinking back into the water. They did not know what it was. Could it have been a transformation of a dragon or a similar mythical creature?"

    ○僧行悦
    　　长白山醴泉寺，乃景德寺西禅院之下院也，岁久颓圮，僧行悦志欲营葺。因灵市岩川董将军庄大木百余章，有大榆，其上巨枝岐分，向因雷雨，枝间有大足迹，长仅二尺。僧伐视之，上下如一，因断为数十百片，俾其徒伪称佛所践履，持之化诱诸郡，三岁得钱五千万，寺宇一新，颇极壮丽。事在天禧中，李省山人目睹。

    ○Monk Xingyue
    　　The Liquequan Temple on Changbai Mountain is a subsidiary temple to the West Zen Temple of Jingde Temple. After many years, it had fallen into disrepair. Monk Xingyue intended to renovate and rebuild it. He obtained hundreds of large logs from the estate of General Dong in Ling City, Yan River. There was a large elm tree with large branches that split into multiple directions. Previously, during a thunderstorm, there was a large footprint between the branches, measuring only two feet in length. The monk cut it into dozens or hundreds of pieces and instructed his disciples to falsely claim it was a footprint of the Buddha. He used it to persuade people in various prefectures, collecting five million coins in three years. The temple was completely renovated and became quite magnificent and splendid. This occurred during the Tianxi era, and Mr. Li, a scholar from Shanshan, witnessed it.

    121

    评曰：佛之徒以因果祸福，恣行诱胁，持元元死生之柄，自王公而下趋向者十八九。悦又能假诡异之迹，俾夫庸忄柔者破帑倾箧而甘心焉。呜呼！人之好怪也甚矣。
    　　○康定民
    　　康定军未建时，古城卑缺，人得而逾。有邑居王某与北郊村民联亲，景五年秋，村民为子娶妇，王赴。其花烛中夜，二姻家交争纷然，王不喜，遂于厨中得焚余柴枝长三四尺，持之以归。时月色微明，行二三里过古道，有小儿约十数岁遽来，持王衣裾啼哭不已，问其家，亦不答。乃力解其手，未数步又来相逐，遂以所持柴枝击之，即仆地，不闻鼻息。王默念曰：“儿定死。”大惧，又虑路人见而迹露，乃疾走，逾毁垣而入。翌日，不敢出门，恐官捕杀人者。日既高，不得，出里巷伺探消息，寂尔不闻。遂由旧路覆其事，惟见一朽腐棺板，长三尺余，中微骨折，尚有火煤之迹。其古道左右皆土崖，高五六仞，居民多穴之以瘗小儿。盖游鬼凭而为变耳。

    Explanation

    121

    Translation

    The commentator said: Followers of Buddhism use the concepts of cause and effect, blessings and misfortunes, to act freely with inducement and coercion, holding the power of life and death over the common people. From the emperor down to the commoners, nearly nineteen out of twenty were drawn to it. They could also pretend to have strange and mysterious traces, making the simple and weak-hearted people empty their treasuries and willingly submit. Alas! How much people love the strange!

    ○ Kangding People

    Before the establishment of the Kangding military garrison, the old city walls were low and incomplete, allowing people to easily cross them. There was a man named Wang who lived in the city and was related to villagers in the northern suburbs. In the autumn of Jingyou Year Five, the villagers were getting married for their son, and Wang attended. During the middle of the night of the wedding ceremony, the two families were fighting fiercely. Wang was unhappy and, in the kitchen, found a piece of burned firewood about three or four feet long, which he took with him. The moonlight was faint, and he walked two or three miles past the ancient road. A child, about ten or eleven years old, suddenly came running towards him, holding onto Wang's clothes and crying uncontrollably. When Wang asked about the child's home, the child did not answer. Wang tried to pull the child away, but after a few steps, the child came running after him again. Wang then struck the child with the piece of firewood, and the child fell to the ground, no longer breathing. Wang silently thought, "The child is definitely dead." He was greatly frightened and also worried that passersby might see and expose him. So, he ran quickly, leaping over the ruined wall and entering the city. The next day, he dared not go out, fearing that the authorities would arrest him for killing someone. By noon, he had not heard anything, so he went out into the neighborhood to inquire about the news, but there was no response. He then retraced his steps along the old road and found only a rotten coffin board, about three feet long, with a slight fracture and still showing traces of fire. The ancient road was flanked by earth cliffs, about fifteen to twenty meters high, where the locals often dug holes to bury children. It was likely that a wandering ghost or spirit had caused the transformation.

    122

    ○郑前
    　　治平中，武昌县令郑前尝觉腠理不宁，昼寝曲室，梦一老父古衣冠，揖郑曰：“君小疾，煮地骨皮汤饮之即愈。”郑曰：“素不奉展，何故至此”云：“我西汉时与君尝联局事，君已为三世人，我尚留滞幽壤。”即询其名氏，云：“前将军何复。或欲寻吾所居，可来费家园也。”临别口占诗一绝，云：与子相逢西汉年，半成枯骨半成烟。欲知土室长眠处，门有青松涧有泉。郑官满，之鄂渚，游头陀寺，山下城小路见丛薄蔚然。问寺僧，乃费家园也。道次有断碑，字已漫灭，惟有何复字可辩。冢前有涧水洎老松数株。

    Explanation

    122

    During the Zhiping era, the magistrate of Wuchang County, Zheng Qian, once felt uneasy in his skin and muscles. While taking a daytime nap in a small room, he dreamed of an elderly man dressed in ancient attire. The old man bowed to Zheng and said, "You have a minor illness; drink a decoction made from the bark of the dogwood tree, and you will recover." Zheng asked, "I have never met you; why are you here?" The old man replied, "In the Western Han Dynasty, I worked with you on a project. You have already lived through three generations, while I remain lingering in the underworld." Zheng then inquired about the old man's name, and he answered, "I am General He Fu. If you wish to find where I rest, you can come to Fei Family Garden." Before parting, the old man composed a short poem: "We met in the Western Han year, half turned to bones, half to smoke. To know where I lie in the earth, there are green pines at the gate and a stream nearby." After completing his term as magistrate, Zheng went to Ezhu, visited Tathagata Temple, and on a small path below the mountain, he saw a lush and verdant garden. He asked the temple monk, who told him it was Fei Family Garden. Along the way, he found a broken tombstone with most of the characters worn away, but the name "He Fu" was still legible. In front of the tomb, there was a stream and several old pine trees.

    123

    ○陈州女厉
    　　庆历皇中，陈州通判厅夜有妇人尝出与人笑语，或见其状颇美。询其名氏，曰：“我孔大姐也，本石太尉家女奴，以过被杀。”问何不他适，云：“此中亦有所属，安得自便耶”时晏相国镇宛丘，屡倚新声，作小词，未出，鬼即呕唱于外。或早暮人有登厅，忽于掖下作大声，人恐悸则笑。有市买卒时被惊，丧所持，甚苦之，遂常以刀自随。后复来惊，随声斫之，数夕但闻呻吟，曰：“聊与汝相戏，何故伤我如是”自此遂绝。

    123

    Translation:

    The Ghostly Woman of Chen Prefecture

    During the reigns of Emperor Renzong (Qingli) and Emperor Yingzong (Shaoxing), a woman would appear at night in the office of the Prefectural Judge in Chen Prefecture, engaging in laughter and conversation with people. Some saw her as being quite beautiful. When asked for her name, she replied, "I am Kong Dajie, formerly a slave in the household of General Shi, who was killed for a crime." When asked why she did not go elsewhere, she said, "I am bound to this place and cannot leave freely." At the time, Yan Shu, the Prefect of Wanchu, often composed new lyrics and short poems. Before he could finish writing, the ghost would imitate his singing outside. Sometimes, early or late, people entering the office would hear a loud noise from the side, causing fear and laughter. A market worker was frequently startled and lost his goods, so he carried a knife with him. Later, when the ghost came again, he attacked it with the sound of the blade. For several nights, the ghost could only be heard moaning, saying, "I was just playing with you, why did you hurt me like this?" After this, the ghost disappeared.

    ●卷十
    　　○钟离发运
    　　钟离瑾，开宝间宰江州之德化，明年将以女妇许氏。居一日，谕其胥魁俾市婢以送女，翌日，胥与老妪引一女子来，问其何许人，妪曰：“抚之临川人也，幼丧其亲，外氏育之。”女受妪戒，亦不敢有他言。君视事少间归，遇于屏，是女流涕，有戚容，且疑其家叱骂，诘，曰：“不然。某之父，昔曾令是邑，不幸与母俱丧，无亲戚以为依，时方五岁，育于胥家十年矣，且将为己女，今明府欲得媵妾，胥与妪以某应命。适见明府视事，追感吾父，不觉涕零。”君大惊，呼胥妪以审，如女言，诫家人，易其衣食，如己所生。

    Explanation

    Volume Ten
    ○ Zhongli Fa Yun
    Zhongli Jin, during the Kai Bao era, served as the magistrate of Dehua County in Jiangzhou. The following year, he was to marry his daughter to Xu Shi. After a day, he ordered the chief clerk to buy a concubine to accompany his daughter. The next day, the clerk and an elderly woman brought a girl to him. He asked where she came from, and the old woman replied, "She is from Linchuan, Fuzhou. She lost her parents at a young age and was raised by her maternal relatives." The girl followed the old woman's instructions and did not speak of anything else. When the magistrate returned home after attending to his official duties, he met her behind the screen. The girl shed tears and had a sad expression. She suspected that her family had scolded her, but when questioned, she said, "No, it's not like that. My father once served as the magistrate of this county. Sadly, both he and my mother died. With no close relatives to rely on, I was only five years old when I was raised by the clerk's family for ten years. I am about to be treated as your own daughter. Now you, the magistrate, want to take a concubine, and the clerk and the old woman presented me in response to your request. Just now saw you attending to your official duties, recalled my father, and could not help shedding tears." The magistrate was greatly surprised. He called the clerk and the old woman to verify, and they confirmed what the girl said. He instructed his family to provide her with better clothing and food, treating her as if she were born into the family.

    以书抵许氏，告缓期，姑将辍吾女之资以嫁焉。许亦恻然，复曰：“君侯独能抑己女，而拔人之孤女，予固有季子，愿得以为妇，安事盛饰哉”卒以二女归许氏。久之，君梦一绿衣丈夫造庭，拜而谢曰：“不图贱息辱赐于君，然得请于帝，愿奉十任有土官，故来致命。”后果历十郡太守，终于江淮发运使。今钟离氏有仕籍于朝常十余，独出君之后，故世为肥之冠族，若许之名爵，父老已失其传。呜呼！二君之用心非有求于世者，特发诸至仁耳。彼附贵而亲，然自以为得，独何人哉施报之事，儒者盖鲜言，若蛟龙断蛇、杜回结草，千古岂苟传亦有以警劝云。

    To send a letter to the Xu family, requesting an extension of time, and temporarily to withdraw the dowry of my daughter to marry her. Xu was moved with compassion and replied, "I already have a younger son, and I wish for him to marry her; why bother with elaborate adornments?" Finally, both daughters were given to the Xu family. After a long time, the lord dreamed of a green-clad man coming to the courtyard, who bowed and said, "I did not expect my humble daughter to be favored by you, but I have obtained permission from the Emperor, and I wish to offer ten generations of land officials." As a result, he later served as the governor of ten commanderies and finally as the transport commissioner of Jianghuai. Now the Zhongli family has more than ten officials in the court, all descendants of the lord, thus they are the foremost family of Fei. As for the Xu family's titles and ranks, the elders have lost their transmission. Alas! The two lords' intentions were not to seek anything from the world, but to express their utmost benevolence. Those who attach themselves to the powerful and flatter them, thinking they have gained something, are truly what kind of people? The matter of giving and receiving rewards, Confucian scholars rarely speak of it. For a thousand years, these stories are not casually transmitted, but serve as warnings and encouragements.

He ascended the steps, bowed, and knelt, introducing himself as the young master and saying, "In a past life, I was your brother." He insisted on being received and paying respects.     ”恳告以母子之情，呼出，母见即大恸，急就之，遂灭去，叹曰：“果惊去矣。”又数月，遇蔡诞辰，贽纨素数匹以为寿，举视之，若烟绡雾，又如以蛛丝组织而成，固非女工之所能杼轴也。逮半岁，来告曰：“兄已授明越巡检，明日宣下，令先兄往彼，择阒室而上焉。扬子江神相与素善，恐知是亲戚，故起风涛相戏，不须惮也。”言讫，即不见，虹梁自室门而起，南望无际，辎重仪卫如来时。翌日，果徙明越巡检。将至任，一日，郎君前方丈悉水陆珍品，顾蔡曰：“非敢故为异味，有吝于兄，恐不相益耳。”到任又半年，一旦来见，曰：“与兄缘数已尽，从此辞矣。”复由虹梁而去，竟不知所适，蔡族亦无他咎。

    130

    In the second year of Jia You (1057), Chang Xun, a Judicial Censor of the Dali Temple, was the magistrate of Qianjiang County in Jingzhou. While patrolling, he reached the end of a road at a town called Jingtou. Along the path, he encountered two girls aged thirteen or fourteen, naked and resembling beggars. They hunched forward and approached him on horseback, saying they were the slave girls of Huang Babu and had come to seek mercy from the authorities. When questioned, one of the girls said: "The mistress was angry because I ate some leftover food, so she whipped me over a hundred times and then burned my body with a metal rod." The other girl said: "I was resting after working and didn't notice the mistress coming. She was furious that I didn't get up and hung my feet from the beam, then cut my buttocks with a knife. They stripped me of all my clothes and locked me in a cage, and I haven't eaten for three days." Chang asked how they managed to escape, and they replied: "Just then, an elderly man with white hair appeared before the cage, called us to jump out. I said, 'We are too hungry and the cage is too deep to jump out of.' He said, 'Just jump.'"

    ○韩元卿
    　　韩元卿，泗州人也，景五年第进士，皇中为陕州推官监司，俾鞠狱于武昌。事讫，归夷陵，至荆州黄潭驿，忽持刀自刭，喉虽断而未死。祖择之时为荆湖北提刑，韩之同年进士也，即视之。韩不能语，但举手如索纸笔状，因授之，书云：赃滥分明，罪宜处斩。乃弃笔于地。祖命取桑根线缝其创，自以手褫去，翌日遂卒。先是元卿调于京师，绐称无妇，娶富室之女，资送良厚。洎挈之到任，则故妻在焉，有男女数人矣。富人之女欲以书诉于家，则提防甚密，无由而达，岁余悒抑而卒。又不敢权厝于外，但裹以茵席，瘗于廨宇之隙地，韩既死，方具枢而敛焉。赃滥之诛，岂非此耶

    Explanation

    132

    Translation

    Han Yuanqing
    Han Yuanqing, a man from Si Prefecture, passed the imperial examination in the fifth year of Jingyou (1038) and served as a judicial officer in Shaan Prefecture under the supervision of the regional governor during the Huaihe period. He was sent to Wuchang to handle a case. After the case was resolved, he returned to Yiling and arrived at the Huangtan Post Station in Jingzhou, where he suddenly took a knife and attempted suicide. Although his throat was cut, he did not die immediately. At that time, Zu Zhe was the regional governor of the northern part of Jinghu, and he was a fellow top-ranked graduate from the same imperial examination. Zu Zhe immediately examined Han Yuanqing. Han Yuanqing could not speak, but he raised his hand as if asking for paper and pen. Zu Zhe gave him the paper and pen, and Han Yuanqing wrote, "The corruption is clear, the punishment should be death." He then threw the pen on the ground. Zu Zhe ordered a needle made from mulberry root to sew up the wound, and Han Yuanqing himself removed it. The next day, he died.

    Before this, Han Yuanqing had been transferred to the capital and falsely claimed to have no wife. He married a wealthy woman, and the dowry was very generous. When he brought her to his post, his former wife was already there, and they had several children. The wealthy woman wanted to write a letter to her family, but the guards were very strict, and she had no way to send it. After more than a year, she died of depression. They dared not temporarily bury her outside, so they wrapped her body in a mat and buried her in a vacant lot near the government office. After Han Yuanqing's death, they finally prepared the coffin and buried him. The punishment for corruption, was it not this?

    ○李敏
    　　李敏尝为兖州奉符县主簿，会岳庙炳灵公殿岁久，再加营葺，命敏督其役。或曰：“宜先具公裳，再拜，启其事于神。”李不应，遂彻瓦，未□半，黑云满殿庭，风雹大作，李始惧，披简拜阶下，仰视神座，帐上有黄龙长数丈，震霆数声，穿屋而去，凡损稼百余里。炳灵公自后唐明宗听医僧之语，遂赠官立祠。余谓：龙蛰于神帐上，因彻瓦而惊，随风雷徙去，未必神之灵变也。

    Explanation

    133

    Li Min

    Li Min once served as the chief clerk in the county of Fengfu, Tai'an, Shandong Province. When the temple dedicated to the deity Bingling Gong, located in a mountainous area, had been there for a long time and was renovated again, Li Min was ordered to oversee the work. Someone suggested, "It would be appropriate to first wear the ceremonial robe, bow twice, and inform the deity of the matter." Li Min did not follow this suggestion and began removing the tiles. Not even halfway through, black clouds filled the hall and courtyard, and a great hailstorm began. Li Min started to feel afraid and unfolded the scroll, bowing at the steps, and looked up at the deity's seat. He saw a yellow dragon several zhang long on the canopy, and several thunderclaps sounded, piercing through the roof and departing. The storm destroyed crops over a hundred miles. After the Later Tang Emperor Mingzong listened to the words of a medical monk, he then bestowed an official title and established a shrine. However, it may not have been a divine transformation.

    134

    ○乐平港鼍
    　　潭州乐平桥港，乃湘之支流，传有鼍能变怪食人，岁有溺死者。天圣中，市民李姓者弟溺死不得尸，以为鼍之食也。李氏痛切，无方以复其冤，因刺掌血濡墨作章，夜醮奏而焚之，祈达于帝。是夜，梦吏若道士画天神之从官者，驱民以行。久之，至一处，深严虚洁，若大府廨，而屏之外。有数吏以铁索絷一物，长数丈，如龙而一角，目光如电，甚可畏。吏指告民曰：“尔将与此共见也。”民方悟为鼍妖。已而俱入立庭下，遥视殿上若有人物往来，而不辨其详。有顷，一人下殿，呼曰：“江鼍肆暴，枉害平人，决铁杖一百，处死；李某不合以掌血腥秽上渎高真，宜付王硕决脊杖十五。”遂俱驱出。民觉而历历志之，常惕息寅畏，惧罹罪罟，杜门不预外事。后十余年，侍御史王硕知潭州，民坐遗火延烧一坊，伏罪，竟如所梦。

    Explanation

    134

    ○Le Ping Port Alligator
    The Le Ping Bridge Port in Tan Prefecture is a tributary of the Xiang River. It is said that an alligator can transform into monsters and eat people, causing people to drown every year. During the Tian Sheng era, a man surnamed Li from the city had his younger brother drown, and the body was not found. He believed it was eaten by the alligator. The Li family was deeply grieved and had no way to clear the injustice. He then pricked his palm with a needle to draw blood, mixed it with ink, and wrote a petition. At night, he performed a ritual offering and burned the petition, praying for it to reach the emperor. That night, he dreamed of officials who looked like Taoist priests, drawing attendants of heavenly gods, driving the people to walk. After a while, they arrived at a place that was deeply solemn, empty, and clean, like a grand government office, but outside the screen. Several officials bound something with an iron chain. It was several zhang long, like a dragon with one horn, and its eyes were like lightning. It was very frightening. The officials pointed and told the people, "You will see this with us." The people realized it was the alligator demon. They all entered and stood in the courtyard, looking up at the hall and saw people moving about, but could not discern the details. After a while, one person came down from the hall and called out, "The alligator has been wreaking havoc, wrongfully harming ordinary people. He should be sentenced to one hundred strokes with an iron rod and executed. Li should not have used his bloody palm to defile the high and true with filth. He should be handed over to Wang Shuo for fifteen strokes on the back." They were then all driven out. The people woke up and recorded everything in detail. They always felt fearful and cautious, afraid of falling into legal punishment, and closed their doors, not participating in external affairs. More than ten years later, Wang Shuo, the Imperial Censor, became the governor of Tan Prefecture. The people were punished for a fire that spread to a block and confessed, and the outcome matched their dream.

    135

    ○遵道者
    　　僧令遵，陕州人也，多智数，善附丽权势。天圣中，出入刘皇城家，因而名闻宫掖。庄献赐与巨万，于陕州造一寺，备极壮丽，凡用钱十余万缗。尝自安业南街乘马而西，呼仆取坠策，时有瞽者坐茶肆，前仰而言曰：“僧豪也。”遵异之，过百许步，下马复来，揖之未已，即曰：“岂非坠策之僧乎”遵曰：“然。”复曰：“若之声名尝达天听，有之乎”僧曰：“有之。

    Explanation

    135

    ○ Zun Dao

    The monk named Ling Zun, a native of Shan State, was intelligent and skilled at attaching himself to powerful people. During the Tian Sheng period, he frequently visited the home of Liu Huangcheng, thereby gaining fame in the palace. Emperor Zhaoran bestowed upon him a large sum of money, and he built a temple in Shan State, which was extremely grand and beautiful, costing over ten thousand strings of coins. Once, while riding a horse westward on the south street of Anye, he called his servant to retrieve a fallen whip. At that time, there was a blind man sitting in a teahouse who, upon looking up, said, "The monk is a powerful figure." Ling Zun was surprised by this and walked about a hundred steps before dismounting and returning. He bowed to the blind man and then asked, "Are you not the monk who fell off his horse?" Ling Zun replied, "Yes." The blind man then asked, "Has your reputation ever reached the emperor?" The monk answered, "It has."

    136

    ”因问将来之事，良久曰：“自此十五年，岁在丙戌，当有大祸，宜杜门避之，不尔免死为幸。”僧不怿而起。既归陕，具有瞽者之言告其徒，咸曰：“遵道者，戒行素严，礻周何由而至”以谓不然。至庆历六年，传岩渊马道人将图不轨，陕有市民亦预其谋，民将自陈于官，密诣僧谋之。僧曰：“若自首于郡，不过免死而已。我有主人在京师，地连□□，但持我书诣之，因其言以达朝廷，岂止免罪当获重赏。”民从之。行至洛，党中二卒告变，籍有民名，捕得，尽道所以然之状。”及出遵书，时薛绅守陕郊，大怒，遂黥遵，为武昌城卒。

    Asking about future matters, after a long time, he said, "Fifteen years from now, in the year of Bing Xu, there will be a great calamity. It is advisable to stay indoors and avoid it. Otherwise, escaping death would be fortunate." The monk was displeased and got up. Upon returning to Shanxi, he had the blind man's words told to his disciples, all of whom said, "Zun Dao, who has always been strictly observant of precepts, how could Zhou come to this?" They thought it was not so. In the sixth year of Qingli, Chuan Yan Yuan Ma Dao Ren planned to commit treason. A citizen from Shanxi was also involved in the plot and planned to report to the authorities but secretly went to the monk for advice. The monk said, "If you confess to the authorities, you would only escape death. I have a master in the capital, with connections in □□. Just bring my letter to him, through his words to reach the court. Not only would you avoid punishment but also receive a heavy reward." The citizen followed him. Traveling to Luoyang, two soldiers in the gang reported the change, and the register had the citizen's name. They were captured and fully described the reasons for the situation. When Zun's letter was produced, at that time, Xue Shen was in charge of Shanxi. He became very angry and then branded Zun, making him a soldier in Wuchang City.

    137

    ○董中正
    　　董中正，宿州高资户也，邢州僧慈演者寓外宿有年矣，蓄镪千余万，寄于董室，其后僧病且死，钱遂没于董氏。治平三年春，中正病亟，大呼曰：“邢州不须呵诋，待我还尔钱。”数日卒。其长男为符离衙校，既殡父，即日得病，信宿遂恍惚，云：“邢州就我父索钱，有人监督甚急，乞少缓，讵敢诋谰也”既而又死。宿有乐人张遂，自岱岳回，出徐州界张弓手店，见衙校者跃马而来，问何之，曰：“大人有少缗钱，为券约不明，在兖州对辨，暂往省问。若今归耶，可至我家，言我甚安，道中不暇作书也。”张至宿，诣董宅，将道其事，方知董之父子皆已死矣。

    Explanation

    137

    Dong Zhongzheng, a man of high social status in Suzhou, had a long-standing relationship with a monk named Ciyuan from Xingtai, who had lived in Suzhou for many years. The monk accumulated over a million taels of silver and entrusted it to Dong's household. After the monk fell ill and died, his wealth was lost to the Dong family. In the spring of the third year of the Zhiping era, Dong Zhongzheng himself became gravely ill and shouted, "Xingtai does not need to scold me; I will return your money to you." He died a few days later. His eldest son, who was a military officer in Fulidi, fell ill on the same day his father was buried. After two nights, he became dazed and said, "Xingtai is coming to my father for the money. There is someone supervising very urgently. Please wait a little longer; how dare I slander?" He died shortly after. A musician named Zhang Sui from Suzhou, returning from Mount Tai, passed by Zhanggongshou's shop near the border of Xuzhou and saw the military officer galloping towards him. Zhang asked where he was going, and the officer replied, "My master has a small amount of money, and the contract is unclear. We are going to Yanzhou to discuss it. If you are returning now, you can come to my home. I am very well, but I did not have time to write a letter on the way." Zhang went to Suzhou and visited Dong's house to tell him about the matter. Just then, he learned that both Dong Zhongzheng and his son had died.

    138

    ○同州村民
    　　同州冯翊村民，宝元中有牛生一儿，旋失之。民家有老翁八十余，夜则来与老翁共语，人皆闻之。忽谓公曰：“我昨日往延州与羌贼交战，南兵失利，刘石二大将皆为贼擒。”邻里相传，喧然闻于邑大夫，方将逮翁诘之，后三日，败问果至自兹州。县屡有呼问，儿谢翁曰：“我住此，令翁家不宁。”遂去不复来。

    Explanation

    138

    A Villager from Tongzhou

    In the Fengyi district of Tongzhou, during the Baoyuan era, a cow gave birth to a calf, which soon disappeared. A villager's household had an elderly man over eighty years old, who at night would come to talk with the old man, and everyone could hear him. Suddenly, he said to the public, "I went to Yanzhou yesterday to fight the Qiang bandits, and the southern soldiers suffered defeat; Generals Liu and Shi were captured by the bandits." The news spread among the neighbors and was widely heard by the county officials, who were about to arrest the old man and interrogate him. Three days later, the news of the defeat indeed came from this state. The county officials repeatedly called and questioned him. The child thanked the old man and said, "I live here, making your family uneasy." Then he left and did not return.
